Punishment for Leaving the Ramadan Fast: Hanafi Ta'zir vs. Inter-Madhhab Dispute on Killing
Prescribes beating and imprisonment for leaving fast, but no killing; discusses killing for juhud or istikhfaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for one who leaves the Ramadan fast out of laziness, explain the distinction between laziness and denial/contempt, and evaluate the Shafi'i and Hanbali counter-arguments.

Core Idea
A lazy faster is beaten and imprisoned, never killed; only denial or contempt makes him an apostate.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on the penalty for abandoning the Ramadan fast without a valid excuse. The text distinguishes between mere laziness—which warrants ta'zir (discretionary punishment) but not execution—and outright denial or contempt of the obligation, which elevates the act to apostasy. We will also examine the opposing views of the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools, which advocate capital punishment even for simple abandonment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the default Hanafi ruling
The passage addresses the one who abandons the Ramadan fast 'out of laziness' (kasalan). The default ruling: he is beaten (yudrab) and imprisoned (yuhbas) until he fasts, but not killed (la yuqtal).
The act is sinful but not capital; the punishment is ta'zir.
2
Spot the exceptions: juhud and istikhfaf
If the person denies the obligation (juhud) or shows contempt (istikhfaf) for the fast—e.g., breaking it openly without excuse or saying 'Ramadan is heavy'—then he is treated as an apostate (murtadd). His doubts are removed, he is imprisoned, and if he persists, he is killed.
Denial of a known necessity of the religion is itself apostasy; contempt similarly indicates rejection.
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
The hashya records that the Shafi'is hold that such a person is killed as a hadd penalty, and Imam Ahmad (Hanbali) holds he is killed for kufr (apostasy). The Hanafi response insists on the distinction between mere laziness and denial/contempt.
This is a critical refinement: the Hanafi school limits capital punishment to cases involving religious rejection.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Hanafi law, a lazy faster is not executed; under Shafi'i/Hanbali, he is. This affects the mufta bihi: the Hanafi mufti must ensure the conditions of juhud or istikhfaf are met before issuing a ruling of apostasy.
The practical difference is life or death.
5
Classify the evidence and authority
The Hanafi position is based on the principle that mere sinful omission does not remove one from Islam. Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah. The Shafi'i/Hanbali views are noted as legitimate ikhtilaf but not mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا تارك صوم رمضان كسلا يضرب كذلك، ويحبس حتى يصوم ولا يقتل بمجرد ترك الصلاة والصوم مع الإقرار بفرضيتهما إلا إذا جحد افتراض الصلاة أو الصوم لانكاره ما كان معلوماً من الدين إجماعاً أو استخف بأحدهما كما لو أظهر الافطار في نهار رمضان بلا عذر تهاوناً، أو نطق بما يدل عليه فيكون حكمه حكم المرتد فتكشف شبهته، ويحبس، ثم يقتل إن أصر 
قوله: (ولا يقتل) وقالت الشافعية يقتل حذا وقال الإمام أحمد : يقتل كفراً كما نقله صاحب المواهب عنه، ونقله ابن تيمية عن أكثر السلف في الرسالة المتعلقة بالسياسة. قوله : (نهاوناً) وأما إذا كان لضرورة فلا قوله أو نطق بما يدل عليه) أي على الاستخفاف كما إذا قال رمضان ثقيل، أو سامج. قوله : ( ويحبس) حبس المرتد مندوب وكذا کشف شبهته والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
And likewise, the one who abandons the fast of Ramadan out of laziness is beaten similarly, and imprisoned until he fasts, and is not killed merely for leaving prayer and fasting while acknowledging their obligation, unless he denies the obligation of prayer or fasting for rejecting what is known of the religion by consensus, or shows contempt for either, such as if he openly breaks the fast during Ramadan without excuse out of disregard, or says something indicating that. Then his ruling is that of an apostate: his doubts are removed, and he is imprisoned, then killed if he persists. His statement: (and is not killed) The Shafi'is said that he is killed as a hadd punishment, and Imam Ahmad said he is killed as kufr, as transmitted by author of al-Mawahib from him, and Ibn Taymiyya transmitted it from most of the salaf in the treatise on politics. His statement: (out of disregard) as for necessity, then no. His statement: (or says something indicating it) i.e., indicating contempt, such as if he says 'Ramadan is heavy' or 'boring'. His statement: (and he is imprisoned) imprisoning the apostate is recommended, and likewise removing his doubts. And Allah knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Great.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on one who abandons the Ramadan fast out of laziness: he is beaten and imprisoned until he fasts, but not killed. The exception is if he denies the obligation of prayer or fasting (juhud) which is tantamount to disbelief, or if he shows contempt for the fast, e.g., by openly breaking it without excuse in a manner showing disregard, or making derogatory statements. In such cases, he is treated as an apostate and may be executed if he persists. The hashya records the inter-madhhab dispute: the Shafi'is hold that such a person is killed as a hadd penalty, while Imam Ahmad holds he is killed as an apostate. The Hanafi position distinguishes between leaving out of laziness (which is sinful but does not entail execution) and denial/contempt (which leads to apostasy).

Key Terms
جحد (jahada): To deny the obligation (of prayer or fasting) knowing it is obligatory.
استخفاف (istikhfaf): Showing contempt or belittling a religious obligation.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for sins that have no fixed hadd penalty. In this context, beating and imprisonment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this text, when is a person killed for leaving the fast of Ramadan?
A) Whenever he misses a fast
B) If he acknowledges the obligation but is lazy
C) If he denies the obligation or shows contempt
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between leaving the fast out of laziness (punished by ta'zir) and denying or showing contempt for it (apostasy, punishable by death if persistent).

The Ruling on Reviving the Last Ten Nights of Ramadan
Ruling on reviving the last ten nights of Ramadan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reviving the last ten nights of Ramadan and explain the primary evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Reviving the last ten nights is mustahabb, especially to seek Laylat al-Qadr.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi establishes the recommendation (mandub) of reviving the last ten nights of Ramadan. It grounds this ruling in the prophetic practice as narrated by Aisha, and highlights the purpose: seeking Laylat al-Qadr, a night better than a thousand months. Understanding this ruling encourages believers to increase worship during these blessed nights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the matn: the word 'yundab' indicates the act is recommended (mustahabb). Confirm that the hukm level is not wajib but mandub.
The term 'nadb' is synonymous with mustahabb in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the primary proof
Identify the hadith of Aisha as the main dalil. Note its transmission: narrated by Bukhari and Muslim (mutawatir in meaning).
3
Analyze the prophetic practice
Examine the phrases 'ahya al-layl' (revive the night), 'ayqaza ahlahu' (wake his family), and 'shadda al-mi'zar' (tighten the cloth). They show intensity and dedication.
The commentary explains 'shadda al-mi'zar' as exertion in worship.
4
Understand the purpose
The text states the goal is to seek Laylat al-Qadr. Read the stories illustrating its superiority over a thousand months of worship.
The revelation of Surat al-Qadr confirms this virtue.
5
Note the wisdom of concealment
The passage explains that Laylat al-Qadr is hidden so that believers strive to revive many nights, increasing their worship.
This is a key practical takeaway: seek it every night of the last ten.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وندب إحياء ليالي العشر الأخير من رمضان) لما ورد عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان إذا دخل العشر الأخير من رمضان أحيا الليل وأيقظ أهله وشدّ المئزر والقصد منه إحياء ليلة القدر فإن العمل فيها خير من العمل في ألف شهر خالية منها وروى أحمد من قام ليلة القدر إيماناً واحتساباً غفر له قوله : وشدّ المئزر ) أي اجتهد في العبادة. قوله: (فإن العمل فيها الخ) روي أنه ذكر رجلاً من بني إسرائيل لبس السلاح في سبيل الله تعالى ألف شهر فعجب المسلمون، فأنزل الله سورة القدر أي ليلة القدر خير من الألف شهر التي لبس فيها ذلك الرجل السلاح في سبيل الله ، ويروى أنه ذكر أربعة من بني إسرائيل فقال : عبدوا الله ثمانين عاماً لم يعصوه طرفة عين فذكر أيوب وزكريا، وحزقيل، ويوشع بن نون عليهم السلام، فعجبت الصحابة من ذلك فنزل جبريل وقال يا محمد عجبت أمتك من عبادة هؤلاء النفر ثمانين سنة لم يعصوا الله طرفة عين، فقد أنزل الله عليك خيراً من ذلك، وقرأ السورة فهذا أفضل مما عجبت أنت وأمتك فسر النبي ، والناس معه، والألف شهر ثلاث وثمانون سنة، وأربعة أشهر قال النووي : وقد خص الله تعالى هذه الأمة بها فلم تكن لمن قبلهم على الصحيح المشهور، وقد أجمع من يعتد به على وجودها، ودوامها إلى آخر الدهر للأحاديث المشهورة، وأنها ترى حقيقة لمن شاء الله في كل رمضان كما تظاهرت عليه الأحاديث، ويستحب كتمانها لمن رآها إتباعاً له ، والحكمة في إخفائها أن يجتهد من يريدها في إحياء الليالي الكثيرة طلباً لموافقتها فتكثر عبادته له تعالى .اهـ. قوله (واحتساباً) أي ادخاراً لثوابها عند الله تعالى.
And recommended is reviving the last ten nights of Ramadan. Due to what was narrated from Aisha: The Prophet, when the last ten days of Ramadan entered, would revive the night, wake his family, and tighten his cloth. The purpose is to revive Laylat al-Qadr, for work in it is better than work in a thousand months devoid of it. Ahmad narrated: Whoever stands (in prayer) on Laylat al-Qadr with faith and seeking reward, his past sins are forgiven. He said: (And tighten his cloth) meaning he exerted himself in worship. He said: (For work in it, etc.) It is narrated that a man from the Children of Israel was mentioned who wore weapons in the path of Allah for a thousand months, and the Muslims were amazed. So Allah revealed Surat al-Qadr, i.e., Laylat al-Qadr is better than the thousand months in which that man wore weapons. And it is narrated that four from the Children of Israel were mentioned: they worshipped Allah for eighty years without disobeying Him in the blink of an eye. He mentioned Ayyub, Zakariyya, Hizqil, and Yusha' ibn Nun. The companions were amazed at that, so Jibril came down and said: O Muhammad, your ummah was amazed at the worship of these eighty years, but Allah has sent down to you something better than that, and he recited the surah. So that is better than what you and your ummah wondered at. The Prophet and the people were pleased. And a thousand months are eighty-three years and four months. Al-Nawawi said: Allah has specifically given this to this ummah; it was not for those before them according to the correct and well-known view. And those whose opinion is considered have agreed on its existence and its continuity until the end of time due to the well-known hadiths, and that it is seen in reality by whom Allah wills in every Ramadan, as the hadiths indicate. It is recommended to conceal it for those who see it, following the Prophet. The wisdom in hiding it is so that those who seek it will strive to revive many nights hoping to coincide with it, thus increasing their worship of Allah. End. He said: (and seeking reward) meaning storing up its reward with Allah.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for reviving the last ten nights of Ramadan, especially Laylat al-Qadr. The matn states it is recommended (mandub). The proof is from Aisha's hadith describing the Prophet's practice: he would revive the night, wake his family, and tighten his cloth (exert himself). The commentary explains that 'tightening the cloth' means striving in worship. The commentary also narrates stories illustrating the superiority of Laylat al-Qadr over a thousand months of worship, including the story of a man who fought in Allah's path for a thousand months and the story of four prophets who worshipped for eighty years. The revelation of Surat al-Qadr showed that Laylat al-Qadr is better. Al-Nawawi is quoted stating that this night is specific to this ummah and that it continues until the end of time. The wisdom of its concealment is to encourage worshippers to seek it throughout the last ten nights, thereby increasing their worship. The phrase 'with faith and seeking reward' means intending the reward from Allah.

Key Terms
إحياء الليل (iḥyā' al-layl): Spending the night in acts of worship, such as prayer, recitation, and supplication.
ليلة القدر (laylat al-qadr): The Night of Decree, a specific night in the last ten nights of Ramadan, better than a thousand months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why is Laylat al-Qadr hidden?
A) To test the faith of believers
B) So that people will worship more nights seeking it
C) Because it is no longer available after the Prophet
D) To prevent disputation among scholars

Key Takeaway
Reviving the last ten nights is a recommended sunnah aimed at seeking Laylat al-Qadr, whose precise night is hidden to encourage greater worship.

Will for Missed Fasts: Obligation and Conditions
Ruling on when a will is required for missed fasts and from which wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a will is required for missed fasts and explain the role of istihsan in extending that ruling to missed prayers.

Core Idea
A will for missed fasts is wajib from one-third; prayers are analogized by istihsan.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: when a person dies with missed obligatory fasts (and by extension, prayers), is a will required? The Hanafi school uses the Quranic permission of fidyah for fasting and extends it to prayer through istihsan. The ruling depends on whether the deceased had a genuine opportunity to make up the missed acts. Understanding this illustrates how Hanafi jurists balance textual proof with juristic reasoning to meet the needs of the ummah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is making a will (wasiyya) for missed fasts. Determine its hukm level (wajib, sunnah, etc.) and when it becomes obligatory.
The obligation is conditional on having had time to make up the fasts but failing to do so before death.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic text (implied: 2:184) allows fidyah for those unable to fast. This is the foundation. Identify the type of proof and its certainty.
The text states 'al-nass fi al-sawm bi-isqatihi bi al-fidyah' – the textual basis is for fasting only.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah for prayer
How is the ruling on fasting extended to prayer? The mashayikh use istihsan (juristic preference) because prayer is more important. Understand the reasoning: the illah (effective cause) is the inability to perform the act, which applies to both.
This is a form of qiyas, but reliance on istihsan indicates the jurists prioritized the underlying benefit.
4
Distinguish the conditions for obligation
The passage distinguishes between a traveler/sick person who dies before being able to make up (no will) and one who had time but did not (will required). Also consider those who broke without excuse.
The key is whether the deceased had a period (zaman) sufficient for qada.
5
Apply the financial limit: one-third
The will is executed from one-third of the estate because the deceased's right during illness is limited to one-third; heirs' rights protect the rest.
This is general Hanafi law of wasiyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في إسقاط الصلاة والصوم لا يخفى حسن ذكر هذا الفصل بعد ذكر أحكام المريض، اعلم أنه قلا ورد النص في الصوم بإسقاطه بالفدية، واتفقت كلمه المشايخ على أن الصلاة كالصوم استحساناً لكونها أهم منه، وإنما الخلاف بينهم في أن صلاة أو كل فريضة كصوم يوم، وهو المعتمد كصومه، يوم إذا علمت ذلك تعلم جهل من يقول أن إسقاط الصلاة لا أصل له إذ هذا إبطال للمتفق عليه بين أهل المذهب، وأراد المصنف بقوله : والصوم صوم رمضان بدليل قوله: بعد وغيرهما فإن المراد به صوم كفارة اليمين وقتل وظهار وجناية على إحرام وقتل محرم صيد، أو صوم منذور أفاده في الشرح قوله : (بالإيماء برأسه) قيد به لأنه لا يعتبر الإيماء بنحو الحاجب، فلا بعد به قادراً فلا تلزمه الوصية وقياس قول زفر أنه إذا تركها مع قدرته على الإيماء بنحو الحاجب أوصى قوله : (عن) صلاة يوم وليلة) إنما ذكره لأنه إذا سقط في هذه الحالة القليل الذي لا حرج فيه فأولى الكثير الذي فيه الحرج. قوله : (لما رويناه) من قوله : «فإن لم يستطع فالله أحق بقبول العذر منه قوله : (لعدم قدرته الأولى الإتيان بالواو لتكون علة ثانية عقلية بعد النقل، ويحتمل أنه علة للعلة قوله : ( بإدراك زمن متعلق بقوله: قدرته، والباء للسببية. قوله : ( على قول من يفسر الخ) فإن القائل به لا يقول بلزوم القضاء إلا بإدراك زمن يسعه ولم يوجد، ولزوم الوصية فرع لزوم القضاء، وبه يندفع ما أورد من أن الوجوب قد تعلق حكم (الصوم) في شهر رمضان إن أفطر فيه المسافر والمريض ومانا قبل الإقامة) للمسافر (و) قبل (الصحة) للمريض لعدم إدراكهما عدة من أيام أخر فلا يلزمهما الإيصاء به (و) لزم (عليه) يعني على من أفطر في رمضان ولو بغير عذر الوصية بما) أي بفدية ما قدر عليه) من إدراك عدة من أيام أخر إن أفطر بعذر، وإن لم يدرك عدة من أيام أخر إن أفطر بدون عذر لزمه بجميع ما أفطره لأن التقصير منه لكنه يرجى له العفو بفضل الله بفدية ما لزمه (ويقي بذمته) حتى أدركه الموت من صوم، فرض وكفارة وظهار وجناية على إحرام ومندور فيخرج عنه وليه) أي. من له التصرف في ما له لوراثة أو وصاية من ثلث ما ترك) الموصي لأن حقه في ثلث ماله حال مرضه وتعلق حق الوارث بالثلثين، فلا ينفذ قهراً على الوارث إلا في الثلث إن أوصى به، وإن لم يوص لا يلزم الوارث الإخراج فإن تبرع جاز كما سنذكره وعلى هذا دين صدقة الفطر أو النفقة الواجبة، والخراج والجزية
Chapter on Dropping Prayer and Fasting: The benefit of mentioning this chapter after the rulings of the sick is not hidden. Know that it is said: the text came regarding fasting, dropping it by fidyah, and the mashayikh agreed that prayer is like fasting by istihsan because it is more important. The difference among them is whether one prayer or every obligatory prayer is like one day's fast, and the relied-upon view is like it. When you know that, you know the ignorance of the one who says dropping prayer has no basis, for this is invalidating what is agreed upon among the madhhab's people. The author intended by 'fasting' the fast of Ramadan, as indicated by his later saying 'and others', for the intent is the fast of expiation for oath, killing, zihar, violation of ihram, killing of game by a muhrim, or vowed fast, as clarified in the sharh. His saying: (by gesturing with his head) is qualified because gesturing with the eyebrow is not considered; so he is not regarded as capable, so a will is not obligated. By analogy with Zufar's saying, if he left it while able to gesture with the eyebrow, he would will. His saying: (of a day and night's prayer) He only mentioned this because if the little that involves no difficulty is dropped in this case, then the much that involves difficulty is more deserving. His saying: (based on what we narrated) from his saying: 'If he cannot, then Allah is more deserving of accepting the excuse from him.' His saying: (due to his inability) It would be better to add the waw to make it a second rational cause after the transmitted cause, and it is possible it is a cause for the cause. His saying: (by reaching a time) is attached to his saying 'his ability', and the ba' is for causation. His saying: (according to the one who interprets) For the one who says that only requires making up if a time that can accommodate it is reached, and it was not found; the obligation of a will is a branch of the obligation of making up, and by this is repelled the objection that obligation was attached. The ruling (of fasting) in the month of Ramadan: if a traveler and a sick person break the fast and die before the traveler's return and before the sick person's health, due to not reaching other days, then a will is not required. And it is required upon the one who broke the fast in Ramadan, even without an excuse, to will a fidyah for what he was able (to make up) of other days if he broke with an excuse. If he did not reach other days and broke without an excuse, he is required to will for all that he broke, because the shortcoming is from him, but he may hope for forgiveness from Allah's bounty by the fidyah of what was required. And it remains a debt on him until death overtakes him of fasts: obligatory, expiation, zihar, violation of ihram, vowed. So his guardian (one who has authority over his wealth by inheritance or executorship) pays it from one third of what he left, because his right is in one third of his wealth during his illness, and the heirs' right attaches to two thirds, so it is not enforced over the heir except in the third if he willed; if he did not will, the heir is not obligated to pay, but if he volunteers it is allowed, as we will mention. And similarly the debt of sadaqat al-fitr or obligatory maintenance, and kharaj and jizya.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on when a will (wasiyya) is required for missed fasts and from which portion of the estate it is paid. It begins by explaining the methodology: since the Quranic text mentions fidyah for fasting, the scholars extend it to prayer by istihsan (juristic preference) because prayer is more important. The relied-upon view is that each missed prayer is equivalent to a day's fast. The passage then discusses the case of a traveler or sick person who breaks the fast in Ramadan and dies before being able to make up the missed days. For these, no will is required because they were unable to make up the fasts. However, for a person who broke the fast without an excuse, or even with an excuse but later had time to make up but died, a will is required. The amount: if he had time to make up some days, he only must bequeath fidyah for those days; if he had no time due to excuse, no will; if he broke without excuse and never made up, he bequeaths for all missed days. The hadith quoted ('If he cannot, then Allah is more deserving of accepting the excuse') supports dropping the obligation for those who cannot. The passage also clarifies the analogy with Zufar's view on gesturing: if the deceased was capable of even minimal gestures (like moving an eyebrow), he should will; otherwise not. Finally, the ruling on payment: the will is executed from one third of the deceased's estate, because his right during illness is limited to one third, and the heirs' right to two thirds is protected. If he did not will, the heir is not obligated but may volunteer. This also applies to debts like sadaqat al-fitr, maintenance, kharaj, and jizya.

Key Terms
فدية (fidyah): A compensatory payment (feeding a poor person) for each missed fast or prayer when one cannot make them up.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to extend the ruling of fasting to prayer despite qiyas.
وصية (wasiyya): A bequest made by a person during illness for fulfillment of missed religious obligations.
إدراك زمان (idrak zaman): Reaching a period of time sufficient to make up missed religious duties (e.g., health or residence after travel).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under which condition is a will for missed fasts NOT required?
A) When the deceased broke the fast with an excuse and never had time to make up
B) When the deceased broke the fast without an excuse and never made up
C) When the deceased had time to make up but did not
D) When the deceased made a will for the full estate

Key Takeaway
A will for missed fasts (and prayers by istihsan) is wajib only if the deceased had a genuine opportunity to make them up; the limit is one-third of the estate.

Obligation of Wasiyya for Missed Fasts: Exceptions and Scope
Ruling on wasiyya for missed fasts with excuses and without

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a person is exempt from making a will for fidyah and when it is obligatory, and list the types of missed fasts that require compensation.

Core Idea
A traveler or sick person who dies before qada' is exempt; one who missed without excuse must will fidyah for all days.

This lesson addresses a critical refinement in Hanafi fiqh: the obligation of making a will (wasiyya) for missed Ramadan fasts. While a person who intentionally misses fasts must arrange for fidyah after death, those with valid excuses who die before making them up are not liable. We will examine the reasoning and the scope of obligations, including various types of fasts that remain on the deceased's liability.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish excused from unexcused
Identify the two scenarios: 1) A traveler or sick person who dies before being able to make up missed fasts is excused and has no obligation to make a will. 2) One who missed fasts without a valid excuse (or with an excuse but later gained ability and died without making up) is obligated to make a will for all days missed (or for the portion he was able to make up if he had an excuse).
The key is whether the person had a valid excuse at the time of death for not making up the fasts.
2
Identify the scope of liability
The passage lists the types of fasts that remain on the deceased's liability: obligatory Ramadan fasts, expiatory fasts (kaffara), zihar fasts, fasts for offenses during ihram, and vowed (nadhr) fasts. Understand that these are all wajib fasts that may be compensated by fidyah after death.
Fidyah is only valid for fasts that have a compensatory alternative; some expiations require the fast itself.
3
Implement the obligation through the guardian
The guardian (heir or executor) pays the fidyah from one-third of the deceased's estate, because the testator's right to bequeath is limited to one-third during illness. If no will was made, the heir is not obligated but may volunteer to pay.
This principle applies similarly to other debts like sadaqat al-fitr, maintenance, kharaj, and jizyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Ruling on fasting in Ramadan: If the traveler and the sick person broke their fast and died before the traveler's return or the sick person's recovery, due to their not having caught up with a number of other days, they are not obligated to make a will for it. And it is obligatory upon him, meaning upon the one who broke his fast in Ramadan even without an excuse, to make a will for what he was able to catch up with from other days if he broke his fast with an excuse. And if he did not catch up with a number of other days and he broke his fast without an excuse, the will is necessary for all that he broke, because the shortcoming is from him, but it is hoped that he will be forgiven by the grace of Allah through the fidyah of what was required of him. And what remains on his liability until death overtakes him from fasting: obligatory, expiation, zihar, offense during ihram, and vowed fasts. So his guardian, meaning one who has authority over his wealth due to inheritance or executorship, takes it out from one-third of what he left, because the testator's right is in one-third of his wealth during his sickness and the heir's right is attached to two-thirds, so it is not enforceable against the heir except in the third if he bequeathed it. And if he did not bequeath, the heir is not obligated to pay it out; if he volunteers, it is permissible, as we will mention. And upon this model are the debt of sadaqat al-fitr, obligatory maintenance, kharaj, and jizyah on his liability. ...
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi discusses the rulings on missed fasts and the obligation of making a will (wasiyya) for fidyah. The text first addresses the case of a traveler or sick person who dies before being able to make up missed fasts: since they had an excuse, they are not required to make a will for fidyah. Then it covers the case of one who broke his fast without an excuse: he must make a will for fidyah for all the days he missed, because the shortcoming was his fault. The passage then explains what types of fasts remain on the deceased's liability: obligatory fasts, expiatory fasts (kaffara), zihar, offenses during ihram, and vowed fasts. The guardian (heir or executor) should pay from one-third of the deceased's wealth, as the deceased's right to dispose of his wealth during illness is limited to one-third. If the deceased did not bequeath, the heir is not obligated but may volunteer. The same principle applies to other debts like sadaqat al-fitr and maintenance. The commentary includes technical clarifications on wording and references to the durr al-mukhtar.

Key Terms
إيصاء (īṣāʾ): Making a will (wasiyya) regarding the payment of fidyah for missed fasts or other obligations.
فدية (fidya): Compensatory payment (usually food) for missed fasts that cannot be made up, given to the poor.
ظهار (ẓihār): A type of divorce-like declaration that requires expiation (kaffara) including fasting if unable to free a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must make a will for fidyah for all missed days.
B) He is not required to make a will because he had an excuse.
C) His heir must fast on his behalf.
D) His estate must pay a penalty.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of wasiyya for missed fasts depends on whether the deceased had a valid excuse at the time of death; those who died without being able to make up due to ongoing excuses are exempt.

Specification for Qada of Fasting from Two Ramadans
Ruling on ta'yin for qada of two Ramadans

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on ta'yin in qada of fasting from two Ramadans and apply the mufta bihi ruling to a scenario.

Core Idea
For qada of multiple Ramadans, specification is not required—completing the number suffices.

When a person owes missed fasts from two different Ramadans, does he need to specify which Ramadan each makeup fast belongs to? There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on this precise question. This lesson examines the two corrections (tashih) and identifies the relied-upon view that general intention is sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two corrections
Note that two different 'tashih' (corrections) are mentioned: one by al-Zayla'i requiring specification, and one by al-Khulasah rejecting it.
The passage explicitly calls them 'تصحيحين مختلفين' — two different corrections.
2
State al-Zayla'i's position and reasoning
Al-Zayla'i corrected that specification is necessary (luzum al-ta'yin). Understand that this implies a stricter view when multiple obligations exist.
Reasoning not fully given, but likely based on principle of distinguishing multiple obligations.
3
State al-Khulasah's position and its basis
Al-Khulasah corrected that specification is not necessary. The passage supports this by noting that the cause (sabab) of fasting is the month, not the specific day; completing the number is sufficient.
This view is consistent with the qada of fasts from a single Ramadan.
4
Apply the mufta bihi (chosen view)
The text says 'على المختار' (according to the chosen view), indicating that the view of no specification is the operative ruling for fatwa.
This is the tarjih: al-Khulasah's correction is preferred.
5
Distinguish from the case of one Ramadan
The passage notes that even for two days from one Ramadan, specification is not required, and it is even more clearly the case for two Ramadans.
This shows the issue is only about multiple Ramadans, but the principle is the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا الصوم الذي عليه من رمضانين إذا أراد قضاءه يفعل مثل هذا على أحد تصحيحين مختلفين صحح الزيلعي لزوم التعيين وصحح في الخلاصة عدم لزوم التعيين. وقضاء عليه قضاء يومين من رمضان واحد فقضى يوماً، ولم يعين جاز لأن السبب في الصوم واحد، وهو الشهر فالواجب عليه إكمال العدد وفي الأشباه عن الفتح من الصوم، ولو وجب عليه يومين من رمضان واحد الأولى أن ينوي أول يوم وجب عليه قضاؤه من هذا الرمضان، وان لم يعين جاز، وكذا لو كانا من رمضانين على المختار حتى لو نوى القضاء لا غير جاز اهـ.
And likewise, fasting that is due from two Ramadans, if he wants to make it up, he does like this according to one of two different corrections: al-Zayla'i corrected the necessity of specification, and al-Khulasah corrected the non-necessity of specification. And it is said: if there is a qada of two days from one Ramadan, and he makes up one day without specifying, it is valid because the cause of fasting is one, i.e., the month, so what is obligatory upon him is completing the number. In al-Ashbah from al-Fath regarding fasting: if two days from one Ramadan are obligatory upon him, it is better for him to intend the first day of qada from this Ramadan, and if he does not specify, it is valid. Likewise, if they are from two Ramadans, according to the chosen view, even if he intends the qada without specification, it is valid. End quote.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage extends the principle of ta'yin to fasting. When a person owes fasts from two different Ramadans, there is a difference of opinion: al-Zayla'i insists on specification, while al-Khulasah does not. The commentary also clarifies that if the fasts are from a single Ramadan, specification is not needed. The relied-upon position according to the text is the one from al-Khulasah (no specification).

Key Terms
تصحيح (tashih): A correction or preferred ruling in a matter of dispute among Hanafi scholars.
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification; making an intention specific to a particular Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Specification is only required if from one Ramadan
D) Fasting cannot be made up from two Ramadans

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that specification (ta'yin) is not necessary when making up missed fasts from two different Ramadans; general intention suffices.

The Definition of Fasting: Linguistic and Legal Meanings
Opening of Kitab al-Sawm: defining sawm linguistically and legally

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definitions of sawm according to the Hanafi school and explain why 'imsak' is used instead of 'tark'.

Core Idea
Fasting is active abstention (imsak) from entering anything during the daytime, not mere abandonment.

Fasting (sawm) is a physical act of worship like prayer, so it is placed right after the book of prayer. Before discussing its rulings, the author first defines what fasting means both in language (lughah) and in the Shari'ah (shar'an). This lesson unpacks that definition, showing that the word 'imsak' (restraint) is deliberately chosen over 'tark' (abandonment) to highlight the active nature of refraining.

Guided Path
1
Separate the two definitions
Identify the linguistic definition ('abstention from action and speech') and the legal definition ('abstention during the daytime from entering'). Understand that the legal definition adds temporal boundaries and the object of abstention.
The linguistic definition is broader; the legal one is specific to the act of worship.
2
Analyze the term 'imsak'
Note that the author uses 'imsak' (restraint) rather than 'tark' (abandonment). The commentary explains that this is because the commanded act is a positive deed (fi'l) of the mukallaf, not mere passivity. This distinction affects issues like intention and the ruling of remaining inactive.
Imsak implies a conscious, ongoing effort.
3
Define the temporal frame
The daytime is defined as the period from true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq) to sunset (ghurub al-shams). The commentary explains that sunset occurs when the entire disk of the sun has disappeared, confirmed by darkness appearing in the east.
This matches the hadith: 'When the night comes from here, the fasting person has broken his fast.'
4
Recognize the implied elements
The definition 'abstention from entering' hints at the things that break the fast (food, drink, sexual intercourse). Also, the legal definition presupposes intention (niyyah), which is discussed later.
The full legal definition in Hanafi fiqh includes intention, but that is covered in subsequent sections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصوم
لما كان عبادة بدنية كالصلاة ذكره عقبها ويحتاج لمعرفته لغة وشريعة، وسببه، وشرطه وحكمه وركنه وحكمة شرعيته وصفته فمعناه لغة الإمساك عن الفعل والقول وشرعاً (هو الإمساك نهاراً) النهار ضد الليل من الفجر الصادق إلى الغروب (عن إدخال
قوله : (ذكره) أي الصوم عقبها، وكثير من المؤلفين ذكر الزكاة بعد الصلاة، وأخر الصوم ووجهه اقتران الزكاة مع الصلاة في آيات كثيرة من الكتاب العزيز ولما في القهستاني أفضل الأعمال بعد الزكاة الصوم وفرض بعد صرف القبلة إلى الكعبة لعشر في شعبان بعد الهجرة بسنة، ونصف، وفي الأجهوري بعد مضي ليلتين من شعبان المذكور. قوله : ( ويحتاج لمعرفته الخ) قد ذكر ذلك من هنا إلى آخر الفصل، فلا يحتاج إلى التنبيه عليه، ويحتاج بالبناء للمجهول أي يحتاج المكلف. قوله: (فمعناه لغة الإمساك الخ) ظاهره أنه حقيقة لغوية في وهي ما تفيده عبارة ،الصحاح وفي المغرب هو إمساك الإنسان عن الأكل والشرب ومن مجازه صام الفرس إذا لم يعتلف، وقول النابغة :
ذلك،
خيل صيام، وخـيـل غــيـر صــائـمـة
نهر قوله : (هو الإمساك نهاراً) إنما عبر به دون ترك لأن المأمور به فعل المكلف، وهو الإمساك بحر. قوله : (النهار) ضد الليل قال في الشرح : النوار عبارة عن زمان ممتد من طلوع الفجر الصادق إلى غروب الشمس، وهو قول أصحاب الله واللغة. قوله : (إلى الغروب) هو أول زمان بعد غيبوبة تمام جرم الشمس بحيث تظهر الحلمة في جهة المشرق، وفي البخاري عنه : إذا أقبل الليل من ههنا فقد أفطر الصائم أي إذا وجدت الظلمة حساً في جهة المشرق فقد دخل وقت الفطر، أو صار مفطراً في الحكم لأن الليل ليس ظرفاً للصوم
Book of Fasting. Since it is a physical act of worship like prayer, he mentioned it after it. One needs to know its meaning linguistically and legally, its cause, its condition, its ruling, its pillar, the wisdom of its legislation, and its description. Its meaning linguistically is abstention from action and speech. Legally, it is abstention during the daytime – daytime is the opposite of night from true dawn to sunset – from entering... His statement: (he mentioned it) i.e., fasting after it. Many authors mention zakat after prayer and delay fasting, the reason being the association of zakat with prayer in many verses of the Noble Book, and as in al-Qahistani: the best deeds after zakat is fasting, and it was made obligatory after the change of qibla to the Kaaba on ten nights in Sha'ban, one and a half years after the hijrah, and in al-Ujhuri: after the passage of two nights of the mentioned Sha'ban. His statement: (and one needs to know it etc.) He has mentioned that from here to the end of the chapter, so no need to draw attention to it; 'one needs' is in the passive voice, i.e., the obligated person needs. His statement: (so its meaning linguistically is abstention etc.) Its apparent meaning is that it is a linguistic reality in what the phrase means. In al-Sihah and al-Mughrib, it is a person's abstention from eating and drinking. Among its metaphorical uses is 'the horse fasted' when it does not eat fodder, and the saying of al-Nabigha: 'Horses are fasting and horses are not fasting.' His statement: (it is abstention during the daytime) he expressed it with abstention rather than abandonment because the command is the action of the obligated person, which is abstention with restriction. His statement: (the daytime) opposite of night. He said in al-Sharh: The daytime is a time period extending from the rising of the true dawn to the setting of the sun, which is the statement of the people of Allah and language. His statement: (to sunset) it is the first time after the complete disappearance of the sun's disk such that the darkness appears in the east. In al-Bukhari from him: When the night comes from here, the fasting person has broken his fast, i.e., when darkness is perceived in the east, the time of breaking the fast has entered, or he becomes one who has broken the fast in ruling because the night is not a time for fasting.
Source pages p. 631

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Fasting (Kitab al-Sawm) in Maraqi al-Falah with the commentary of al-Tahtawi. The author notes that fasting is a physical act of worship like prayer, so it is mentioned right after the book of prayer. Many authors place zakat before fasting, but here fasting follows prayer because of its similarity in being a bodily act. The passage then outlines that one must know the definition of sawm both linguistically and legally, as well as its cause, conditions, rulings, pillars, wisdom, and description. The linguistic definition is 'abstention from action and speech' (al-imsak an al-fi'l wa al-qawl). This is the literal meaning. The legal definition (shar'an) is 'abstention during the daytime from entering' — with the daytime defined as the period from true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq) to sunset. The commentary explains that the author used 'abstention' (imsak) rather than 'abandonment' (tark) because the commanded act is the positive action of refraining, not mere non-action. The daytime is defined as the opposite of night, extending from true dawn to sunset, based on the statements of the scholars of language and the Shari'ah. The end of fasting time is determined by complete sunset, when the darkness appears in the east, as confirmed by the hadith in Bukhari: 'When the night comes from here, the fasting person has broken his fast.' This means that once the night begins (which is the time for iftar), fasting is no longer valid because the night is not the time for fasting. The commentary also references Qahistani and Ujhuri for the historical context of when fasting was made obligatory.

Key Terms
صوم (sawm): Linguistically: abstention (imsak) from action and speech. Legally: abstention from entering anything during daytime from true dawn to sunset, with the intention of worship.
إمساك (imsak): To hold back or restrain oneself; in fasting, it is the active abstention from things that break the fast.
الفجر الصادق (al-fajr al-sadiq): The true dawn; the horizontal light that spreads across the horizon, marking the beginning of the fasting day.
غروب الشمس (ghurub al-shams): Sunset; the complete disappearance of the sun's disk below the horizon, marking the end of the fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the legal (shar'i) definition of fasting?
A) Not eating or drinking from dawn to sunset
B) Abstention from entering anything during daytime from true dawn to sunset
C) Abstention from all pleasures and sleep
D) Silence and avoidance of all actions

Key Takeaway
Fasting (sawm) is not merely abandoning food and drink but actively refraining (imsak) from entering anything that breaks the fast during the specific daytime period from true dawn to sunset.

Sawm — Fasting

The Hanafi Legal Definition of Fasting (Sawm) and Its Cause of Obligation
Opens the Book of Fasting with definition and cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal definition of sawm, identify its key components, and explain the cause of obligation for Ramadan.

Core Idea
Fasting in Hanafi fiqh is abstaining from nullifiers with intention, from dawn to sunset.

This lesson opens the Book of Fasting by defining its core act linguistically and legally. You will learn that sawm is more than just refraining from food and drink — it includes abstaining from sexual desire and any intentional entry into the body, with intention to worship. We will also examine the cause that makes fasting obligatory: sighting the new moon of Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Recognize that fasting (sawm) is a physical worship (ibada badaniyya), similar to prayer, hence mentioned after it in the text.
2
Distinguish linguistic vs. legal meaning
Linguistically, sawm means abstention from actions and speech. Legally, it is a specific, conditioned abstention during the day with intention.
The text uses 'imsak' (active refrain) rather than 'tark' (leaving) to emphasize the commission of worship.
3
Deconstruct the legal definition into components
The definition comprises: (1) Imsak (abstention), (2) Nahar (day: from true dawn to sunset), (3) from 'idkhal' (entry of anything into the body, including through mouth/nose/wounds), (4) from 'shahwat al-farj' (sexual desire, i.e., intercourse and emission), (5) with 'niyyah' (intention to distinguish worship from habit).
Forgetfulness and entry of dust are excluded from nullifiers.
4
Define the cause of obligation (sabab wujub)
The cause for fasting Ramadan is sighting the new moon (shahud juz' minhu). Obligation begins with sighting or completing 30 days of Sha'ban.
This is a cause (sabab), not a condition or pillar.
5
Apply conditions of validity (shurut)
Three conditions for validity: Islam, purity from menstruation/postpartum bleeding, intention. Additional conditions for obligation (not validity) include puberty and ability.
A child’s fast is valid; a person who becomes insane after intention retains a valid fast.

Book of Fasting. Since it is a physical worship like prayer, he mentioned it after it. One needs to know it linguistically and legally: its cause, condition, ruling, pillar, wisdom of legislation, and description. Its linguistic meaning is abstention from action and speech. Legally: (It is abstention during the day) - day is the opposite of night from true dawn to sunset - (from entering anything) whether usually eaten or otherwise. The restriction of entry excludes entry of dust, and being (intentional or mistaken) excludes forgetfulness. The mistaken one is he from whom rinsing water precedes to his throat; then it is like intentional, whether he entered it (into a belly) from the mouth or nose, or from a wound in the interior called al-ja'ifa, or he entered it into (what has the ruling of the interior) which is the brain like medicine for al-amma. (And) abstention during the day from the desire of the private part encompasses intercourse and emission through foreplay, (with intention) to distinguish worship from habit, from its people, excluding the menstruating, postpartum, disbeliever, and insane. An abbreviation of this correct definition is: abstention from nullifiers intended for Allah the Exalted with His permission in its time. (And the cause of obligation of Ramadan) means the obligation of its fast (witnessing a part) valid for fasting (of it) i.e. al-Qahustani, and for the rememberer of al-wisal is given. He said: (whether usually eaten or otherwise) i.e. in the ruling of breaking the fast, even if the ruling differs concerning the obligation of expiation or not. He said: (it excludes forgetfulness) i.e. entry forgetfully, like one who eats or drinks forgetfully, then his fast is not invalidated, and similarly one who has intercourse forgetfully. He said: (it is like intentional) i.e. in invalidation, not in obligation of expiation. He said: (whether he entered it etc.) the first is omitted, and his word 'belly' is made object of his word 'entry of something'. He said: (from the mouth) is attached to 'he entered it', and similar to what is mentioned is if he enters it into his anus, or inserts drops into his urethra or ear. He said: (called al-ja'ifa) it is a wound reaching the cavity. He said: (al-amma) with elongation and shaddah on the mim, a wound reaching the membrane of the brain. He said: (and emission through foreplay) then it invalidates even if expiation is not obligatory, and what is meant by intercourse is the usual intercourse. He said: (to distinguish worship) which is abstention from nullifiers with intention of worship, and his word from habit, which is abstention from eating following his usual habit, and similarly abstention as a diet. He said: 'from its people' is the specific person in whom the three conditions of validity are gathered: Islam, purity from menstruation and postpartum bleeding, intention, and knowledge of obligation if in dar al-harb, or being in our dar, and if he does not know the obligation, then Islam and purity are conditions of obligation and validity, and knowledge of obligation or residing in our dar is a condition of obligation only. As for puberty and ability, they are not conditions of validity because the fast of a child is valid and he is rewarded, and the fast of one who becomes insane or unconscious after intention is valid, but their fast the next day is not valid due to lack of intention. He said: (excluding the menstruating and postpartum) i.e. as long as menstruation and postpartum bleeding are upon them, but if they become pure from them, their fast is valid even if they do not perform ghusl. He said: 'abstention from nullifiers' - object that there is circularity in this definition since nullifiers are invalidators of fasting, so their knowledge depends on knowing fasting, depending on knowing them. He said: (with His permission) excludes what his word 'from its people' produces, and his word 'in its time' is the day mentioned in the lengthy definition. He said: (cause of obligation of Ramadan) - it is originally from ramada 'he burned', named because sins burn therein, and it is indeclinable for being a proper noun and the extra alif and nun, and Jumada is indeclinable for the alif of feminine prolongation, and it is declined.
Source pages p. 631

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the Book of Fasting from Hashiya al-Tahtawi, defining fasting linguistically and legally and stating its cause of obligation. The author first explains why fasting is mentioned after prayer: because it is a physical worship like prayer. He then lists what needs to be known: its linguistic and legal meaning, cause, condition, ruling, pillar, wisdom, and description. Linguistically, fasting (saum) means abstention from actions and speech. Legally, it is defined as abstention during the day (from true dawn to sunset) from entering anything into the body, whether food or otherwise, intentionally or mistakenly (excluding forgetfulness and dust). The definition also includes abstention from sexual desire (intercourse and emission). Intention (niyyah) is required to distinguish worship from habit. The author then gives a concise definition: abstention from nullifiers intended for Allah with His permission in its time. The cause of obligation of fasting Ramadan is witnessing (sighting) a part of it. The commentary expands on each phrase: it clarifies that the definition covers both eating and non-eating nullifiers, intentional and mistaken (except forgetfulness which does not break the fast), and specifies that the interior includes wounds reaching the cavity and brain. Conditions of validity are explained: Islam, purity from menstruation/postpartum, intention, and knowledge of obligation depending on location. The fast of a child is valid, and of one who becomes insane after intention. The menstruating and postpartum are excluded while bleeding, but valid when pure. A circularity objection about defining fasting with nullifiers is answered: 'nullifiers' here means edibles and the like. Finally, the etymology of Ramadan is given: from 'ramada' (burning) because sins burn, and its grammatical status is indeclinable.

Key Terms
صوم (sawm): Legally: abstention from nullifiers during the day with intention from dawn to sunset.
إمساك (imsak): The act of refraining; used in definition of sawm as abstention.
نية (niyyah): Intention to distinguish worship from habit; required for validity.
مفطر (muftir): Something that breaks the fast; includes edibles, non-edibles, intercourse, etc.
سبب وجوب (sabab wujub): Cause of obligation; for Ramadan it is sighting the new moon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in this passage, what is the legal meaning of fasting (sawm)?
A) Refraining from eating and drinking only from dawn to sunset
B) Abstention during the day from entering anything into the body, from sexual desire, with intention, from dawn to sunset
C) Not eating or drinking for the entire day
D) Avoiding sin and performing good deeds

Key Takeaway
Fasting (sawm) in Hanafi fiqh is abstention from all nullifiers during the day with intention, and its obligation is triggered by sighting the new moon of Ramadan.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
6 min
The Cause of Obligation for Fasting Ramadan: Two Hanafi Views
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the sabab of fasting obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on the sabab of fasting each day of Ramadan and identify the precise difference in their definitions.

Core Idea
The cause of fasting each day is witnessing a suitable part of that day, not any part of the month.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi debate: what exactly triggers the obligation to fast a specific day of Ramadan? Is it merely witnessing any part of the month (day or night) as Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi held, or is it witnessing a specific part of each day that is suitable for initiating the fast, as Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi argued? The answer determines who must make up missed fasts in unusual circumstances. Let us unpack the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Find the two contrasting views of al-Sarakhsi and Fakhr al-Islam on what constitutes the sabab for fasting each day.
Al-Sarakhsi: absolute witnessing of any part of the month. Fakhr al-Islam: witnessing the suitable part of each day.
2
Define 'suitable part'
What exactly is the 'suitable part' according to Fakhr al-Islam? Note the time range: from fajr sadiq to just before al-duha al-kubra.
This time window is when fasting can be initiated; after duha kubra the day is not suitable for starting the fast.
3
Understand the rationale
Why does Fakhr al-Islam restrict the sabab to that window? Because the night interposes and breaks continuity, and after duha the day is no longer suitable for initiating the fast.
The fast is a daytime act; the night is a separate unit that prevents the obligation from carrying over.
4
Contrast with al-Sarakhsi's view
Al-Sarakhsi holds that witnessing any part of the month, including nights, is sufficient. What logic supports that?
He considers the month as a continuous whole; any part triggers obligation for the entire month.
5
Recognize the agreement
Both agree that Ramadan is only obligatory by witnessing a part of it; they differ on which part counts.
The dispute is within the school; both are valid, but the majority supports Fakhr al-Islam.

الفعل شاغل له من أوله إلى آخره قال في الشرح، ولئلا يلزم تقديم الشيء على سببه أي لو جعلنا السبب المجموع، والواجب الصوم قبل تحقق المجموع للزم تقديم الصوم على سببه
The book of fasting: Ramadan excludes the night and what is after midday according to what Fakhr al-Islam and those who follow him said, contrary to Shams al-A'imma that the cause is the absolute time in the month, and every day of it (i.e., of Ramadan) is a cause for performing it, i.e., for the obligation of performing that day, due to the dispersion of days. So whoever reaches puberty or embraces Islam is obligated for what remains, not what has passed nor other than them. It contains that Sha'ban is like Ramadan. Al-Jawhari said it is pluralized as armida', ramadanat, and ramadin like salatin. They agreed that the proper noun in three months is the combination of the mudaf and mudaf ilayhi: Shahr Ramadan, Rabi' al-Awwal, and Rabi' al-Akhir. So the deletion of 'shahr' here is of the type of deleting part of a word, except that they permitted it because they treat such a proper noun like a mudaf-mudaf ilayhi construction where they give i'rab to both parts. And in Sharh al-Mashariq by Ibn Malik: Rabi' with tanwin, and al-Awwal is an adjective, and its idafa to al-Awwal is a mistake. He (the author) said: 'meaning the obligation of fasting it' - he indicated that wujub means obligation, and that there is a deleted mudaf in the expression. He said: 'witnessing of a suitable part' - an objection was raised that a boy who reaches puberty during the month has witnessed a part of it, so it would require making up what passed before puberty. The answer is that the condition of obligation (i.e., puberty) did not exist in the past. The upshot of what the author mentioned is that they agreed that Ramadan is only obligatory by witnessing a part of it, then they differed. al-Sarakhsi held that the cause is absolute witnessing of any part of the month, so days and nights are equal. Fakhr al-Islam and those who followed him held that it is the part in which fasting can be initiated each day, as in al-Durr, which is from the break of true dawn until just before the major forenoon. What is after that until dawn does not obligate anything by its witnessing. The practical consequence of the difference appears in the case of one who becomes conscious on the first night of the month, then becomes insane before dawn for the entire month, then regains consciousness after that; or who becomes conscious during a night of it, or after midday of a day of it, then insanity returns before dawn; he must make up on the view of Shams al-A'imma, contrary to the other view. In al-Mughni, the view of Fakhr al-Islam and his followers was authenticated, and the fatwa is upon it as in al-Mujtaba and al-Nahr from al-Diraya. More than one authenticated it, and it is the truth as in al-Ghaya. In al-Khabbazi, the first view was chosen, so there are two authenticated opinions, but the fatwa and most authentication are on the view of Fakhr al-Islam. His saying: 'suitable part' means suitable for initiating fasting, which is from dawn to just before the major forenoon. His saying: 'absolute time in the month' is better, for he said the cause is absolute time in the month. His saying: 'and every day of it' means the first part in which fasting can be initiated from each day, not the whole day, otherwise it would entail obligation after the completion of that day, nor the absolute part, otherwise it would obligate fasting a day in which a boy reaches puberty after midday. This is from Tuhfat al-Akhyar. It is an explanatory conjunction to his saying: 'witnessing of a suitable part'. So the author relied on the statement of Fakhr al-Islam and did not mention the statement of Shams al-A'imma; the sharh mentioned it by saying 'contrary to Shams al-A'imma'. His saying: 'the dispersion of days' - in the sharh: because fasting days are a worship that is dispersed like the dispersion of prayer in times, even more so due to the interposition of a time unsuitable for fasting at all, which is the night. So this interposition prevents the extension of the part of the day to what follows. His saying: 'not what has passed' i.e., by agreement. His saying: 'no contradiction in combining the two causes' - in the sharh: we followed al-Hidaya in combining the two causes because there is no contradiction: the witnessing of a specific part of the month is a cause for the whole, then each day is a cause for its own fasting. At most, the cause for the obligation of fasting a day is repeated in terms of its specificity and its inclusion within another. Al-Kamal said: How is this combination possible? They are two divergent opinions, and what is branched on one cannot be branched on the other. Also, if the cause is the combination, each is a partial cause, not independent, otherwise the effect would follow from each alone. Also, what need is there for the general cause when the specific is sufficient, for witnessing a part of the day contains a part of the month? Moreover, the author did not combine, as we pointed out; rather, he relied on the view of Fakhr al-Islam. So let one reflect. His saying: 'from the combination' means from the whole month. His saying: 'for the first part' where we said that it is permissible to intend performing the obligation from the first night, despite the permissibility of intention before the cause of obligation, like if one intends to fast tomorrow before sunset. This is in the sharh, and it is better to express 'to' instead of 'for'. His saying: 'observing its role as a standard' means considering it as a standard that does not accept anything else, so its time is like a single thing; witnessing its beginning is like witnessing its completion, and the act fills it from beginning to end. In the sharh: And to prevent the advancement of the thing before its cause: if we made the cause the combination, the obligatory fast would be before the realization of the combination, requiring the advancement of the fast before its cause.
Source pages p. 633

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the sabab (cause) that triggers the obligation to fast Ramadan. The base text and commentary discuss two positions. The first, from Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, holds that the cause is the mere witnessing of any part of the month – day or night. The second, from Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and others, holds that the cause is specifically witnessing the part of each day that is suitable for initiating the fast, i.e., from fajr sadiq (true dawn) to just before the major forenoon (duha kubra). The commentary provides the thamarah (practical consequence): a person who becomes conscious at the first night then becomes insane for the whole month must make up all fasts according to al-Sarakhsi, but not according to al-Bazdawi. The author (al-Tahtawi) clarifies that although both views have been authenticated, the fatwa and the majority of authentications are on the view of Fakhr al-Islam. The commentary then addresses an objection about combining the two causes, arguing that they are not contradictory: the part of the month causes the obligation, and each day's suitable part causes its own fast. Ultimately, the author follows Fakhr al-Islam's view.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The legal cause that triggers the obligation of fasting; in this context, the witnessing of a part of the day or month
شهود جزء صالح (shuhud juz' salih): Witnessing (i.e., experiencing or being present in) a suitable part of the day, specifically from fajr sadiq to just before the major forenoon
الضحوة الكبرى (al-duha al-kubra): The major forenoon, approximately the time when the sun is well above the horizon, before noon; until this time is considered suitable for initiating the fast

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in this passage, what triggers the obligation to fast a specific day of Ramadan?
A) Witnessing any part of the month, including nights
B) Witnessing the entire day from dawn to sunset
C) Witnessing the part of the day suitable for initiating the fast (dawn to before major forenoon)
D) The mere intention to fast

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi position is that the cause for fasting each day of Ramadan is the witnessing of the suitable part of that day, not any part of the month.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for Obligation and Validity of Ramadan Fasting
States conditions for obligation and validity of Ramadan fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for obligation of Ramadan fasting, distinguish them from the three conditions for validity, and apply the Hanafi dispute on the knowledge requirement for a new Muslim in dar al-harb.

Core Idea
Fasting Ramadan is fard 'ayn only when four conditions are met; its validity requires separate conditions.

Fasting in Ramadan is a fundamental act of worship, but not everyone is obligated to perform it immediately. The classical Hanafi scholars delineated precise conditions that must exist for the obligation to apply and for the fast to be valid. This lesson unpacks those conditions as explained in Al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah, highlighting the key distinctions between shurut al-wujub (conditions of obligation) and shurut al-sihha (conditions of validity).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Start by recognizing that the act under discussion is the fast of Ramadan, which is fard 'ayn (an individual obligation) for every qualified Muslim.
This is the foundation before examining conditions.
2
Distinguish Shurut al-Wujub from Shurut al-Sihha
Understand the Hanafi classification: shurut al-wujub are prerequisites for the obligation itself, while shurut al-sihha are prerequisites for the act to be valid when performed.
Missing a wujub condition means no duty; missing a sihha condition means invalid fast.
3
List the Four Conditions for Obligation
Extract the four conditions: Islam, reason (‘aql), puberty (bulugh), and knowledge of the obligation. For a new Muslim in dar al-harb, knowledge depends on a reliable report; note the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the reporter's qualifications.
The knowledge condition applies only to those in dar al-harb; in dar al-Islam ignorance is no excuse.
4
Identify the Three Conditions for Obligation of Performance
The obligation to perform the fast in its time also requires: soundness from illness, freedom from menstruation/postpartum bleeding, and residency (i.e., not traveling).
These relate to being able to perform the fast physically and legally.
5
List the Three Conditions for Validity
For the fast to be valid, three conditions must be met: intention (niyyah) at the appropriate time, freedom from menstruation/postpartum bleeding (which invalidate), and freedom from other invalidators (like eating/drinking). Note that major ritual impurity (janabah) is not a condition for validity.
Intention is required for each day of fasting and must be made before fajr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وهو) رمضان (فرض) عين (أداء وقضاء على من اجتمع فيه أربعة أشياء) هي شروط لافتراضه والخطاب به وتسمى شروط وجوب أحدها (الإسلام) لأنه شرط للخطاب بفروع الشريعة (و) ثانيها (العقل) إذ لا خطاب بدونه (و) ثالثها (البلوغ) إذ لا تكليف إلا به (و) رابعها العلم بالوجوب) وهو شرط لمن أسلم بدار الحرب) وإنما يحصل له العلم الموجب باخبار رجلين عدلين أو رجل وامرأتين مستورين أو واحد عدل، وعندهما لا تشترط العدالة ولا البلوغ والحرية وقوله (أو (الكون شرط لمن نشأ (بدار الإسلام) فإنه لا عذر له بالجهل ويشترط لوجوب أدائه الذي هو عبارة عن تفريغ الذمة في وقته (الصحة من مرض) لقوله تعالى : فمن كان منكم مريضاً ) الآية (و) الصحة أي الخلو عن (حيض ونفاس) لما قدمناه (والإقامة) لما تلوناه ويشترط لصحة أدائه أي فعله ليكون أعم من الأداء والقضاء (ثلاثة) شرائط (النية) في وقتها لكل يوم ( والخلو عما ينافيه) أي ينافي صحة فعله (من حيض ونفاس) لمنافاتهما (و) الخلو (عما يفسده) بطرقه عليه (ولا يشترط) لصحة (الخلو عن الجنابة) لقدرته على الإزالة وضرورة حصولها ليلاً وطرق النهار وليس العقل
And it (Ramadan) is a personal obligation, both performance and make-up, upon whoever gathers four things. These are conditions for its obligation and addressing it, and they are called conditions of obligation. One of them is Islam, because it is a condition for addressing with the branches of Shariah. The second is reason, for there is no address without it. The third is puberty, for there is no obligation except with it. The fourth is knowledge of the obligation, and it is a condition for one who becomes Muslim in a land of war. And he only obtains knowledge that obligates him by the report of two just men, or one man and two women who are covered (i.e., reliable), or one just person. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), neither uprightness, nor puberty, nor freedom is a condition. And His (the author's) saying: 'or being (a condition) is a condition for one who grew up in a land of Islam, for he has no excuse due to ignorance.' And for the obligation of its performance, which is the emptying of the liability in its time, soundness from illness is a condition, due to His statement: 'So whoever among you is ill...' and soundness (i.e., being free) from menstruation and postpartum bleeding, as we have mentioned, and residency (is also a condition). And for the validity of its performance, i.e., the act itself, to include both performance and make-up, three conditions are required: intention at its time for each day; being free from what contradicts it, i.e., contradicts the validity of the act, such as menstruation and postpartum bleeding, because they contradict it; and being free from what invalidates it. And being free from major ritual impurity is not a condition for validity, because of the ability to remove it and the necessity of its occurrence at night and the approach of daytime.
Source pages p. 634

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of Al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah defines the conditions for the obligation and validity of fasting in Ramadan. The author first identifies four conditions that must be present in a person for fasting Ramadan to be obligatory: (1) Islam, because only Muslims are addressed by Shariah; (2) reason (aql), since there is no legal address without rationality; (3) puberty (bulugh), because obligations (taklif) only apply to adults; (4) knowledge of the obligation (ilm al-wujub), which is further conditioned on whether the person is in dar al-harb (non-Muslim territory) or dar al-Islam. In dar al-harb, knowledge is established by the report of two just men, or one man and two reliable women, or one just man according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) do not require uprightness, puberty, or freedom in the reporter. In dar al-Islam, ignorance is no excuse. Next, the passage distinguishes conditions for the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada') from conditions for validity (sihha). For obligation of performance, one must be healthy (not ill), free from menstruation and postpartum bleeding, and a resident (not a traveler). For validity of the act, three conditions are needed: (1) intention (niyyah) at the appropriate time for each day; (2) freedom from anything that contradicts the act, specifically menstruation and postpartum bleeding; (3) freedom from what invalidates it, such as eating and drinking. Notably, major ritual impurity (janabah) is not a condition for validity because one can remove it, and its occurrence at night is common. The commentary thus clarifies the hierarchical structure of conditions in Hanafi fiqh for fasting.

Key Terms
شروط الوجوب (shurut al-wujub): Conditions that must be present in a person for an act to be legally obligatory (wajib/fard).
شرط الصحة (shart al-sihha): A condition that must be present for the act to be valid; if absent, the act is invalid.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where Islamic law is not enforced, used here to determine conditions for knowledge of obligation.
دار الإسلام (dar al-Islam): Territory under Muslim rule where Islamic law is applied; ignorance of obligations is generally not accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of fasting Ramadan?
A) Islam
B) Reason
C) Wealth
D) Puberty

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school conditions the obligation of Ramadan fasting on Islam, reason, puberty, and knowledge, and further separates conditions for performance (health, freedom from menses, residency) from conditions for validity (intention, freedom from menses, avoiding invalidators).

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
10 min
Conditions for Obligation and Validity of Fasting
Explains four obligation conditions and three validity conditions for fasting, with an intra-Hanafi dispute on the knowledge condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for the obligation of fasting and the three conditions for its validity according to the Hanafi school, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the knowledge condition.

Core Idea
Fasting is obligated only when four conditions are met; validity requires three conditions—including pre-dawn intention and freedom from nullifiers—but not janaba.

Fasting in Ramadan is a fundamental obligation, but not everyone is bound by it at all times. The Hanafi school distinguishes between conditions that make fasting obligatory (shurut al-wujub) and conditions that make the act of fasting valid (shurut al-sihhah). This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah unpacks both sets, including a critical nuance: the knowledge condition for a new Muslim in dar al-harb, where a difference of opinion between Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples (the Sahibayn) arises. Let's work through the text to build a precise understanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sets of conditions
The author first lists four conditions for obligation: knowledge, health, freedom from menstruation/postnatal bleeding, and residency. Then he lists three conditions for validity: intention, freedom from menstruation/postnatal bleeding, and freedom from nullifiers. Locate the transition phrase 'ويشترط لصحة أدائه'.
Note that freedom from menstruation appears in both sets.
2
Examine the knowledge condition for a new Muslim
The passage discusses how a person who accepts Islam in dar al-harb learns of the obligation. Abu Hanifa requires the reporter to be 'adil (just) and free, while the Sahibayn do not require justice, puberty, or freedom. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The term 'مستورين' (concealed women) indicates they are known to be upright but not necessarily just.
3
Analyze the dalil for health and residency conditions
The author cites Quran 2:184 as proof: 'فمن كان منكم مريضاً أو على سفر فعدة من أيام أخر'. The verse grants concessions for illness and travel, implying that health and residency are prerequisites for the full obligation.
The dalil is qat'i in transmission (Quran) but zanni in indication (dalala), as it requires interpretation.
4
List the three validity conditions
For the fast itself to be valid, three things are required: intention (made before dawn for Ramadan), freedom from menstruation/postnatal bleeding (which invalidate if they occur), and freedom from things that spoil the fast (intentional eating/drinking, etc.). Janaba (major impurity) is explicitly NOT a condition.
The passage clarifies: 'ولا يشترط لصحة الخلو عن الجنابة'.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on 'adalah affects the obligation of a new Muslim. Under Abu Hanifa, if no just reporter is found, the person is not obligated until a just one appears; under the Sahibayn, any reliable report triggers immediate obligation. The mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn.
The commentary adds that if the person later learns of the obligation, there is no qada' for the missed days because there was no knowledge at the time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قوله: (وإنما يحصل له العلم الموجب) أي للخطاب. قوله : (مستورين) الظاهر أنه بصيغة الجمع، وغلب جانب الرجل فذكر قوله : (أو واحد عدل قال في الينابيع : العدل من لم يطعن عليه في بطن ولا فرج ومنه الكذب لخروجه من البطن ا هـ در من الشهادة، وذكر في مسائل شتى من القضاء أنه يشترط في أخبار المسلم الذي لم يهاجر بالشرائع أحد شطري الشهادة أي أما العدد وأما العدالة من غير ذكر ،خلاف وظاهر كلام المؤلف أن الإمام يشترط البلوغ، والحرية في المخبر ويحرر قوله : ( وعندهما لا تشترط (العدالة أي في المخبر أي ولو واحداً، وأفاد أنه لا بد من العلم اتفاقاً فإذا لم يعلم على اختلاف القولين، ثم علم بافتراض الصوم ليس عليه قضاء ما مضى إذ لا تكليف بدون العلم ثمة للعذر كذا في الشرح قوله : (أو الكون أي الحلول، وهو عطف على العلم أفاده في الشرح قوله : (شرط لمن نشأ) الأولى أن يؤخره عن قوله : بدار الإسلام ويقول وهو شرط لمن نشأ بها قوله : (عن تفزيغ الذمة) أي ذمة المكلف عن الواجب في وقته المعين له قوله (الآية) تمامها، أو على سفر فعدة من أيام أخر. قوله : (أي الخلق) إنما أوله بذلك لأنّ دم الحيض والنفاس دم صحة لا مرض . قوله : (لما قدمناه) أي من أنهما ليسا أهلاً للصوم. قوله : لما تلوناه) أي بقوله الآية، وقد ذكرنا تمامها، والأولى للشرح ذكرها ليتم له المرام. قوله : (في وقتها الوقت بالنسبة لأداء رمضان بعد الغروب إلى قبيل الضحوة فسقي أي جزء منه، وجدت صح، وبالنسبة لقضائه الليل كله، ولا تجزىء النية بعد طلوع الفجر . قوله : أي ينافي صحة فعله الأظهر حذف صحة قوله: (من حيض ونفاس) فالخلو عنهما من شروط الوجوب أي وجوب الأداء وشروط الصحة. قوله: (لمنافاتهما الأولى زيادة إياه . قوله : (بطرقه عليه متعلق بيفسده. قوله: لقدرته على الإزالة أي بخلاف الحيض والنفاس. قوله : (وضرورة حصولها) أي ولضرورة حصولها يعني أن الإنسان قد يضطر إليها ليلاً ويطرأ عليه النهار أي يطلع عليه الفجر أي من غير تمكن من الغسل، وليس القصد التقييد بالضرورة أي بل المراد أن ذلك قد يحصل فلم يعتبر الشارع ذلك.
Book of Fasting. Fourth: Knowledge of obligation. It is a condition for one who embraced Islam in dar al-harb.
