Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
12 min
Classification of Voluntary and Disliked Fasts
Classifies fasts into types and details disliked fasts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a non-obligatory fast as nafl, makruh tanzih, or makruh tahrim based on Hanafi criteria and evidence, and apply the rulings on specific disliked fasts.

Core Idea
Non-obligatory fasts are either supererogatory or disliked, with two degrees of dislike determined by the strength of prohibition evidence.

Fasting beyond Ramadan is a meritorious act, but not all voluntary fasts are equal. The Hanafi school distinguishes between nafl (supererogatory) and makruh (disliked) fasts, with the latter subdivided into tanzih (light) and tahrim (prohibitive). This lesson presents the evidence-based classification from Hashiya al-Tahtawi, including the widely debated connecting of the six days of Shawwal and the rulings on fasting specific days like Friday, Saturday, and Persian festivals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of non-obligatory fasts
Read the passage to extract the two major categories: nafl (supererogatory) and makruh (disliked). Note that makruh is further divided into tanzih and tahrim.
The classification is from Kamal Ibn al-Humam.
2
For each category, locate the proofs
Find the hadith or textual evidence cited for each ruling: e.g., the hadith of Dawud for the best voluntary fast, prohibitions for Eid and Tashriq, and the hadith of Friday and Saturday.
Focus on the dalil al-naqli (textual evidence) presented.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the six days of Shawwal
Examine the conflicting views: al-mukhtar (preferred) to separate them vs. al-Thani al-Hawi who permitted connecting. Note the tarjih mechanism that determines the mufta bihi.
The dispute is resolved by preferring separation to avoid resemblance to the People of the Book.
4
List examples of makruh tanzih and makruh tahrim
From the text, pick out specific fasts: Ashura alone (tanzih), Eid and Tashriq (tahrim). Also note the conditions for Friday, Saturday, and the Persian days.
Observe how the degree of prohibition is tied to the clarity of the evidence.
5
Apply the ruling on a woman's voluntary fast
Read the passage on a woman fasting supererogatorily without husband's consent. Understand the condition: huband's right takes precedence, and he may break her fast with qada required.
This highlights the interplay between voluntary worship and marital obligations.

الأيام إلا أن يكون في صوم يصومه أحدكم رواه مسلم (قوله: (وكره إفراد يوم الجمعة إلا أن يضم إليه يوماً قبله، أو بعده كما في الحديث، واعلم أنه ثبت بالسنة طلب صومه والنهي عنه، والأخير منهما النهي كما وضحه بخصوصها، أما إذا كان اتفاقياً، فلا التعمد لا ينتفي الثواب. قوله: (إلا) أن يكون في صوم أي مع صوم قبله، أو بعده) (و) كره (إفراد يوم السبت) به لقوله : (لا تصوموا يوم السبت إلا قيام افترض عليكم فإن لم يجد أحدكم إلا لحاء عنبة أو عود شجرة فليمضغه رواه أحمد وأصحاب السنن إلا النسائي (قوله: (وكره إفراد يوم السبت) للتشبه باليهود بحر. قوله: (إلا فيما افترض عليكم مثله ما إذا ضم إليه غيره) (و) كره إفراد (يوم النيروز) أصله نوروز لكن ما لم يكن في أوزان العرب فوعول أبدلوا الواو ياء وهو يوم، في طرف الربيع (أو) إفراد يوم (المهرجان) معرب مهر كان وهو يوم في طرف الخريف لأن فيه تعظيم أيام نهينا عن تعظيمها إلا أن يوافق ذلك اليوم (عادته) لفوات علة معتاده (قوله: (الإلحاء عنبة) أي قشر عنبة. قوله: (فليمضغه) بفتح الياء والضاد المعجمة. قوله: (أصله نوروز) ومعناه اليوم الجديد فنو بمعنى الجديد وروز بمعنى اليوم. قوله: (وهو يوم في طرف الربيع) هو اليوم الذي تحل فيه الشمس برج الحمل قوله: (وهو يوم في طرف الخريف) المراد منه أول حلول الشمس في الميزان وهذا اليوم والذي قبله عيدان للفرس. قوله: (إلا أن يوافق ذلك اليوم أي الصادق باليومين قبله واستثنى في عدمة الفتاوى من كراهة صوم النيروز والمهرجان ما إذا صام يوماً قبلهما، فلا يكره كما في يوم الشك، وقيد كراهة صومهما في الدر بما إذا تعمده) وكره صوم الوصال ولو واصل بين يومين فقط للنهي عنه (وهو) أي الوصال أن لا يفطر بعد الغروب أصلاً حتى يتصل صوم الغد بالأمس) (قوله: وكره صوم (الوصال أي لغيره صلى الله عليه وسلم أما هو فلا يكره له) وكره صوم أن وهو يصوم ولا يتكلم بشيء فعليه أن يتكلم بخير وبحاجة دعت إليه (قوله: (ولا يتكلم بشيء) أي معتقداً أن ذلك قرية أما إذا سكت بالعادة فلا كراهة) وكره صوم الدهر) لأنه يضعفه أو يصير طبعاً له ومبنى العبادة على مخالفة العادة ولا تصوم المرأة نفلاً بغير رضا زوجها وله أن يفطرها لقيام حقه واحتياجه (قوله: (ولا تصوم المرأة نقلاً أما الفرض ولو عملاً فلا يتوقف على رضاه لأن تركه معصية، ولا طاعة لمخلوق في معصية الخالق، وفي الدر ولا تصوم المرأة نفلاً إلا بإذن الزوج إلا عند عدم الضرر به، ولو قطرها وجب القضاء بإذنه أو بعد البينونة) والله الموفق.
Meaning: connecting it (the six days of Shawwal) due to the apparent meaning of His statement: 'then follow it' and it was said to separate them, as a manifestation of opposing the People of the Book in imitating them by increasing beyond the obligatory. And among it is every fast whose seeking and promise is established by the noble Sunnah, like the fast of Dawud (peace be upon him), and it is the best of fasts and most beloved to Allah Almighty due to the Prophet's saying: 'The most beloved fast to Allah is the fast of Dawud, and the most beloved prayer to Allah is the prayer of Dawud: he used to sleep half the night, and stand for a third, and sleep a sixth; and he used to break fast one day and fast one day.' Reported by Abu Dawud and others. As for the fifth category, which is supererogatory (nafl), it is what we have explained — any fast for which dislike has not been established from the Lawgiver, nor its specification to a time. As for the sixth category, which is disliked (makruh), it is of two types: disliked as tanzih (abstention) and disliked as tahrim (prohibition). The first, which is disliked as tanzih, includes fasting on Ashura alone without the ninth or eleventh. The second, which is disliked as tahrim, includes fasting the two Eids (al-Fitr and al-Adha) due to turning away from Allah's hospitality and opposing the command. And from it is fasting the days of Tashriq due to the prohibition of fasting them. This classification was mentioned by the investigator Kamal Ibn al-Humam (may Allah have mercy on him), and he explicitly stated the prohibition of fasting the two Eids and the days of Tashriq in al-Burhan. It is disliked to single out Friday for fasting due to his saying: 'Do not single out Friday night for prayer among other nights, and do not single out Friday for fasting among other days, unless it is a fast that one of you is already observing.' Reported by Muslim. It is disliked to single out Saturday for fasting due to his saying: 'Do not fast on Saturday except in what has been made obligatory upon you; if one of you finds nothing but a grape skin or a piece of wood, let him chew it.' Reported by Ahmad and the authors of the Sunan except al-Nasa'i. It is disliked to single out the day of Nawruz (originally Nowruz, but if not in the Arab metric system, they substitute waw with ya) – and it is a day at the beginning of spring – or the day of Mihrajan (Persianized: Mihr Kan), which is a day at the beginning of autumn, because it involves glorifying days which we are forbidden to glorify, unless that day coincides with his habit, due to the loss of the reason for his habit. It is disliked to fast wasal (continuous fasting), even if he connects only two days, due to the prohibition against it. Wasal means not breaking the fast after sunset at all until the next day's fast connects with the previous day. It is disliked to fast in silence, meaning he fasts and does not speak anything; rather he should speak good and what is necessary. It is disliked to fast perpetually (al-dahr) because it weakens him or becomes a habit for him, and the foundation of worship is to oppose habit. A woman should not fast supererogatorily without her husband's consent, and he has the right to break her fast to uphold his right and need. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 640

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of Al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah provides a detailed classification of non-obligatory fasts. It begins by addressing the ruling on connecting the six days of Shawwal to Ramadan or separating them, clarifying that the preferred view (al-mukhtar) is to separate them, though connecting is not disliked – this is contrary to a view from a later Hanafi authority (al-Thani al-Hawi). The author then extols the fast of Dawud (peace be upon him) as the most beloved to Allah, citing a hadith that describes his alternation. Following this, the text defines two categories of supererogatory fasts: nafl (voluntary) and makruh (disliked). Nafl is any fast that has no established dislike or time specification. Makruh is divided into two degrees: makruh tanzihan (lightly disliked) and makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked). Examples of makruh tanzihan include fasting Ashura alone (i.e., on the tenth without the ninth or eleventh). Examples of makruh tahriman include fasting on the two Eids and the days of Tashriq (11th-13th of Dhul Hijjah), for which explicit prohibition is mentioned, citing Kamal Ibn al-Humam's affirmation. Next, the text addresses specific disliked fasts: singling out Friday or Saturday for fasting is disliked because of explicit prophetic prohibitions; however, if one already has a habit of fasting (e.g., on alternate days), it is permissible. Fasting on the Persian festivals of Nawruz (spring equinox) and Mihrajan (autumnal equinox) is disliked due to their association with non-Islamic practices, unless it coincides with a personal habit. The text also prohibits wasal (connecting two days without breaking fast at sunset) and fasting in silence (dhikr is required instead). Perpetual fasting (every day of the year) is disliked as it can harm the body or make fasting a mere habit. Finally, a woman may not fast voluntarily without her husband's permission, as he has a right to intimacy; if she does, he may break her fast, and she must make it up. This ruling excludes obligatory fasts, which take precedence.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory fast for which no dislike is established
المكروه (al-makruh): Disliked act, divided into tanzih (light) and tahrim (prohibitive)
صوم الوصال (sawm al-wisal): Continuous fasting without breaking fast after sunset, connecting two or more days
صوم الدهر (sawm al-dahr): Fasting every day of the year without break

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on fasting on the day of Ashura alone (without the 9th or 11th)?
A) It is haram (forbidden)
B) It is makruh tanzihan (lightly disliked)
C) It is mustahabb (recommended)
D) It is mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies non-obligatory fasts into nafl, makruh tanzih, and makruh tahrim, with clear evidence distinguishing each level.

Introduction to Intention Requirements for Fasting
Begins chapter on intention conditions for fasting, introducing a key division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two intention-related conditions that are not required for some categories of fasts according to the Hanafi chapter heading.

Core Idea
Some fasts waive the need to specify the intention and to intend at night.

This lesson opens a new chapter on the intention (niyyah) for fasting. The author immediately presents a binary division: there are fasts for which two specific conditions are not required, and others for which they are required. Understanding this division is foundational to applying the rules of intention correctly. We will focus on the first category introduced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions in the chapter title
From the title 'Chapter on what does not require tabiyit al-niyyah and ta'yin al-niyyah', extract the two conditions: making the intention at night (tabyit) and specifying the fast (ta'yin).
These are the two key legal terms.
2
Recognise the two categories of fasts
The chapter heading explicitly states that there is a category for which these two conditions are not required, and another category for which they are required. Memorise this binary division.
The first category is mentioned first.
3
Understand the grammatical construction of 'ta'yin al-niyyah'
The footnote clarifies that 'ta'yin al-niyyah' is an idafah (construct phrase) where the verbal noun 'ta'yin' is added to its object 'al-niyyah'. This is similar to 'tabyituha' (making it at night).
This helps in parsing similar legal phrases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما لا يشترط تبييت النية وتعيينها فيه وما يشترط فيه ذلك (أما القسم الذي لا يشترط فيه تعيين النية لما يصومه (ولا تبييتها) أي النية (قوله: (تعيين النية) من إضافة المصدر إلى مفعوله كقوله : ولا تبييتها .)
Chapter on what does not require the intention to be made at night and its specification, and what does require that. As for the category for which specification of the intention for what one is fasting is not required, nor making it at night (i.e., the intention). (His saying: 'specification of the intention' is from the verbal noun's idafah to its object, like his saying: 'making it at night'.)
Source pages p. 641

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of a new chapter in the book of fasting, dealing with the conditions of intention (niyyah). The text introduces a fundamental division: there are fasts for which it is not required to specify the intention (ta'yin) nor to make it at night (tabyit), and there are fasts for which these are required. The footnote clarifies that the term 'ta'yin al-niyyah' is a genitive construction (idafah) where the verbal noun is added to its object, similar to the phrase 'tabyituha' (making it at night). This linguistic note is important for understanding the legal phrasing. The chapter then proceeds to list those fasts, but the text provided is incomplete; it only states the first category. In Hanafi fiqh, the general rule is that for obligatory fasts like Ramadan and qada', the intention must be made at night (before dawn) and the specific fast must be specified. For supererogatory fasts, the intention can be made during the day as long as nothing has been eaten, and the specification is not required (one can intend 'a supererogatory fast' without specifying which day). This chapter will elaborate on these distinctions.

Key Terms
تبييت النية (tabyit al-niyyah): Making the intention for fasting during the night before dawn
تعيين النية (ta'yin al-niyyah): Specifying which fast one intends (e.g., Ramadan, qada', vow)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Specifying the intention and making it at night
B) Fasting at night and daytime
C) Intention and abstinence
D) Pre-dawn meal and breaking fast

Key Takeaway
The chapter establishes a fundamental division of fasts: those that require both specification and nighttime intention, and those that do not.

Disliked Fasts: Nawruz, Mihrajan, Wisal, and Others
Enumeration of disliked acts in fasting with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which fasts are considered makruh tanzihi in the Hanafi school and state the conditions under which the ruling changes (e.g., habit, intention, or necessity).

Core Idea
Fasting on non-Muslim festivals is disliked unless it coincides with a regular habit; other disliked fasts include continuous, silent, and perpetual fasting.

The text from Hashiya al-Tahtawi ala Maraqi al-Falah enumerates several types of fasting that are considered makruh (disliked) in the Hanafi school. These rulings are refined in the commentary, which provides exceptions and conditions. Understanding these nuances helps avoid practices that are discouraged while preserving the validity of the fast.

Guided Path
1
List the disliked fasts
Identify each type of fast mentioned: fasting on Nawruz, Mihrajan, Wisal (continuous), silent fasting, perpetual fasting (sawm al-dahr), and a woman's supererogatory fast without husband's permission.
2
Determine the general ruling
The passage states each is 'kareeha' (disliked). In Hanafi fasting terminology, this is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) unless specified otherwise.
Some are more strongly disliked (e.g., Wisal) but still not haram.
3
Identify exceptions and conditions
Note the exceptions: Nawruz/Mihrajan are not disliked if they coincide with a habitual fast (e.g., Monday/Thursday). The commentary adds that fasting the day before also removes dislike. For Wisal, it is disliked for others but not for the Prophet ﷺ.
Silent fasting is disliked only if intended as worship; if silent out of habit, no dislike.
4
Apply the rulings
Consider a scenario: a woman wants to fast on a day that happens to be Nawruz. She has no habit of fasting on that day. The ruling: makruh tanzihi unless she fasts the day before as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصوم
إلا لحاء عنبة أو عود شجرة فليمضغه رواه أحمد وأصحاب السنن إلا النسائي (و) كره إفراد (يوم النيروز) أصله نوروز لكن ما لم يكن في أوزان العرب فوعول أبدلوا الواو ياء وهو يوم، في طرف الربيع (أو ) إفراد يوم (المهرجان) معرب مهر كان وهو يوم في طرف الخريف لأن فيه تعظيم أيام نهينا عن تعظيمها إلا أن يوافق ذلك اليوم (عادته) لفوات علة معتاده وكره صوم الوصال ولو) واصل بين (يومين فقط للنهي عنه (وهو) أي الوصال أن لا يفطر بعد الغروب أصلاً حتى يتصل صوم الغد بالأمس) وكره صوم أن وهو يصوم ولا يتكلم بشيء فعليه أن يتكلم بخير وبحاجة دعت إليه وكره صوم الدهر) لأنه يضعفه أو يصير طبعاً له ومبنى العبادة على مخالفة العادة ولا تصوم المرأة نفلاً بغير رضا زوجها وله أن يفطرها لقيام حقه واحتياجه، والله الموفق.
(الإلحاء عنبة) أي قشر عنبة. قوله: (فليمضغه) بفتح الياء والضاد المعجمة. قوله: (أصله نوروز) ومعناه اليوم الجديد فنو بمعنى الجديد وروز بمعنى اليوم. قوله : (وهو يوم في طرف الربيع) هو اليوم الذي تحل فيه الشمس برج الحمل قوله : (وهو يوم في طرف الخريف) المراد منه أول حلول الشمس في الميزان وهذا اليوم والذي قبله عيدان للفرس. قوله : (إلا أن يوافق ذلك اليوم أي الصادق باليومين قبله واستثنى في عدمة الفتاوى من كراهة صوم النيروز والمهرجان ما إذا صام يوماً ،قبلهما، فلا يكره كما في يوم الشك | هـ، وقيد كراهة صومهما في الدر بما إذا تعمده قوله : وكره صوم (الوصال أي لغيره صلى الله عليه وسلم أما هو فلا يكره له . قوله: (ولا يتكلم بشيء) أي معتقداً أن ذلك قرية أما إذا سكت بالعادة فلا كراهة قوله : (ولا تصوم المرأة نقلاً أما الفرض ولو عملاً فلا يتوقف على رضاه لأن تركه معصية، ولا طاعة لمخلوق في معصية الخالق، وفي الدر ولا تصوم المرأة نفلاً إلا بإذن الزوج إلا عند عدم الضرر به، ولو قطرها وجب القضاء بإذنه أو بعد البينونة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر
الله العظيم.
Book of Fasting: Except the skin of a grape or a piece of wood from a tree, then he may chew it. Narrated by Ahmad and the authors of the Sunan except al-Nasa'i. And it is disliked to single out the day of Nawruz (originally Nawruz, but if not in the weights of the Arabs, they changed the waw to ya; it is a day at the edge of spring) or to single out the day of Mihrajan (Persianized from Mihr Kan, it is a day at the edge of autumn) because it involves glorifying days which we are forbidden to glorify, unless that day coincides with his habit, due to the absence of the cause of habit. And it is disliked to fast Wisal (continuous fasting), even if he connects only two days, due to the prohibition against it. And it (Wisal) is that he does not break his fast after sunset at all until the fast of the next day connects with yesterday. And it is disliked to fast while remaining silent, not speaking anything; he should speak good and when needed. And it is disliked to fast perpetually, because it weakens him or becomes a habit for him, and the foundation of worship is opposing habit. And a woman should not perform supererogatory fasting without her husband's consent, and he may break her fast to uphold his right and need. And Allah is the Grantor of Success. [Commentary:] (The skin of a grape) meaning the peel of a grape. His saying: (then he may chew it) with fatha on the ya and the emphatic dad. His saying: (its origin is Nawruz) meaning the new day; 'naw' means new and 'ruz' means day. His saying: (it is a day at the edge of spring) it is the day when the sun enters Aries. His saying: (it is a day at the edge of autumn) what is meant is the first entry of the sun into Libra; this day and the previous one are two festivals for the Persians. His saying: (unless that day coincides) i.e., the truthful one with the two days before it; and an exception is made in 'Umdat al-Fatawa from the dislike of fasting Nawruz and Mihrajan if he fasts a day before them, then it is not disliked, as on the day of doubt. And in al-Durr, the dislike of fasting them is restricted to when he intends it intentionally. His saying: (And it is disliked to fast Wisal) i.e., for others besides the Prophet ﷺ; as for him, it is not disliked. His saying: (and does not speak anything) i.e., believing that to be an act of worship; but if he remains silent out of habit, there is no dislike. His saying: (and a woman should not perform supererogatory fasting) as for obligatory fasting, even if it is a make-up, it does not depend on his consent, because abandoning it is disobedience, and no obedience to a creature in disobedience to the Creator. And in al-Durr: a woman should not perform supererogatory fasting except with the husband's permission, unless there is no harm to him; and if he breaks her fast, she must make it up with his permission or after separation. And Allah knows best, and I seek forgiveness of Allah the Great.
Source pages p. 641

Commentary
This passage is a section from Kitab al-Sawm listing various fasts that are makruh (disliked) in the Hanafi school. The author first mentions that it is permissible to chew the skin of a grape or a piece of wood from a tree while fasting, as long as nothing reaches the throat (this is based on a hadith narrated by Ahmad and the Sunan authors). Then it states that it is makruh to single out the Persian festivals Nawruz (spring equinox) and Mihrajan (autumn equinox) for fasting, because these days are glorified by non-Muslims, and we are forbidden to glorify them. However, if these days coincide with one's habit (e.g., one normally fasts every Monday and Thursday), it is not disliked. The commentary clarifies that the ruling of dislike applies only if one intentionally fasts on these days; if one fasts the day before as well, it is not disliked. Next, the passage discusses Wisal (continuous fasting), where one fasts without breaking the fast after sunset, connecting two days. This is makruh for the Ummah, though it was permissible for the Prophet ﷺ alone. Fasting while remaining silent, intending it as worship, is also makruh; one should speak good and when needed. Fasting every day (sawm al-dahr) is makruh because it weakens the body or becomes a habit, whereas worship should oppose habit. Finally, a woman may not perform supererogatory fasts without her husband's permission, and he may break her fast to uphold his marital rights. The commentary adds that if a husband breaks his wife's supererogatory fast, she must make it up later. The overall legal weight of these rulings varies; some are from earlier sources, while the exception for Nawruz and Mihrajan is from later fatawa.

Key Terms
الوصال (al-wisal): Continuous fasting without breaking the fast after sunset, connecting two or more days.
النيروز (al-nayruz): The Persian New Year, occurring at the spring equinox.
المهرجان (al-mihrajan): A Persian festival at the autumn equinox.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition is fasting on Nawruz not disliked?
A) If one intends it as a supererogatory fast.
B) If it coincides with one's habitual fast (e.g., Monday/Thursday).
C) If one is traveling.
D) If one fasts alone without informing others.

Key Takeaway
Fasting on non-Muslim festivals is disliked unless it aligns with a regular habit, and other disliked fasts (Wisal, silent, perpetual, woman without permission) have specific conditions that can remove the dislike.

Intention for Fasting: Which Fasts Allow Daytime Intention?
Classification of fasts regarding intention requirements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify fasts into those that require night intention and specification and apply the intention timing rule for Ramadan and specified vows.

Core Idea
For Ramadan and specified vows, intention before noon suffices; other obligatory fasts require night intention.

Many assume that all fasts require intention at night. The Hanafi school distinguishes: for Ramadan, specified vows, and nafl, the intention can be made during the day before noon if nothing invalidating occurred. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the categories and the rationale behind the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
List the types of fasts mentioned: Ramadan (ada'), specified vows (nadhrmu'ayyan), supererogatory (nafl), and other obligatory (e.g., make-up, unspecified vows).
The passage states that the first three do not require tabayyut and ta'yin.
2
Determine the requirement for each
For Ramadan, specified vows, and nafl: intention can be at night or during the day before noon. For other obligatory fasts: night intention and specification are required.
The text says 'فهو أداء رمضان و أداء النذر المعين... وأداء النفل' - these are valid with intention from night or day before noon.
3
Understand 'nafy kamal'
The hadith 'No fast for one who does not intend from the night' is interpreted as negation of perfection, not validity. Evidence: the Prophet allowed those who had not eaten to start fasting when the crescent was sighted during the day.
This shows intention can be made during the day for Ramadan.
4
Apply the time limit
For Ramadan and specified vows, intention can be made until noon. But if one eats, drinks, or has intercourse after dawn, intention later is invalid. One must intend from the beginning, not from the time of intention.
The condition is that no invalidator occurred after Fajr.
5
Note the superiority of night intention
Though daytime intention is valid, the best is to intend at night. Verbal utterance is sunnah, not required.
The text says 'من الليل وهو الأفضل'.

Section: On what does not require intention to be made at night and specified, and what requires that. He only mentioned what does not require it before what requires it, even though the waw does not indicate order, due to the fewness of its divisions, for its superiority because it includes the performance of Ramadan. And he made the demonstrative name singular considering what was mentioned. His saying: (specification of intention) is from verbal noun added to its object, like his saying: nor its making at night. In it (so it is the performance of Ramadan and the performance of a vow) whose time is specified, like saying: I owe Allah the fast of this Friday. So if he makes the intention in its night or its day before noon, it is valid, and he fulfills his obligation. And the performance of supererogatory fasts, so each of these three is valid with an intention specified and made at night, which is best. The reality of intention is his purpose and determination in his heart to fast tomorrow. And no Muslim is devoid of this on the nights of the month of Ramadan except rarely. And verbal utterance is not a condition. And the negation of the fast of one who does not make intention at night is negation of perfection, so the intention is valid, even during the day before noon, because the condition is the existence of intention in most of the day as a precaution, and by that it exists in the entire day legally due to the majority. And this is specific to fasting, so Hajj and prayer are excluded because they [require intention at the beginning?]. He said: (and the performance of a specified vow) as for making up a specified vow, and it is only in a suspended vow... on a condition intended to be realized, so it requires specification and making at night. His saying: (before noon) meaning, even if a little, because the majority is found accompanying it. His saying: (and he fulfills it) i.e., by his fast. His saying: (and the performance of supererogatory) meaning what is other than obligatory and necessary, general whether sunnah, recommended, or disliked, as in al-Bahr. His saying: (from night) so it is not valid before sunset, nor at it, according to al-Durr. His saying: (his purpose and determination in his heart) i.e., the adult's firm intention in his heart. For if he intends to break his fast the next day if invited, and if not invited he is fasting with this intention, then if he wakes up in Ramadan not intending to fast nor to break, while knowing it is Ramadan, apparently he is not fasting, he becomes [not?]... And whoever eats suhoor with the majority opinion that dawn has not risen, it is fine if the person is not ignorant of that. But if he is one who is ignorant, his way is to stop eating, and it is not permissible to break the fast by guesswork in the apparent narration. And if he wants to rely on the rooster's crow for suhoor, some of our scholars objected, and some said it is fine if he has tested it repeatedly and it appears to hit the time. (Indian). His saying: (and negation of the fast of one who does not make intention at night) i.e., in his saying: No fast for one who does not intend fasting from the night and resolve. His saying: (negation of perfection) is indicated by what is established that when a Bedouin testified before him of sighting the crescent, he told a man: Announce among the people: whoever ate should refrain for the rest of the day, and whoever did not eat should fast. His saying: (even during the day before noon) means from night to this time is the time of intention, so whenever it occurs in a part of this time, the fast is valid for what the author mentioned. And if he intends the fast from the day, he intends that he is fasting from its beginning, so if he intends before noon that he is fasting from the time he intended, not from the beginning of the day, he does not become... It is only permissible before forenoon, if he did not do what invalidates the fast like eating, drinking, and intercourse, even forgetfully; but if that occurs after dawn, it is not permissible. Source pages p. 642

Commentary
This section (fasl) from Kitab al-Sawm discusses the requirements for intention (niyyah) in fasting. The author first classifies fasts into those that do not require intention to be made at night (tabayyut) and specified (ta'yin), and those that do. He states that the performance (ada') of Ramadan fasts and specified vow fasts (nadhrmu'ayyan) do not require specification or night intention; one may intend during the day before noon. Supererogatory (nafl) fasts also fall into this category. However, for a vow that is general or conditional, intention at night is needed. The commentary expands: the best is to intend at night, but if one forgets, intending before noon suffices for Ramadan and specified vows, as long as nothing invalidating the fast occurred after dawn. The reality of intention is a firm resolve in the heart to fast tomorrow. Most Muslims naturally have this on Ramadan nights. Uttering the intention verbally is sunnah, not obligatory. The report that a Bedouin testified of sighting the crescent and the Prophet ordered those who had eaten to abstain and those who had not eaten to start fasting indicates that intention can be made during the day. The commentary also discusses cases like fasting based on the rooster's crow or suhoor before doubt, and notes that for supererogatory fasts, intention can be made until before noon as long as nothing invalidating occurred. The text also touches on the distinction between fasting and prayer/Hajj regarding intention timing. The passage ends abruptly, but the overall ruling is clear: for Ramadan and specified vows, intention can be made before noon of the day, while for other obligatory fasts (like make-up or unspecified vows), night intention is required.

Key Terms
تبييت النية (tabayyut al-niyyah): Making the intention for fasting during the night, before Fajr.
تعيين النية (ta'yin al-niyyah): Specifying which type of fast one intends (e.g., Ramadan, vow, nafl).
نفي كمال (nafy kamal): Negation of perfection, not absolute negation, meaning the fast is valid but lacking completeness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The fast is invalid because intention must be at night.
B) The fast is valid and counts as Ramadan.
C) The fast is valid only if he did not eat or drink after Fajr.
D) The fast is valid but he must make it up later.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits daytime intention before noon for Ramadan, specified vows, and nafl fasts, provided no invalidator occurred after dawn.

Timing and Types of Intention for Fasting
Rules of intention for fasting: timing, types, and rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of intention for fasting and apply it to Ramadan, nadhr mu'ayyan, and nafl fasts.

Core Idea
Daytime intention before half the day suffices for Ramadan, vowed, and nafl fasts, but night intention is best.

The Hanafi school is known for its leniency regarding the timing of intention (niyyah) for fasting. While the ideal is to resolve the intention the night before, this passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains that for the performance of Ramadan, a designated vow, and voluntary fasts, intention made during the day before half the day has passed is also valid. This ruling is based on the unique nature of fasting as a single continuous act of abstention, unlike prayer or Hajj which require intention at the start of each pillar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of fasts discussed
The passage focuses on three types: the performance of Ramadan (ada' Ramadan), a designated vow (nadhr mu'ayyan), and voluntary fast (nafl). Note that qada (make-up) and kaffarah (expiation) are not included and require night intention.
Designated vow means a vow tied to a specific time, e.g., 'I owe Allah fasting on this Friday'.
2
State the general rule on timing
For these three fasts, intention can be made at night (muragba or mubayyatah) – which is best (afdal) – or during the day up to before half the day has passed. The condition is that the intention exists during most of the day (akthar al-nahar).
Half the day is calculated from Fajr until just before the major forenoon (duha kubra), not from sunrise.
3
Understand the proof and rationale
The proof is that the hadith 'No fast for one who does not resolve the intention at night' is interpreted as a negation of perfection, not validity, because the condition can be fulfilled later. The rationale is that fasting has only one continuous pillar (abstention), so the intention, once made, covers the entire act. This differs from prayer and Hajj which have multiple pillars requiring intention at each start.
This is a Hanafi usul principle: the negation in 'la siyama liman lam yubayyit al-siyam' is of completion, not validity, unless proven otherwise.
4
Note the intra-madhhab clarification
The author clarifies that 'half the day' follows al-Jami' al-Saghir (the most correct view), cautioning against al-Quduri's apparent wording that half is from sunrise. The correct calculation is from Fajr to just before duha kubra, because the day linguistically starts at sunrise but legally, for this ruling, Fajr is used.
If intention is made just before zawal (noon), it is too late because it would not cover the majority of the day.
5
Apply the ruling on absolute intention
The passage also states that absolute intention (mutlaq al-niyyah) – intending to fast without specifying – is valid for these determined fasts because the time itself specifies the fast. For example, intending 'I am fasting tomorrow' in Ramadan suffices, even without saying 'Ramadan'. Similarly, intending a voluntary fast covers it, even if one is a traveler who may not be required to fast.
This applies only to mu'ayyan fasts (Ramadan, designated vow). For non-mu'ayyan vows or qada, specific intention is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصوم
فيه (فهو أداء رمضان و أداء النذر) المعين (زمانه كقوله : الله علي صوم يوم هذه الجمعة فإذا أطلق النية ليلته أو نهاره إلى ما قبل نصف النهار صح، وخرج به عن عهدة المندور (و) أداء النفل فيصح كل من هذه الثلاثة (نية) معينة مبيتة (من الليل) وهو الأفضل، وحقيقة النية قصده عازماً بقلبه صوم غد، ولا يخلو مسلم عن هذا في ليالي شهر رمضان إلا ما ندر، وليس النطق باللسان شرطاً ونفي صيام من لم يبيت النية نفي كمال فتصح النية، ولو نهاراً إلى ما قبل نصف النهار لأن الشرط وجود النية في أكثر النهار احتياطاً، وبه توجد في كله حكماً للأكثر وخص هذا بالصوم فخرج الحج والصلاة لأنهما أركان فيشترط قرانها بالعقد على أدائها ابتداء وإلا خلا بعض الأركان عنها فلم يقع عبادة والصوم ركن واحد وقد وجدت فيه، وإنما قلنا إلى ما قبل نصف النهار تبعاً للجامع الصغير (على الأصح) احتراز عن ظاهر عبارة القدوري وإنما قال ونصف النهار من) ابتداء (طلوع الفجر إلى قبيل وقت الضحوة الكبرى لا عندها لأن النهار قد يطلق على ما عند طلوع الشمس إلى غروبها لغة وعند الزوال نصفه فيفوت شرط صحة النية بوجودها قبيل الزوال (ويصح أيضاً) كل من أداء رمضان والنذر المعين والنفل (بمطلق النية) من غير تقييد بوصف للمعيارية، والنذر معتبر بإيجاب الله تعالى ( وبنية النفل) أيضاً ولو كان) الذي نواه (مسافراً
Book of Fasting. In it: (So it is performance of Ramadan and performance of the designated vow) whose time is specified, like saying: 'I owe Allah fasting on this Friday.' So if he releases the intention at night or during the day until before half the day, it is valid, and he thereby fulfills his pledge. (And) performance of voluntary fast. So each of these three is valid with a specific intention resolved from the night, and that is best. The reality of intention is his determination with resolve in his heart to fast tomorrow. And no Muslim is free from this on the nights of Ramadan except rarely. And verbal utterance is not a condition. And the negation of fasting of one who did not resolve the intention at night is a negation of perfection, so intention is valid even during the day until before half the day, because the condition is the existence of intention in most of the day as a precaution. And by that it exists in the whole day legally due to the majority. And this is specific to fasting, so Hajj and prayer are excluded because they have multiple pillars, so their intention must accompany the contract at the beginning, otherwise some pillars would be devoid of it and would not be an act of worship. And fasting has one pillar, and it is found in it. And we only said 'until before half the day' following al-Jami' al-Saghir (according to the most correct view), as a precaution against the apparent wording of al-Quduri. And he said: half of the day from the beginning of Fajr until just before the time of the major forenoon, not at it, because the day may be linguistically applied to what is from sunrise to sunset, and at zawal is its half, so the condition for validity of intention would be missed if it occurs just before zawal. (And also valid) each of the performance of Ramadan, designated vow, and voluntary fast (with absolute intention) without restriction by a description, due to the determinate nature [of these fasts]; and the vow is considered by the obligation of Allah (and with intention of voluntary fast) also, even if the one intending it is a traveler.
Source pages p. 642

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi explains the rulings of intention (niyyah) for fasting. The author first states that three types of fasts—the performance of Ramadan, a designated vow (nadhr mu'ayyan), and voluntary (nafl)—are valid with a specific intention that is resolved at night (mubayyatah). However, it is also valid to make the intention during the day up to before half the day has passed, for these three types. The reality of intention is a firm resolve in the heart to fast tomorrow; verbal utterance is not a condition. The negation in the hadith 'No fast for one who does not resolve at night' is interpreted as negation of perfection, not validity, because intention can be made later. The condition for validity is that the intention is present during the majority of the day (akthar al-nahar). This is a precaution to ensure the intention covers most of the day. This leniency is specific to fasting because fasting consists of a single continuous act (abstention), unlike prayer and Hajj which have multiple pillars requiring intention at the start of each act. The passage then clarifies that 'half the day' is calculated from Fajr until just before the major forenoon (duha kubra), not from sunrise. If intention is made just before zawal, it is too late because it would not be in the majority of the day. Finally, the author states that for Ramadan and designated vows, absolute intention (mutlaq niyyah) without specifying the fast is valid because these fasts are determined (mu'ayyan) by their time. Similarly, intending a voluntary fast suffices for them, even if the person is a traveler (who may have the option to not fast).

Key Terms
نية مبيتة (niyyah mubayyatah): Intention resolved from the night before Fajr, for a fast.
مطلق النية (mutlaq al-niyyah): Absolute intention without specifying the type or reason of fast, e.g., intending to fast in general.
أكثر النهار (akthar al-nahar): The greater part of the day; the condition that intention must exist during this majority for daytime intention to be valid.
نفي كمال (nafy al-kamal): Negation of perfection, not absolute negation of validity. Used to interpret the hadith 'No fast...'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which of the following fasts is it valid to make intention after Fajr but before half the day according to the Hanafi school?
A) Making up a missed Ramadan fast (qada)
B) A voluntary fast (nafl)
C) An expiatory fast (kaffarah)
D) A contingent vow (nadhr mu'allaq)

Key Takeaway
Daytime intention before half the day is valid for Ramadan, designated vows, and voluntary fasts, but night intention is superior; this leniency is unique to fasting due to its single continuous pillar.

Intending Another Wajib Fast During Ramadan: Categories and Ikhtilaf
Explains the ruling on intending a different obligatory fast while fasting in Ramadan for resident, traveler, sick, and one under a vow.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each category (resident, traveler, sick, one with a specified vow) when a different wajib fast is intended during Ramadan and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf for the traveler and sick.

Core Idea
Ramadan is the criterion for the resident but not for the traveler; intention can divert a wajib fast within Ramadan only when the person has a license to break it.

When a person fasts in Ramadan but intends another obligatory fast, does the fast count as Ramadan or as the intended one? This question arises in different scenarios: a healthy resident, a traveler, a sick person, and one under a vow. The Hanafi school has nuanced answers, with significant internal differences between Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and later scholars. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying the rules of intention (niyyah) in fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories of persons
List the four types: healthy resident (muqim sahih), traveler (musafir), sick (marid), and one with a specified vow (manthur mu'ayyan zamanuhu). Each has a different ruling.
The categories are based on the presence or absence of a license to break the fast.
2
State the ruling for each category according to the most sound view
For the resident: his fast counts as Ramadan even if he intended another wajib. For the traveler: according to Abu Hanifa, it counts as the intended wajib; according to the Sahibayn, as Ramadan. For the sick: the most sound view is that it counts as Ramadan. For the one under a vow: if he intends another wajib, it does not fulfill the vow; the vow remains due. If he intends nafilah, it fulfills the vow.
The mi'yar (criterion) of Ramadan applies only to the resident, not to those with a license.
3
Analyse the ikhtilaf for the traveler
Abu Hanifa argues that because the traveler has a license to not fast, he can divert the fast to another obligation. The Sahibayn say that the time of Ramadan is fixed, so any fast in it counts as Ramadan unless nafilah is intended. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view (one narration).
The disagreement is based on whether the license affects the nature of the time.
4
Analyse the ikhtilaf for the sick
Hasan ibn Ziyad and the author of al-Hidayah prefer that the sick person's fast falls as the intended wajib, due to estimated incapacity (similar to traveler). Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'immah maintain it falls as Ramadan, which is the most sound (al-ashah).
The sick person's license is based on estimated hardship, not actual action, which makes it weaker than the traveler's license.
5
Apply the principle to the one under a vow
A specified vow is like Ramadan in that it requires specific intention. If one intends another wajib, it does not discharge the vow. If one intends nafilah or makes an absolute intention, it does discharge the vow, per the majority. There is a narration from Abu Hanifa that it falls as what he intended (nafilah/vow).
The key is that intention matters more for the vow because it is a personal obligation tied to a specific time.

أو) كان مريضاً في الأصح من الروايتين وهو اختيار فخر الإسلام وشمس الأئمة وجمع وتلغى زيادة النفلية لأنهما لما تحملا المشقة التحقا بمن لا عذر له نظراً لهما (ويصح أداء رمضان بنية واجب (آخر) هذا المن كان صحيحاً مقيماً لما أنه معيار فيصاب بالخطأ في الوصف كمطلق النية بخلاف) المسافر فإنه إذا نوى واجباً آخر (يقع عما نواه من ذلك (الواجب) رواية واحدة عن أبي حنيفة لأنه صرفه إلى ما عليه وقالا : يقع عن رمضان واختلف الترجيح في صوم المريض إذا نوى واجباً آخر بصومه (في) شهر (رمضان) روى الحسن أنه عما نوى واختاره صاحب الهداية وأكثر مشايخ بخارى لعجزه المقدر وقال فخر الإسلام وشمس الأئمة: الصحيح أنه يقع صومه عن رمضان وفي البرهان وهو الأصح (ولا يصح) أي لا يسقط المنذور المعين زمانه بصومه (بنية واجب غيره بل يقع عما نواه الناذر (من الواجب المغاير للمنذور في الروايات كلها ويبقى المنذور بذمته ويقضيه وقيدنا بواجب آخر لأنه لو نوى نفلاً وقع عن المنذور المعين كإطلاق النية وروي عن أبي حنيفة أنه يكون عما نواه (فيه) أي الزمن المعين
Or) he was sick, in the most sound of the two narrations, and it is the choice of Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'immah and [some] gathered. And the increase of nafilah is invalidated because when they both undertook hardship, they joined one who has no excuse, out of consideration for them. (And it is valid to perform Ramadan with the intention of (another) wajib, this one being healthy and resident, because it is a criterion, so it may be mistaken in the description like absolute intention, contrary to) the traveler, for if he intends another wajib, (it falls as what he intended of that (wajib) in one narration from Abu Hanifah, because he diverted [the fast] to what is upon him. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it falls as Ramadan. And the tarjih differed regarding the fasting of the sick person if he intends another wajib with his fast (in) the month (of Ramadan). Al-Hasan narrated that it is what he intended, and the author of al-Hidayah and most of the scholars of Bukhara chose it due to his estimated incapacity. Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'immah said: the correct is that his fast falls as Ramadan, and in al-Burhan it is the most sound. (And it is not valid) i.e., the vowed (nadhr) whose time is specified is not discharged by his fast (with the intention of another wajib; rather it falls as what the one under vow intended (of the wajib different from the vowed) in all narrations, and the vowed remains in his liability and he must make it up. And we restricted it to another wajib because if he intended nafilah, it would fall as the specified vowed like absolute intention. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifah that it is what he intended (therein) i.e., the specified time.
Source pages p. 644

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on intending an obligatory fast other than Ramadan while fasting in Ramadan. It is a hashia (super-commentary) clarifying positions from the Hanafi school. The commentary begins by addressing the case of a sick person: there are two narrations, with the most sound being that the fast falls as Ramadan, as chosen by Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'immah. The rationale is that if we made it nafilah, they would have to make up the Ramadan fast, causing hardship. Then it addresses a healthy resident: his fast is valid as Ramadan even if he intended a different wajib, because Ramadan is the criterion; his intention may be mistaken but the fast counts as Ramadan. For the traveler, according to one narration from Abu Hanifa, his fast falls as the wajib he intended, because he diverted the fast to an obligation upon him. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it falls as Ramadan. Regarding the sick person, there is a split: some prefer the view that it falls as what he intended due to his estimated incapacity, while others hold it is Ramadan (the more correct view). Finally, for one who has a vowed fast with a specified time (nadhr mu'ayyan), if he intends another wajib, it does not satisfy the vow; rather the fast counts as that other wajib, and the vow remains in his liability. However, if he intended nafilah, it would satisfy the vow, like an absolute intention. There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa that it falls as what he intended (i.e., the nafilah or other). This section highlights the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on these issues.

Key Terms
معيار (mi'yar): Criterion: Ramadan is the standard by which intentions are measured; if one intends another wajib, the fast still counts as Ramadan because the time is defined by the Shari'ah.
منذور معين زمانه (manthur mu'ayyan zamanuhu): A vow with a specified time, i.e., a nadhr that is tied to a particular day or period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most sound view in the Hanafi school, if a sick person (who is not excused from fasting) intends another wajib fast while fasting in Ramadan, what does his fast count as?
A) The other wajib he intended
B) Ramadan
C) Nafilah
D) The sick person's fast is invalid

Key Takeaway
Ramadan is a criterion that overrides intention for the resident, but for the traveler and sick, the school's internal ikhtilaf means the mufta bihi differs: Abu Hanifa's view is followed for the traveler, while the more correct view for the sick is that it counts as Ramadan.

Fasting Requiring Specified and Night Intention
Critical refinement on intention conditions and internal dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fasts that require ta‘yīn and tabyīt, apply the conditions of intention, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding combined intention.

Core Idea
A fast requiring specification and night intention is not fulfilled by a combined intention; it becomes nafl.

This passage from the Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies which fasts demand a specified intention made at night. It also delves into a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens if one intends both qaḍā’ and kaffārah together? Understanding these conditions ensures our fasts correctly discharge our obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify fasts requiring ta‘yīn and tabyīt
List the categories of fasts mentioned: qaḍā’ of Ramadan, qaḍā’ of invalidated fasts, expiatory fasts (kaffārāt), tamattu‘, qirān, and absolute vows.
These fasts have no fixed time; hence they require specification.
2
Understand continuity and revocation
The intention must be continuous from night until dawn. Revoking it at night nullifies the fast; breaking the fast after revocation requires only qaḍā’, no kaffārah.
Renewal is possible before ḍuḥā al-kubrā.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abū Ḥanīfa holds that intending both qaḍā’ and kaffārah together results in neither; the fast becomes nafl. Abū Yūsuf holds it counts as qaḍā’.
The muftā bihī position follows Abū Ḥanīfa.
4
Apply the rulings to scenarios
Given a situation, determine whether the intention is valid, which fast is performed, and whether obligations are fulfilled.
Consider also the effect of saying 'in shā’ Allāh'.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(وتبييتها) فلو نوى تلك الصيامات نهاراً كان تطوعاً، وإتمامه مستحب، ولا قضاء بإفطاره، والتبييت في الأصل كل فعل دبر ليلاً قهستاني قوله : (وصوم التمتع والقرآن) بالرفع . عطفاً قوله : قضاء رمضان، وذلك لأنّ الصوم بدل عن الدم الواجب فيهما، وهو دم شكر للتوفيق لإداء النسكين قوله : ( ووجد) أي الشرط. قوله : (أو مطلق) أي عن التعليق. قوله: (لأنها ليس لها وقت معين أي وإنما اشترط التعيين والتبييت فيها لأنّ تلك الصيامات ليس لها وقت معين لأن الواجب ثابت في الذمة، وكل زمان صالح لإدائه، وللنفل فلم يقع عما في ذمته إلا بالتعيين، وليس وقتها معياراً لها فاشترط فيه التبييت . قوله: (فلم تتأدي) المناسب حذف الألف للجازم. قوله: (وهو الأصل) أي المقارنة . الأصل في النية وإنما ذكر باعتبار الخبر. قوله: (للضرورة) لأن تحري وقت الفجر مما يشق والحرج مدفوع قوله : (فلو رجع عما نوى ليلاً لم يصر صائماً قال في الهندية : ولو قوله: (إلا أن يعود إلى تجديد النية استثناء من قوله : لانقطاع النية بالرجوع أي، فإذا جددها قوله : ( ويحصل مضيه فيه أي في الصوم بنيته في وقتها أي النية بعد الفجر إلى قبيل الضحوة الكبرى، وقوله: تجديداً شربه أو جماعة بعدها كذا في حاشية السيد عن هي صح صومه.
As for the second category, which requires specification of intention and its making at night in order to be performed and to discharge the obligation for the responsible person: it is the make-up of Ramadan, the make-up of what he invalidated by sexual intercourse, and the fasts of expiations of all types, such as the expiation of an oath, the fast of tamattu' and qiran, and the absolute vow without restriction of time, which is either conditional upon a condition that occurs, like his saying: 'If Allah cures my sick person, then I owe a day of fasting,' and the cure occurs, or absolute, like his saying: 'I owe Allah a day of fasting,' because these have no specific time, so they are not performed except with a specific intention made at night, or concurrent with the break of dawn, which is the original, and it is presented [before dawn] due to necessity. Continuity of intention is required; if he revokes what he intended at night, he does not become a faster, and if he breaks the fast, nothing is due from him except make-up, due to the interruption of intention by revocation, so there is no expiation upon him in Ramadan unless he returns to renewing the intention, and its continuation occurs in it at its time as a renewal of it. The intention is not invalidated by his saying: 'I will fast tomorrow if Allah wills' because it is in the sense of seeking assistance and asking for success, unless he intends the real exception. Upon his saying: 'And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that it becomes what he intended,' i.e., from supererogatory. His saying: 'And it is what requires specification of intention' is based on the condition of specification that if he intended both expiation and make-up together, he would not be commencing either, and it becomes supererogatory, and Abu Yusuf said: he becomes a make-up faster as in Sukk al-Anhur. His saying: 'and its making at night'—if he intended those fasts during the day, it would be supererogatory, and completing it is recommended, and no make-up is required for breaking it. At-tabyit originally means every action done at the end of the night, as in Qahistani. His saying: 'and the fast of tamattu' and qiran' is in the nominative as an appositive to his saying: 'make-up of Ramadan,' because the fast is a substitute for the blood sacrifice obligatory in both, which is a blood of thanks for the success of performing the two rites. His saying: 'and it occurs' i.e., the condition. His saying: 'or absolute' i.e., without conditioning. His saying: 'because they have no specific time'—he means that specification and making at night are required because those fasts have no specific time, because the obligation is established in the liability, and every time is suitable for its performance, and for supererogatory, it does not fall upon what is in his liability except with specification, and its time is not a measure for it, so making at night is required. His saying: 'it does not become performed'—the appropriate is to drop the alif for the jussive. His saying: 'and it is the original' i.e., concurrence with dawn. The original in intention is mentioned in consideration of the hadith. His saying: 'due to necessity' because ascertaining the time of dawn is difficult, and hardship is repelled. His saying: 'so if he revokes what he intended at night, he does not become a faster'—it is stated in al-Hindiyya: 'If he intended from the night and then revoked his intention before the break of dawn, his revocation is valid in all fasts.' His saying: 'and if he breaks the fast' i.e., in fulfilling Ramadan after his revocation of the intention to fast at night. His saying: 'so no expiation is due from him in Ramadan' due to the doubt of disagreement of those who require making at night. His saying: 'unless he returns to renewing the intention' is an exception from his saying: 'due to the interruption of intention by revocation' i.e., when he renews it. His saying: 'and its continuation occurs in it' i.e., in the fast by his intention at its time, i.e., the intention after dawn until before the great forenoon, and his saying: 'as a renewal of it' i.e., of the intention, i.e., a realization of it because the first is not considered due to the revocation of it. His saying: 'and the intention is not invalidated by his saying: 'I will fast tomorrow if Allah wills' because intention is an act of the heart, and it is not invalidated by eating, drinking, or intercourse at night after it, as in the hashiya of al-Sayyid from... his fast is valid.
Source pages p. 645

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya) on the second type of fasting requiring intention (niy·yah). The author specifies that qaḍā’ of Ramaḍān, expiatory fasts (kaffārāt), tamattu‘ and qirān fasts, and absolute nadhr fasts all require: (1) specification (ta‘yīn) of what one is fasting, and (2) making the intention at night (tabyīt). If one intends these during the day, the fast becomes nafl (supererogatory). A key intra-Ḥanafī dispute is mentioned: If one intends both qaḍā’ and kaffārah together, Abū Ḥanīfa holds that neither is performed—it becomes nafl—while Abū Yūsuf holds that it counts as qaḍā’. The text also clarifies that revoking intention at night nullifies the fast entirely, and no kaffārah is due due to the doubt (shubhah) of those who require tabyīt. Saying 'in shā’ Allāh' does not affect the intention unless one really intends a conditional suspension.

Key Terms
تعين النية (ta‘yīn al-niyyah): Specification of intention—clearly identifying which fast one intends (e.g., qaḍā’ of Ramaḍān, not just any fast).
تبييت النية (tabyīt al-niyyah): Making intention at night—from after sunset until the break of dawn. For obligatory fasts, it must be done during this time.
القضاء (al-qaḍā’): Make-up fast—performing a fast to compensate for a missed or invalidated obligatory fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if someone at night intends to fast both qaḍā’ of Ramaḍān and an expiatory fast (kaffārāt) together for the next day, what is the Ḥanafī ruling according to Abū Ḥanīfa?
A) The fast counts as qaḍā’.
B) The fast counts as kaffārāh.
C) The fast becomes supererogatory (nafl) and does not fulfill either obligation.
D) The fast is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Fasts that are debts on the liability (qaḍā’, kaffārāt, nadhr) require a specified intention made at night; combining two obligations in one intention fails to fulfill either and results in a supererogatory fast.

Establishing the Crescent of Ramadan
Ruling on establishing the crescent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on establishing the crescent of Ramadan, identify the primary dalil, and apply the rule when the crescent is obscured.

Core Idea
Ramadan is established only by sighting the crescent; if obscured, complete 30 days of Sha‘ban.

The Hanafi school, like all Sunni schools, relies on actual sighting of the crescent to confirm the start of Ramadan. This passage presents the foundational hadith and the derived ruling, emphasizing that seeking the crescent is a collective obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal classification of seeking the crescent: the text states it is wajib (fard kifayah) because it is a means to fulfill the obligation of Ramadan.
The obligation is collective (kifayah), meaning if some fulfill it, others are absolved.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the Prophet's hadith: 'Fast upon seeing it and break your fast upon seeing it; if it is hidden from you, then complete the count of Sha‘ban as thirty.' This hadith is mutawatir in meaning.
The hadith is found in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'صوموا' indicates obligation, and the conditional clause 'فإن غم عليكم' provides the exception when sighting is impossible, requiring completion of the 30-day count.
In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub (the command indicates obligation).
4
Note the consensus
The text indicates that this ruling is by consensus: if the crescent is obscured by cloud, dust, or any other obstruction, the month is completed as 30 days.
This consensus (ijma) reinforces the binding nature of the ruling.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الحديث فإن غم عليكم الخ. قوله : (وغيره) كظلمة مانعة، أو ضوء كذلك أو دخان قوله: (هو ما يلي التاسع والعشرين قال في الهندية هو إذا لم ير علامة ليلة الثلاثين، والسماء متغيمة، أو شهد واحد فردت شهادته أو شاهدان فاسقان فردت شهادتهما ا هـ، وفي شرح المختار أن يتحدث الناس بالرؤية ولا تثبت وظاهر التقييد بأنه ما يلي التاسع والعشرين أنه لا يكره صوم التاسع من ذي الحجة عند الشك في أنه يوم نحر، والظاهر الكراهة ويحرر. قوله: (وقد استوى فيه الخ) بيان لوجه إضافة اليوم إلى الشك قوله : (بحقيقة الحال) متعلق بالجهل، وحذف من العلم نظيره أو متعلق بالعلم وحذف من الجهل نظيره. قوله : (بأن غم الهلال الباء للسببية. قوله : (فاحتمل) بالبناء للمجهول أي احتمل الحال. قوله: (وخنس إبهامه لم يبين أنه إبهام اليمني أو اليسرى قوله : (وقوله بالجر عطفاً على قوله الأول قال ابن حجر وثواب الناقص كالكامل في الفضل المترتب على رمضان أما ما يترتب على صوم يوم الثلاثين من ثواب واجبه أي ،فرضه ومندوبه عند سحوره، وفطوره فهو زيادة يفوق بها الناقص
Section on what establishes the crescent and on fasting on the day of doubt and other matters. It is a collective obligation to seek the crescent on the night of the 30th of Sha‘bān, because it may be a deficient day. And Ramadan is established by sighting its crescent, due to his saying: 'Fast upon seeing it and break your fast upon seeing it, and if it is hidden from you, then complete the count of Sha‘bān as thirty.' So he said: 'or after completing Sha‘bān thirty days, if the crescent is obscured by cloud, dust, or other [obstructions],' by consensus. And the day of doubt is that which follows the 29th of Sha‘bān; in it, both knowledge and ignorance are equal regarding the true reality of the situation because the crescent (i.e., the crescent of Ramadan) is obscured, so the case is probable that Sha‘bān is complete or incomplete, considering his saying: 'The month is like this, like this, like this'—and he tucked his thumb in the third time, meaning twenty-nine, and his saying 'like this, like this' without tucking means thirty. So doubt exists. The 'mark' is 'miskīn' (a poor person?), and the explanation indicates that the will [of Allah] does not entirely annul it even if he intended its reality, but according to the author's words, there is a way, which is that if he intended conditional suspension, he was not resolute in intention, and that is apparent. And Allah knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah Almighty. Section: What establishes the crescent, i.e., the crescent of Ramadan and other. His saying: 'and other' like fasting two days at the end of the month. His saying: 'it is obligatory'—apparently it is an obligation because it leads to the obligatory; likewise, it is obligatory to seek the crescent of Shawwāl at sunset on the 29th of Ramadān. His saying: 'seeking the crescent' i.e., seeking its sighting. It is stated in the Sharḥ: 'It is disliked to point at the crescent when seeing it because it is an act of ignorance.' This indicates that there is no consideration given to the sayings of astrologers, so the crescent is not established by that. His saying: 'for it is hidden from you' i.e., concealed from you. His saying: 'so that' i.e., because of his saying in the hadith: 'and if it is hidden from you...' etc. His saying: 'and other' like a preventing darkness, or light like that, or smoke. His saying: 'it is what follows the 29th'—it is stated in al-Hindiyya: 'It is when no sign [of the crescent] is seen on the night of the 30th, and the sky is cloudy, or one witness whose testimony is rejected, or two immoral witnesses whose testimony is rejected.' End quote. And in Sharḥ al-Mukhtār: 'People talk about sighting but it is not established.' The apparent restriction that it is what follows the 29th indicates that fasting on the 9th of Dhū al-Ḥijja (the day of ‘Arafa) is not disliked when there is doubt that it is the day of sacrifice [‘Īd al-Aḍḥā], but the apparent ruling is dislike, and it requires verification. His saying: 'and equality has occurred in it' etc.—an explanation of why the day is attributed to doubt. His saying: 'regarding the true reality' is related to ignorance, and the analogous term is omitted from knowledge, or else related to knowledge and the analogous term is omitted from ignorance. His saying: 'because the crescent is obscured'—the bā' is for causation. His saying: 'so it is probable' in the passive voice, i.e., the situation is probable. His saying: 'and he tucked his thumb'—it is not specified whether it is the right or left thumb. His saying: 'and his saying' in the genitive, as a conjunct to his first saying. Ibn Ḥajar said: 'The reward of the incomplete day is like the complete in the virtue attached to Ramadān; as for what is attached to fasting the 30th day in reward of its obligation, i.e., its obligatory and recommended at its suḥūr and ifṭār, it is an increase by which the incomplete day surpasses.'
Source pages p. 645

Commentary
This section (faṣl) from the ḥāshiya explains how the new moon of Ramaḍān is established and the ruling on the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk). It begins by stating that seeking the crescent on the 29th of Sha‘bān (the night of the 30th) is a collective obligation (farḍ kifāyah) because it may reveal that the month is incomplete (29 days). The primary proof is the authentic hadith: 'Fast upon seeing it and break your fast upon seeing it; if it is obscured (ghumma), then complete the number of Sha‘bān as thirty.' This hadith is the basis for the rule that Ramaḍān is confirmed only by actual sighting of the crescent, not by astronomical calculations. If the sky is cloudy, dusty, or otherwise obscured, one must complete 30 days of Sha‘bān before commencing Ramaḍān. The day of doubt is defined as the 30th of Sha‘bān when the crescent is not seen due to obscurity; knowledge and ignorance are equal as to whether it is the 29th or 30th. The commentary also discusses that pointing at the crescent is disliked (makrūh) as it was a practice of pre-Islamic ignorance, and that the statements of astrologers are of no consequence. The passage ends with a note from Ibn Ḥajar comparing the reward of fasting 29 vs 30 days of Ramaḍān.

Key Terms
الهلال (al-hilāl): The new moon crescent that marks the beginning of a lunar month, especially Ramaḍān and Shawwāl.
يوم الشك (yawm al-shakk): The 30th of Sha‘bān (or 30th of Ramaḍān for Eid) when the crescent is not seen, making it doubtful whether the month has ended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on seeking the crescent on the night of the 30th of Sha‘ban?
A) It is sunnah muakkadah.
B) It is fard kifayah.
C) It is fard ayn.
D) It is mubah.

Key Takeaway
Ramadan is established only by sighting the crescent; if obscured, complete 30 days of Sha‘ban.

The Day of Doubt: Definition and Ruling
Definition and ruling of the day of doubt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the day of doubt, identify its causes, and state the Hanafi ruling on fasting that day.

Core Idea
The day of doubt is the 30th of Sha‘ban when the crescent is obscured; fasting it with the intention of Ramadan is disliked.

When the crescent is not seen on the 29th, the following day becomes uncertain. This passage defines the day of doubt and discusses the legal considerations for fasting on it.

Guided Path
1
Define the day of doubt
It is the 30th day of Sha‘ban when the crescent is not seen due to obscurity, making it equally probable that Sha‘ban is 29 or 30 days.
The text specifies obscurity by cloud, dust, smoke, or rejection of testimony.
2
Identify the ruling on fasting
Fasting the day of doubt with the specific intention of Ramadan is makruh tanzihi (disliked).
However, fasting a general fast or making up a missed fast is permissible.
3
Note the evidence
The hadith 'do not fast before Ramadan' and the principle that one should not anticipate the month without certainty.
The text also cites the prophetic gesture of tucking the thumb to indicate 29 days.

Confirmation of Crescent and Day of Doubt Rulings
Legal rulings on crescent confirmation and fasting on day of doubt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on confirming the Ramadan crescent by sighting and explain when fasting on the day of doubt is makruh or permissible.

Core Idea
Ramadan is confirmed by sighting or completing 30 Sha'ban; the day of doubt fast is makruh except when firmly intended as supererogatory.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies how the beginning of Ramadan is established—by sighting the crescent or completing thirty days—and the crucial ruling on fasting during the day of doubt. It demonstrates the legal reasoning (istidlal) from the hadith 'Fast by its sighting' and shows the refined application of this proof to nuanced scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation of seeking the crescent
Recognize that seeking the crescent on the night of the 30th of Sha'ban is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) because it is a means to determine the start of Ramadan.
The text uses 'يجب' (obligatory) and explains it leads to a fard.
2
Define the day of doubt
The day of doubt (yawm al-shakk) is the 30th of Sha'ban when the crescent is obscured, making it uncertain whether it is the last day of Sha'ban or the first of Ramadan.
It arises when sighting is impossible due to clouds, dust, etc.
3
Derive the ruling from the hadith
The hadith 'صوموا لرؤيته وأفطروا لرؤيته فإن غم عليكم فأكملوا عدة شعبان ثلاثين' establishes that fasting begins only upon confirmed sighting or completion of thirty days.
The imperative 'صوموا' indicates obligation, but the condition shows that without sighting, completion of 30 days is required.
4
Apply the ruling to the day of doubt
Because the day of doubt may be from Ramadan, fasting it without confirmation is disliked (makruh), as it resembles anticipating Ramadan. However, exceptions exist for a firmly intended supererogatory fast or a habitual fast.
The text distinguishes between a hesitant intention (which is makruh) and a firm intention for a supererogatory fast (which is not disliked).
5
Note the difference of opinion on preference
There is a difference among scholars on whether it is better to fast or break fast on the day of doubt for the elite. The fatwa is that the elite may fast with firm intention, while others should break after noon.
This shows the principle of precaution and avoiding common confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصوم
فصل فيما يثبت به الهلال وفي صوم الشك وغيره) يجب كفاية التماس الهلال ليلة الثلاثين من شعبان لأنه قد يكون يوم ناقصاً و(يثبت رمضان برؤية هلاله لقوله : (صوموا لرؤيته وأفطروا لرؤيته فإن غم عليكم فأكملوا عدة شعبان ثلاثين فلذا قال أو بعد شعبان ثلاثين يوماً (إن غم الهلال) بغيم وغبار وغيره بالإجماع (ويوم ما الشك هو يلي التاسع والعشرين من شعبان وقد استوى فيه طرف العلم والجهل بحقيقة الحال بأن غم (الهلال) أي هلال رمضان فاحتمل كمال شعبان ونقصانه نظراً إلى قوله : الشهر هكذا وهكذا وهكذا وخنس إبهامه في المرة الثالثة يعني علة تسعة وعشرين وقوله وهكذا وهكذا أي من غير خنس يعني ثلاثين، فالشك بوجود العلامة مسكين والتعليل يفيد أن المشيئة لا تبطل مطلقاً ولو قصد حقيقته لكن لكلام المؤلف أنه وجه، وهو إذا قصد التعليق كان غير جازم بالنية، وهو ظاهر والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
فصل: فيما يثبت به الهلال أي هلال رمضان وغيره قوله: (وغيره) كصوم يومين من آخر الشهر. قوله: (يجب) الظاهر منه الافتراض لأنه يتوصل به إلى الفرض، وكذا يجب التماس هلال شوال في غروب التاسع والعشرين من رمضان قوله التماس الهلال أي طلب رؤيته قال في الشرح وتكره الإشارة إلى الهلال عند رؤيته لأنه فعل الجاهلية وفي هذا إشارة إلى أنه لا عبرة بقول المنجمين فلا يثبت به الهلال قوله فإن فم (عليكم أي أخفي عليكم. قوله: (فلذا) أي لقوله في الحديث فإن غم عليكم الخ. قوله : (وغيره) كظلمة مانعة، أو ضوء كذلك أو دخان قوله: (هو ما يلي التاسع والعشرين قال في الهندية هو إذا لم ير علامة ليلة الثلاثين، والسماء متغيمة، أو شهد واحد فردت شهادته أو شاهدان فاسقان فردت شهادتهما ا هـ، وفي شرح المختار أن يتحدث الناس بالرؤية ولا تثبت وظاهر التقييد بأنه ما يلي التاسع والعشرين أنه لا يكره صوم التاسع من ذي الحجة عند الشك في أنه يوم نحر، والظاهر الكراهة ويحرر. قوله: (وقد استوى فيه الخ) بيان لوجه إضافة اليوم إلى الشك قوله : (بحقيقة الحال) متعلق بالجهل، وحذف من العلم نظيره أو متعلق بالعلم وحذف من الجهل نظيره. قوله : (بأن غم الهلال الباء للسببية. قوله : (فاحتمل) بالبناء للمجهول أي احتمل الحال. قوله: (وخنس إبهامه لم يبين أنه إبهام اليمني أو اليسرى قوله : (وقوله بالجر عطفاً على قوله الأول قال ابن حجر وثواب الناقص كالكامل في الفضل المترتب على رمضان أما ما يترتب على صوم يوم الثلاثين من ثواب واجبه أي ،فرضه ومندوبه عند سحوره، وفطوره فهو زيادة يفوق بها الناقص
