كتاب الصوم كغيم في الثلاثين أمن رمضان هو أو من شعبان أو نعم من رجب (وكره فيه) أي يوم الشك (كل صوم) من فرض وواجب وصوم ردد فيه بين نقل وواجب إلا صوم نفل جزم به بلا ترديد بينه وبين صوم (آخر) فإنه لا يكره لحديث السرار إذا كان على وجه لا يعلم العوام ذلك ليعتادوا صومه ظناً منهم زيادته على الفرض، وإذا وافق معتاده فصومه أفضل اتفاقاً واختلفوا في الأفضل إذا لم يوافق معتاده قيل : الأفضل الفطر احترازاً لظاهر النهي وقيل: الصوم اقتداء بعلي وعائشة رضي الله عنهما فإنهما كانا يصومانه (وإن ظهر أنه) (رمضان) • من فلرمضان فضل من حيث هو بقطع النظر عن مجموع أيامه كمغفرة الذنوب لمن صامه إيماناً، واحتساباً، والدخول من باب الجنة المعد لصائمه، وغير ذلك من التكريم، وهذا لا فرق فيه بين كونه ناقصاً، أو تاماً، وأما الثوبا المترتب على كل يوم بخصوصه فأمر آخر قد يثبت للكامل ما لا يثبت للناقص، ونظم العارف بالله تعالى الأجهوري أشهر الصوم التامة، والناقصة في حياته صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فقال : بسببه وفرض الصيام ثــانــي الــهــجـرة فصام تســعــة نــبــي الــرحــمــة فأربعا تسعاً وعشــريــن يــومــاً زاد على ذا بالكمال ما كذا لبعضهم، وقال الـهـيـتـمـي ما صام كاملا سوی شهرا ولـــــلـــــدمــــيــــري أنه شهران وناقص ســـــاه خــذ بــــيــــانــــي اهـ من شرح السيد ملخصاً. قوله : (أو يغم من رجب الضمير في يغم يعود إلى شعبان أي أو يغم هلال شعبان من رجب فأكملت عدته ، فإذا لم ير هلال رمضان يقع الشك في الثلاثين من شعبان أهو الثلاثون فيكون رجب ،كاملاً، أو الحادي والثلاثون فيكون رجب ناقصاً، واليوم الآتي أول رمضان قوله : (الحديث السرار) فإنه يدل على استحباب صوم آخر شعبان، وهو قوله لرجل: هل صمت من سرار شعبان قال : لا قال: فإذا أفطرت فصم يوماً مكانه»، وفيه أن محله في آخر شعبان المحقق، ويوم الشك يحتمل أنه من رمضان. قوله : (إذا كان على وجه الخ) شرط في قوله لا يكره قوله : (ذلك) أي الصوم. قوله : (ليعتادوا) علة للمنفي، وهو قوله : يعلم أي فإنهم إذا عملوا اعتادوا، ولو قال لئلا يعتادوا الخ أي إنما شرطنا ذلك لئلا يعتاد، والكان أوضح قوله : ظناً منهم علة لقوله ليعتادوا قوله : (زيادته) أي صوم يوم الشك . قوله : (الظاهر النهي) هو قوله : «لا تتقدموا رمضان بصوم يوم أو يومين إلا أن يوافق صوماً كان يصومه أحدكم، وفي الشرح الكبير عن ظاهر النهي، وهو الأولى قوله: (وقيل: الصوم الخ) هو الذي جزم به المصنف فيدل على أنه صحيح، والكلام الآتي يدل على أنه أفضل في حق الخواص فقط، وفي عبارة التنوير وشرحه وإلا يصومه الخواص، ويفطر غيرهم بعد الزوال به يفتى نفياً لتهمة النهي ا هـ فأفاد الخلاف في أفضلية صومه للخواص قال
The Book of Fasting. Chapter: On what establishes the crescent, and on fasting on the day of doubt and other matters. It is a communal obligation to seek the crescent on the night of the thirtieth of Sha'ban because it might be an incomplete day. Ramadan is established by sighting its crescent due to his saying: 'Fast by its sighting and break your fast by its sighting; if it is obscured for you, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days.' Therefore he said: 'or after Sha'ban thirty days if the crescent is obscured' by clouds, dust, or other [obstructions] by consensus. The day of doubt is the day following the twenty-ninth of Sha'ban, in which knowledge and ignorance of the actual state are equal, because the crescent (i.e., the crescent of Ramadan) was obscured, so the possibility of Sha'ban being complete or incomplete arises, considering his saying: 'The month is like this, like this, like this' and he tucked his thumb in the third occurrence, meaning it is twenty-nine; and his saying 'like this, like this' meaning without tucking, i.e., thirty. So doubt arises with the existence of a sign [of the crescent]. The reasoning indicates that intention does not invalidate absolutely, even if one intended its reality, but according to the author's statement, it is a [possible] interpretation; when one intends a conditional [intention], it is not a firm intention. That is apparent. And Allah knows best. I seek forgiveness from Allah, the Magnificent. Chapter: On what establishes the crescent, i.e., the crescent of Ramadan and others. His saying: 'and others' such as fasting two days from the end of the month. His saying: 'it is obligatory' apparently means obligatory (fard) because it leads to an obligatory act. Similarly, seeking the crescent of Shawwal at sunset on the twenty-ninth of Ramadan is obligatory. His saying: 'seeking the crescent' means seeking its sighting. It is stated in the commentary: 'It is disliked to point at the crescent upon seeing it because it is an act of the Jahiliyyah.' In this is an indication that the statements of astrologers are not considered, so the crescent is not established by them. His saying: 'if it is obscured for you' i.e., hidden from you. His saying: 'therefore' i.e., due to his saying in the hadith: 'if it is obscured for you' etc. His saying: 'and other [obstructions]' such as an obstructing darkness, or light like that, or smoke. His saying: 'it is what follows the twenty-ninth' It is stated in al-Hindiyyah: 'It is when the crescent is not seen on the night of the thirtieth, the sky is overcast, or a single witness testifies and his testimony is rejected, or two immoral witnesses testify and their testimony is rejected.' In Sharh al-Mukhtar: 'that people speak of sighting but it is not established.' The apparent restriction to what follows the twenty-ninth indicates that it is not disliked to fast the ninth of Dhu al-Hijjah when in doubt whether it is the day of sacrifice. The apparent view is that it is disliked, and it requires scrutiny. His saying: 'and knowledge and ignorance of the actual state are equal' is an explanation of why the day is attributed to doubt. His saying: 'by the actual state' is related to ignorance, and its counterpart is deleted from knowledge; or it is related to knowledge and its counterpart is deleted from ignorance. His saying: 'because the crescent was obscured' the ba' is for causality. His saying: 'so the possibility arises' in the passive voice, i.e., the situation becomes possible. His saying: 'and he tucked his thumb' it does not clarify whether it is the right or left thumb. His saying: 'and his saying' in the genitive case, coordinated with his first saying. Ibn Hajar said: 'The reward of an incomplete [month] is like that of a complete one regarding the virtue attached to Ramadan. As for the reward attached to fasting the thirtieth day, including obligatory and commendable acts at its suhur and iftar, it is an increase by which the incomplete excels.' / Page 647: The Book of Fasting. ... like clouds on the thirtieth, whether it is from Ramadan or from Sha'ban or indeed from Rajab. 'And it is disliked on it' i.e., the day of doubt 'every fast' whether obligatory, supererogatory, or a fast with hesitation between supererogatory and obligatory, except a supererogatory fast firmly intended without hesitation between it and another fast. That is not disliked because of the hadith of al-Sirar, if it is done in a manner that the common people do not know, so that they might become accustomed to fasting it, thinking it is additional to the obligation. If it coincides with one's habit, fasting it is better by agreement. They differed over which is better if it does not coincide with habit. Some said: 'The better is to break fast, as a precaution against the apparent prohibition.' Others said: 'Fasting [is better], following the example of 'Ali and 'A'ishah, may Allah be pleased with them, for they used to fast it.' And if it becomes apparent that it is Ramadan, then Ramadan has virtue in itself, irrespective of the total number of its days, such as forgiveness of sins for one who fasts it with faith and seeking reward, entering through the gate of Paradise prepared for its faster, and other honours. There is no difference in this between it being incomplete or complete. As for the reward attached to each specific day, that is another matter; it may be that the complete month has what the incomplete does not. The gnostic al-Ajhuri composed: 'The fasting of Ramadan was ordained in the second year of the Hijra. The Prophet of mercy fasted nine [Ramadans] — four complete and twenty-nine days; he added to that by completion...' etc. Some said like that. Al-Haytami said: 'He did not fast any complete month except one.' Al-Dumayri said: 'Two months [were complete].' Take my explanation... from the commentary of al-Sayyid summarized. His saying: 'or it is obscured from Rajab' the pronoun in 'is obscured' refers to Sha'ban, meaning: 'or the crescent of Sha'ban is obscured from Rajab, so I completed its count.' If the crescent of Ramadan is not seen, doubt arises on the thirtieth of Sha'ban: is it the thirtieth, so Rajab was complete, or the thirty-first, so Rajab was incomplete, and the coming day is the first of Ramadan? His saying: 'the hadith of al-Sirar' indicates the recommendation of fasting the end of Sha'ban, as he said to a man: 'Did you fast from the end of Sha'ban?' He said: 'No.' He said: 'Then if you break your fast, fast one day in its place.' It indicates that its place is in the confirmed end of Sha'ban, while the day of doubt may possibly be from Ramadan. His saying: 'if it is done in a manner' is a condition for 'it is not disliked'. His saying: 'that' i.e., the fast. His saying: 'so that they might become accustomed' is a cause for the negated [action], i.e., his saying 'they do not know'—meaning if they do it, they become accustomed. If he said 'lest they become accustomed', that would be clearer. His saying: 'thinking' is a cause for 'so that they might become accustomed'. His saying: 'the apparent prohibition' is his saying: 'Do not anticipate Ramadan by fasting a day or two, unless it coincides with a fast that one of you habitually observes.' In al-Sharh al-Kabir, the apparent prohibition is the preferred view. His saying: 'and some said: fasting [is better]' is what the author affirmed, indicating its validity. The following discussion indicates that it is better only for the elite. In the expression of al-Tanwir and its commentary: 'Otherwise the elite fast it, and others break fast after midday; this is the fatwa, to negate the suspicion of [violating] the prohibition.' This shows the difference on its superiority for the elite.
Source pages p. 646

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, dealing with the rulings on confirming the crescent of Ramadan and fasting on the day of doubt. The commentary begins by explaining the obligation of seeking the crescent on the night of the thirtieth of Sha'ban, which is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) because it is a means to establish the obligation of Ramadan fasting. The primary proof is the hadith: 'Fast by its sighting and break your fast by its sighting; if it is obscured for you, complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days.' The day of doubt (yawm al-shakk) is defined as the day following the twenty-ninth of Sha'ban when the crescent of Ramadan was obscured, leaving equal possibility that it is the thirtieth of Sha'ban or the first of Ramadan. The comment clarifies that the crescent is confirmed only by sighting, not by astronomical calculations. The ruling on fasting on the day of doubt is that all types of fast are disliked (makruh), including obligatory and supererogatory fasts, except a firmly-intended supererogatory fast without hesitation. This is based on the hadith of al-Sirar and the principle of avoiding anticipation of Ramadan. There is a difference of opinion: some say breaking fast is better to avoid the prohibition, others say fasting is better following the Companions. The fatwa is that the elite may fast, but others should break after noon. The passage also discusses the virtue of Ramadan and the reward of complete vs. incomplete months, and includes a poetic summary of the number of complete Ramadans the Prophet fasted.

Key Terms
هلال (hilal): The new crescent moon that marks the beginning of a lunar month, particularly for Ramadan and Shawwal.
يوم الشك (yawm al-shakk): The day following the 29th of Sha'ban when the crescent is obscured, creating doubt whether it is the 30th of Sha'ban or 1st of Ramadan.
التماس الهلال (iltimas al-hilal): Actively seeking to sight the crescent moon on the night of the 30th of Sha'ban or 29th of Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on fasting on the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk) for a person who has no habitual fast to maintain?
A) It is obligatory to fast.
B) It is permissible and recommended.
C) It is disliked (makruh) in general, except if one firmly intends a supererogatory fast.
D) It is completely forbidden (haram).

Key Takeaway
The day of doubt fast is generally disliked, but permissible with a firm intention for a supererogatory fast.

Rulings on Fasting the Day of Doubt
Explains the disliked fasting on the day of doubt and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each type of fasting on the day of doubt and identify which fasts are disliked and which are exempt, supported by the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Fasting on the day of doubt is disliked except for a firmly intended voluntary fast.

This passage from Maraqi al-Falah, with al-Tahtawi’s hashya, clarifies the nuanced Hanafi position on fasting when the new moon is not sighted. It distinguishes between obligatory, voluntary, and hesitant intentions, balancing the hadith prohibition with the practice of the Companions. Understanding this ruling prevents common errors in Ramadan preparation.

Guided Path
1
Define the day of doubt and its legal context
Identify yawm al-shakk as the 30th of Sha'ban when the moon is not sighted. Understand it is a day of uncertainty between Sha'ban and Ramadan.
The text assumes the moon is not seen due to cloud cover.
2
State the general rule of dislike
Recognize that the matn declares all forms of fasting on this day as disliked (makruh) except one exception.
The dislike is tanzihiyyah (not haram).
3
Identify the exception: firmly intended nafl
A supererogatory fast that is firmly intended without hesitation or condition is not disliked, based on the hadith of al-sirar (end of Sha'ban).
The condition is that the common folk should not know this to avoid confusion.
4
Analyze the effect of habitual fasting and ikhtilaf
If the day coincides with one's custom, all agree fasting is better. If not, there is a difference: some prefer not to fast (out of caution) and others follow 'Ali and 'A'isha who fasted.
The relied-upon position is that fasting is better for the elite (khawass).
5
Understand the consequence if it becomes clear it is Ramadan
For a resident, any fast on the day of doubt suffices for Ramadan regardless of intention, except if the person was a traveler intending another wajib.
This shows the legal flexibility in fulfilling the obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصوم كغيم في الثلاثين أمن رمضان هو أو من شعبان أو نعم من رجب (وكره فيه) أي يوم الشك (كل صوم) من فرض وواجب وصوم ردد فيه بين نقل وواجب إلا صوم نفل جزم به بلا ترديد بينه وبين صوم (آخر) فإنه لا يكره لحديث السرار إذا كان على وجه لا يعلم العوام ذلك ليعتادوا صومه ظناً منهم زيادته على الفرض، وإذا وافق معتاده فصومه أفضل اتفاقاً واختلفوا في الأفضل إذا لم يوافق معتاده قيل : الأفضل الفطر احترازاً لظاهر النهي وقيل: الصوم اقتداء بعلي وعائشة رضي الله عنهما فإنهما كانا يصومانه (وإن ظهر أنه) (رمضان أجزأ عنه أي عن رمضان (ما) صامه) بأي نية كانت إلا أن يكون مسافراً ونواه عن واجب آخر كما تقدم وإن ظهر من شعبان، ونواه نفلاً كان غير مضمون لدخول الإسقاط في عزيمته من وجه وكراهة الواجب لصورة النهي كصلاته في أرض الغير وهو دون كراهته على أنه من رمضان لعدم التشبه، وأما كراهة النفل مع الترديد فلأنه ناو للفرض من وجه وهو أن يقول : من رمضان فعنه وإلا فتطوع ( وإن ردد) الشخص (فيه) أي في يوم الشك (بين)
The Book of Fasting: It is said: If the sky is cloudy on the thirtieth [night], whether it is Ramadan or Sha'ban or even Rajab, (and it is disliked) on it, i.e., the day of doubt, (every fast) of obligatory and required fasts and a fast in which one hesitates between supererogatory and required, except for a supererogatory fast firmly intended without hesitation between it and another fast, for it is not disliked due to the hadith of al-sirar, if it is done in a way that the common people do not know that, so that they may become accustomed to fasting it, thinking it to be an addition to the obligatory fast. And if it coincides with his custom, his fast is better by agreement; and they differed about what is better if it does not coincide with his custom: some said that breaking the fast is better, out of caution due to the apparent prohibition; and some said [that] fasting [is better], following 'Ali and 'A'isha, may Allah be pleased with them, for they used to fast it. (And if it becomes manifest that it is) Ramadan, it suffices for him, i.e., for Ramadan, (what he fasted) with any intention whatsoever, unless he was a traveler and intended another obligatory fast, as has preceded; and if it becomes manifest [that it is] from Sha'ban and he intended it as supererogatory, it is not guaranteed [for compensation] because of the inclusion of discharge in his resolution in one sense; and the dislike of the obligatory fast due to the form of the prohibition is like his prayer on land belonging to others, and it is less than its dislike as being from Ramadan due to lack of resemblance. As for the dislike of supererogatory fasting with hesitation, it is because he intends the obligatory in one sense, and that is when he says: 'If it is from Ramadan, then for it; otherwise, a supererogatory fast.' (And if a person hesitates) on it, i.e., on the day of doubt, between...
Source pages p. 647

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on fasting concerning the ‘day of doubt’ (yawm al-shakk) — the 30th day of Sha'ban when the new moon of Ramadan is not sighted due to cloud cover. The text begins by stating that all types of fasting on this day are disliked (makruh): obligatory (fard), required (wajib), and even a fast where one hesitates between supererogatory and required. The only exception is a supererogatory (nafl) fast that is firmly intended without any hesitation — such as one making a definite intention to fast as a voluntary act, not conditional on whether it is Ramadan. This exception is based on a hadith about the end of Sha'ban (al-sirar), which encourages fasting the last days of Sha'ban without associating it with Ramadan. The condition that common people should not know this wisdom is to prevent them from habitually fasting on the day of doubt thinking it adds to Ramadan. If the day of doubt coincides with one's customary fast (e.g., fasting Mondays or Thursdays), all agree it is better to fast. However, if it does not coincide, there is a difference: some say it is better not to fast due to the apparent prohibition in hadith ('Do not anticipate Ramadan by fasting a day or two'), while others say fasting is better, following the practice of 'Ali and 'A'isha. The text then discusses the legal consequence if the day of doubt turns out to be Ramadan: for a resident, the fast counts as the obligatory Ramadan fast regardless of intention, unless he was a traveler intending a different obligatory fast. If it turns out to be Sha'ban and he intended nafl, it is valid as a voluntary fast and no qada is required, because his intention included the possibility of being scooled from obligation. The dislike of an obligatory fast on the day of doubt is compared to praying on someone else's land without permission — it is disliked due to the form of the prohibition, but less severe than fasting with the assumption that it is Ramadan. Finally, the passage clarifies that if one hesitates between intention for Ramadan and nafl, the fast is still disliked.

Key Terms
يوم الشك (yawm al-shakk): The 30th day of Sha'ban when the new moon of Ramadan is not sighted; it is doubted whether it is the last day of Sha'ban or the first of Ramadan.
السرار (al-sirar): The last part of the lunar month, particularly the last days of Sha'ban. The hadith 'Fast the end of Sha'ban' refers to these days.
صوم نفل جزم به (sawm nafil jazama bihi): A supererogatory fast that one firmly intends without any condition or hesitation about it being Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk), which type of fast is NOT disliked according to the Hanafi school?
A) An obligatory fast (fard)
B) A required fast (wajib)
C) A supererogatory fast firmly intended (nafl muhkam)
D) A fast with hesitation between nafl and wajib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows a firmly intended voluntary fast on the day of doubt while discouraging other types.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate

Ruling on Fasting the Day of Doubt (Yawm al-Shakk)
Explains rulings for fasting the day of doubt with various intentions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fasting the day of doubt, distinguish between the types of intention, and apply the ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Fasting the day of doubt suffices for Ramadan if it becomes Ramadan, but hesitation invalidates the fast.

The day of doubt (yawm al-shakk) is the 30th of Sha'ban when it is unclear whether it is actually Ramadan. The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance on the validity and dislike of fasting on this day depending on one's intention. This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies the rulings and addresses common misunderstandings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Fasting on the day of doubt. First, note the general principle: it suffices for Ramadan if it becomes Ramadan, with any intention except for a traveler intending a different obligatory fast.
The ruling is nuanced: it is not simply forbidden or allowed; it depends on intention.
2
Distinguish between intentions
Differentiate between fasting with the intention of Ramadan, nafl, or with hesitation (taraddad). Each has a different ruling on validity and dislike.
Key: hesitation invalidates the fast entirely.
3
Analyze the dislike (karaha)
The dislike is tanzihi (preventive), not tahrimi (prohibitive). It arises from resemblance to the People of the Book, not from the act itself.
The hadith 'whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim' is deemed unauthentic.
4
Apply to scenarios
Practice applying the rule: if a person says 'if this is Ramadan then I am fasting, otherwise I am not,' they are not considered fasting at all.
Conditional intention breaks the necessary resolve ('azima).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصوم أجزأ عنه أي عن رمضان (ما) صامه) بأي نية كانت إلا أن يكون مسافراً ونواه عن واجب آخر كما تقدم وإن ظهر من شعبان، ونواه نفلاً كان غير مضمون لدخول الإسقاط في عزيمته من وجه وكراهة الواجب لصورة النهي كصلاته في أرض الغير وهو دون كراهته على أنه من رمضان لعدم التشبه، وأما كراهة النفل مع الترديد فلأنه ناو للفرض من وجه وهو أن يقول : من رمضان فعنه وإلا فتطوع ( وإن ردد) الشخص (فيه) أي في يوم الشك (بين إن كان غداً. كلام فظهر المصنف أنه من صوم يوم من الشك فقد عصى هذا ابا في شرح السيد: ومنه أي من قوله إلا صوم نفل المقتضى عدم الكراهة يعلم أن ما استفيد من ماً يعتاده أم لا وسواء الشك نفلاً لا يكره مطلقاً سواء وافق صوم صامه بانفراده أم لا بأن ضم إليه غيره وسواء كان ما ضمه إليه يوماً واحداً أم لا بأن كان يومين فأكثر مسلم لا غبار عليه ولا ينافيه ما يأتي من قوله وكره صوم يوم أو يومين من آخر شعبان لأنه مقيد بما إذا كان التقدم على قصد أن يكون من رمضان ا هـ . قوله: (إلا أن يكون مسافراً) هو مذهب الإمام كما سبق. قوله : (لدخول الإسقاط في عزيمته) أي في نية صومه من وجه، وهو ما إذا ظهر أنه من رمضان فإنه يجزى عنه فكأنه لم يشرع ملتزماً، بل مسقطاً الوجه فلا قضاء عليه لو أفسده قوله : ( وكراهة الواجب الخ) الأولى ما فعله في الشرح حيث قال : أما كراهة صومه على أنه من رمضان فلقوله من صام يوم القاسم، وفيه تشبه بأهل الكتاب في زيادة مدة الصوم فإن ظهرت رمضانيته أجزأه، وإن أفطره من شعبان لم يقضه كالمظنون لشروعه مسقطاً، وأما كراهة الواجب الخ، والفرق بين ظهر الجمعة الذي يصلي بنية الشك في صحة الجمعة حيث ينوي فيه الفرض، وبين صوم الشك حيث لا ينوي فيه الفرض أن نية التعيين في الصلاة لازمة لكون وقتها ظرفاً يسعها، وغيرها بخلاف الصوم فظهر الجمعة لا يصح، ولو في وقتها إلا أن نواه على التعيين بخلاف وقت الصوم فإنه معيار لا يسع غيره ره سيد عن الحموي، وهذا إنما يرد على مذهب أبي يوسف لا على المعتمد بقي أن ما ذكره المصنف من حديث من صام يوما الشك فقد عصى أبا القاسم لا أصل له كما قاله الزيلعي قوله : (الصورة النهي) أي المنهي عنه يعني صورة الواجب كصورة الفرض للقرب بينهما فلذاكره، ولو ظهرت رمضانيته في هذه الصورة أجزأه لو مقيماً، ولو مسافراً فعن الواجب عند الإمام، ولو ظهر من شعبان فعما نوى في الصحيح قوله : (كصلاته في أرض الغير فإن الكراهة هنا للعارض المجاور، وهو الشرح . ملك الغير بلا رضاه كما كره الواجب للعارض وهو تصوره بصورة المنهي عنه. قوله: (لعدم التشبه أي بأهل الكتاب في الزيادة على مقدار الصوم بقي ما لو ردد بين واجب، ونفل ومكروه تنزيهاً ولو تردد بين فرض وواجب كره فإن ظهر أنه من شعبان لم يجز عن الواجب لأن الجهة لم تثبت للتردد فيها، وأصل النية لا يكفيه، ويكون فرضاً غير مضمون بالقضاء إذا كان غير رمضان لشروعه فيه مسقطاً. قوله : (لا يكون صائماً كما أنه ليس بصائم لو نوى إنه إن لم يجد غداء فصائم، وإلا فمفطر تنوير قوله : (والمراد به التقديم الخ) فيه تأمل إذ ليس ذلك بلازم لأن العلة المعقولة توهم الزيادة، ولو من بعض الناس، وهذه تتحقق بتقديم الصوم، ولو على أنه من شعبان، ومعنى الحديث لا تصوموا قبل رمضان الخ ومما يدل على ما ذكرنا قوله : لا تقدموا الشهر أي شهر الصيام المفروض بغيره، وكذا ذكر في التحفة، ونصها الصوم قبل رمضان يومين مكروه أي صوم كان، وما ذكره المحبي أخذه في الفوائد وأفاده في العناية، ومثله في الإيضاح، ونصه لا بأس بصوم يوم، أو يومين، أو ثلاثة قبل رمضان لما روي أنه كان يصل شعبان برمضان، والمراد بقوله : لا لا تقدموا الحديث استقبال الشهر بصوم في الدراية قال الكمال وما في التحفة أوجه فالحاصل أنه إذا صام يومين، أو يوماً هل يكره منه ؟ أو ومثله من بعضهم كصاحب التحفة قال بالكراهة مطلقاً، وبعضهم وهو الأكثر قيد بما إذا نوى أن ذلك رمضان، وما عليه الأكثر هو الذي ذكره في الهداية قوله : (لأن التقديم بالشيء على الشيء أن ينوي الخ) فيه نظر ظاهر فإن تقدم الشيء على الشيء لا يلزم فيه ما ذكره، وأجيب بأن الشيء أعيد معرفة فيكون عيناً والتقديم هنا إنما هو لوصف الفرض قوله : (لا يكره صوم ما فوقهما) وقال الإمام الشافعي: إذا انتصف شعبان، فلا صيام إلا رمضان لحديث ورد فيه، وأوردن التقديم بنية صوم الفرض لا يخص اليومين بل الحكم الكراهة فيما زاد حيث نوى الفرض، وأجيب بأنهم خصوا الكراهة باليوم واليومين لدفع توهم أن القليل عفو كما عفي في كثير من الأحكام أي فيفهم حكم الكثير بالأولى، وبأنه لما كان يقع النقص في الشهور، فيتوهم متوهم وقوع النقص في رجب، وفي شعبان معاً فيصوم يومين قبل الرؤية بناء منه على هذا التوهم من غير تحقيق تأمل، وراجع الشرح قوله : أن يأمر المفتي) إنما كان الأمر المفتي لا القاضي لأنّ الصوم لا يدخل تحت القضاء إلا تبعاً أي يأمر القاضي على أنه إفتاء لا حكم قوله : (بإظهار النداء الباء فيه كالباء في كتبت بالقلم، ويظهر النداء في الأسواق والمنارات كما في الشرح.
Book of Fasting. It suffices for Ramadan that (which one fasts) with any intention, unless he is a traveler and intends another obligatory fast as previously mentioned, and if it appears from Sha'ban and he intended it as nafl, it is not guaranteed because of the inclusion of expiation in his determination in one respect, and the dislike of the obligatory due to the form of prohibition like his prayer in another's land, and it is less than the dislike of it as being from Ramadan due to lack of resemblance. As for the dislike of nafl with hesitation, it is because he intends the obligatory in one respect, and that is to say: if from Ramadan then it is for it, otherwise voluntary. (And if) a person (hesitates in it) i.e. in the day of doubt (between whether it is tomorrow). Speech then the author appeared that he from fasting the day of doubt has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim. In the commentary of al-Sayyid: From it i.e. from his saying 'except a nafl fast' which necessitates no dislike, it is known that what is derived from what he is accustomed to or not, and whether the doubt is nafl is not disliked absolutely, whether it coincides with a fast he fasts alone or not by joining another, and whether what he joined is one day or more like two days, it is sound with no objection, and does not contradict what will come of his saying 'and disliked fasting a day or two from the end of Sha'ban' because it is restricted to when the anticipation is intended to be from Ramadan. End. His saying: (unless he is a traveler) is the madhhab of the Imam as before. His saying: (because of the inclusion of expiation in his determination) i.e. in his intention of fasting in one respect, and that is if it appears that it is from Ramadan, then it suffices for him, as if he did not begin as committed but rather as expiating, so there is no makeup upon him if he invalidates it. His saying: (and the dislike of the obligatory etc.) the first is what he did in the sharh where he said: As for the dislike of his fasting as being from Ramadan, it is due to his saying 'whoever fasts the day of al-Qasim', and in it is resemblance to the People of the Book in increasing the duration of fasting. If its Ramadan-ness appears, it suffices him, and if he breaks it from Sha'ban, he does not make it up like the presumptive because he began as expiating. As for the dislike of the obligatory etc., and the difference between the noon of Friday which he prays with intention of doubt in the validity of Friday where he intends the obligatory, and between the fast of doubt where he does not intend the obligatory, is that the intention of specification in prayer is necessary because its time is a container that accommodates it and others, unlike fasting, so the noon of Friday is not valid even in its time unless he intends it specifically, unlike the time of fasting because it is a measure that does not accommodate others. (rah) al-Sayyid from al-Hamawi. This only counters the madhhab of Abu Yusuf, not the relied upon. Remain that what the author mentioned of the hadith 'whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim' has no basis as al-Zayla'i said. His saying: (the form of prohibition) i.e. the forbidden thing, meaning the form of the obligatory like the form of the obligatory for the closeness between them, so for that reason he disliked it. And if Ramadan-ness appears in this form, it suffices him if a resident, and if a traveler, then from the obligatory according to the Imam, and if it appears from Sha'ban, then from what he intended in the correct view. His saying: (like his prayer in another's land) the dislike here is for the adjacent accident, and it is the sharh. Ownership of another without his consent, just as the obligatory is disliked for the accident which is its taking the form of the forbidden. His saying: (due to lack of resemblance) i.e. to the People of the Book in increasing beyond the measure of fasting. Remain what if he hesitated between obligatory and nafl and makruh tanzihan, and if he hesitated between fard and wajib, it is disliked. Then if it appears that it is from Sha'ban, it does not suffice for the obligatory because the aspect is not established due to hesitation in it, and the basic intention is not sufficient, and it becomes a fard not guaranteed by makeup if it is other than Ramadan because he began it as expiating. His saying: (he is not fasting) just as he is not fasting if he intends 'if I find supper then I am fasting, otherwise I am breaking' (Tanwir). His saying: (and what is meant by anticipation etc.) in it is reflection since that is not necessary because the rational cause suggests increase, even from some people, and this is realized by anticipating the fast even if as from Sha'ban, and the meaning of the hadith 'do not fast before Ramadan' etc. And among what indicates what we mentioned is his saying: 'do not anticipate the month' i.e. the month of obligatory fasting by other than it, and likewise mentioned in al-Tuhfa, and its text: fasting before Ramadan by two days is disliked, whatever fast it is. And what al-Muhibbi mentioned he took from al-Fawa'id and benefited from al-Inaya, and similarly in al-Idah, and its text: there is no harm in fasting a day or two or three before Ramadan because it is narrated that he used to connect Sha'ban with Ramadan. And what is meant by his saying: 'do not anticipate' the hadith is receiving the month by fasting. In al-Diraya, al-Kamal said: and what is in al-Tuhfa is preferred. So the conclusion is that if he fasts two days or one day, is it disliked from him? And similarly some like the author of al-Tuhfa said it is disliked absolutely, and others, which is the majority, restricted it to if he intended that to be Ramadan, and what the majority is upon is what he mentioned in al-Hidaya. His saying: (because anticipation of something is that one intends etc.) in it is apparent consideration, for the precedence of something over something does not necessarily require what he mentioned, and it was answered that the thing is repeated as a definite noun so it becomes a specific entity, and anticipation here is only for the attribute of the obligatory. His saying: (there is no dislike for fasting above two days) and Imam al-Shafi'i said: when half of Sha'ban passes, there is no fasting except Ramadan due to a hadith reported. And we mentioned that anticipation with the intention of obligatory fast is not specific to two days, rather the ruling of dislike applies to more where one intends the obligatory, and it was answered that they specified the dislike to one or two days to repel the assumption that the small amount is excused as excused in many rulings, i.e. so the ruling for more is understood a fortiori. And because when deficiency occurs in the months, someone might imagine deficiency in Rajab and Sha'ban together, so he fasts two days before sighting based on this assumption without investigation. Reflect. And refer to the sharh. His saying: (that the mufti should order) the command is only for the mufti, not the qadi, because fasting is not subject to qada except indirectly, i.e. the qadi orders as ifta' not as a ruling. His saying: (with announcement) the ba' in it is like the ba' in 'I wrote with a pen', and the announcement is made in markets and minarets as in the sharh.
Source pages p. 648

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi addresses two closely related rulings concerning fasting in Sha'ban. The first ruling deals with fasting on the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk)—the 30th of Sha'ban when it is uncertain whether it is actually Ramadan. The second ruling concerns fasting during the last days of Sha'ban in anticipation of Ramadan. The commentary opens by affirming that if a person fasts on the day of doubt and it later turns out to be Ramadan, that fast suffices for Ramadan regardless of the original intention, except in the case of a traveler who intended a different obligatory fast. If the person intended a nafl (supererogatory) fast, it is not considered a guaranteed (ghayr madmun) fast because it has the quality of being a substitute (isqat) should it become Ramadan. The dislike (karaha) of fasting with an obligatory intention on the day of doubt is explained through analogy with praying in another's land without permission—the act is valid but disliked due to an external circumstance (resemblance to the People of the Book's practice of lengthening the fast). The hadith 'Whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim' is cited but noted by al-Zayla'i to have no authentic basis. The commentary then discusses the ruling if one hesitates (taraddad) between intending Ramadan and nafl—such hesitation is disliked. It also covers the scenario where one makes a conditional intention like 'if it is Ramadan then I am fasting, otherwise I am not'—in that case one is not considered fasting. The second part of the passage addresses the ruling on fasting the last days of Sha'ban. The base text states it is disliked to fast a day or two before Ramadan. The commentary clarifies that this dislike applies only if one intends the fast as part of Ramadan or in anticipation of it. If one fasts for a different reason (like making up missed fasts or regular voluntary fasting), it is not disliked. There is an intra-madhhab difference: some scholars like the author of al-Tuhfa hold absolute dislike, while the majority (and the position in al-Hidaya) restrict dislike to cases where the intention is to anticipate Ramadan. The passage also records the Shafi'i view that after mid-Sha'ban no fasting is allowed except for Ramadan. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the ruling for one or two days versus more, and explains that the hadith 'Do not anticipate the month' (لا تقدموا الشهر) is interpreted as prohibiting receiving Ramadan with fasting, not prohibiting all fasting. The commentary concludes with a procedural note: the mufti (not the qadi) should instruct the public to delay fasting until the sighting of the moon, announcing this in markets and minarets.

Key Terms
يوم الشك (yawm al-shakk): The 30th day of Sha'ban when it is uncertain whether it is the first day of Ramadan due to lack of moon sighting.
كراهة (karaha): Religious dislike; an act that is valid but carries a negative moral or legal connotation. In this context, it is karaha tanzihiyya (not tahrimi).
ترديد (taraddad): Hesitation in intention; to intend a fast with a condition, such as 'if this is Ramadan then I am fasting, otherwise I am not'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position as explained in this passage, what is the ruling if a person fasts on the day of doubt (30th Sha'ban) with the intention: 'If this day is Ramadan, then I am fasting, otherwise I am not'?
A) The person is considered fasting and it suffices for Ramadan if it is Ramadan.
B) The person is not considered fasting at all.
C) The person is considered fasting only as nafl.
D) The person is considered fasting but it is disliked.

Key Takeaway
Hesitation in intention (taraddad) on the day of doubt invalidates the fast entirely; a firm intention, whether as Ramadan or nafl, makes the fast valid and suffices for Ramadan if it becomes Ramadan.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Fasting the Last Days of Sha'ban in Anticipation (Taqdim)
Explains the ruling on fasting the last days of Sha'ban and the dispute with Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on fasting one or two days before Ramadan, identify the condition that triggers dislike, and compare the Hanafi view with the Shafi'i view on this issue.

Core Idea
Fasting on the last days of Sha'ban is disliked only if one intends the fast as part of Ramadan, not if fasting for other reasons.

The last days of Sha'ban carry a special ruling: fasting in anticipation of Ramadan is discouraged to avoid adding to the prescribed month. This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi explains the Hanafi position, the evidence from hadith, and the difference with the Shafi'i school. Understanding the precise condition of dislike is crucial for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its apparent ruling
The act is fasting one or two days before Ramadan (the last days of Sha'ban). The base text states it is disliked (makruh). Identify the type of dislike: tanzihi, not tahrimi.
The apparent ruling is from the hadith 'لا تقدموا الشهر بيوم ولا يومين'.
2
Determine the condition for dislike
The commentary specifies that the dislike is conditional upon intention: if one fasts with the intention that this fast is part of Ramadan or in anticipation of Ramadan, then it is disliked. If one fasts for another reason (e.g., making up missed fasts, regular voluntary fasts), it is not disliked.
This is the key point: the ruling is not absolute but tied to intention.
3
Analyze the intra-madhhab difference
Some Hanafi scholars (like the author of al-Tuhfa) held absolute dislike for any fast in the last two days. The majority (including al-Hidaya) restrict dislike to cases of anticipation. Which view is mufta bihi?
The majority view is relied upon.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school holds that after mid-Sha'ban, no fasting is allowed except Ramadan. This is a stricter view. Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
Under Shafi'i, a person cannot fast voluntary fasts after the 15th of Sha'ban.
5
Apply to scenarios
Practice: a person with a habit of fasting Mondays and Thursdays falls on the last two days of Sha'ban. Is it disliked? What if a person who missed days from last Ramadan fasts them now?
Apply the condition of intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصوم أجزأ عنه أي عن رمضان (ما) صامه) بأي نية كانت إلا أن يكون مسافراً ونواه عن واجب آخر كما تقدم وإن ظهر من شعبان، ونواه نفلاً كان غير مضمون لدخول الإسقاط في عزيمته من وجه وكراهة الواجب لصورة النهي كصلاته في أرض الغير وهو دون كراهته على أنه من رمضان لعدم التشبه، وأما كراهة النفل مع الترديد فلأنه ناو للفرض من وجه وهو أن يقول : من رمضان فعنه وإلا فتطوع ( وإن ردد) الشخص (فيه) أي في يوم الشك (بين إن كان غداً. كلام فظهر المصنف أنه من صوم يوم من الشك فقد عصى هذا ابا في شرح السيد: ومنه أي من قوله إلا صوم نفل المقتضى عدم الكراهة يعلم أن ما استفيد من ماً يعتاده أم لا وسواء الشك نفلاً لا يكره مطلقاً سواء وافق صوم صامه بانفراده أم لا بأن ضم إليه غيره وسواء كان ما ضمه إليه يوماً واحداً أم لا بأن كان يومين فأكثر مسلم لا غبار عليه ولا ينافيه ما يأتي من قوله وكره صوم يوم أو يومين من آخر شعبان لأنه مقيد بما إذا كان التقدم على قصد أن يكون من رمضان ا هـ . قوله: (إلا أن يكون مسافراً) هو مذهب الإمام كما سبق. قوله : (لدخول الإسقاط في عزيمته) أي في نية صومه من وجه، وهو ما إذا ظهر أنه من رمضان فإنه يجزى عنه فكأنه لم يشرع ملتزماً، بل مسقطاً الوجه فلا قضاء عليه لو أفسده قوله : ( وكراهة الواجب الخ) الأولى ما فعله في الشرح حيث قال : أما كراهة صومه على أنه من رمضان فلقوله من صام يوم القاسم، وفيه تشبه بأهل الكتاب في زيادة مدة الصوم فإن ظهرت رمضانيته أجزأه، وإن أفطره من شعبان لم يقضه كالمظنون لشروعه مسقطاً، وأما كراهة الواجب الخ، والفرق بين ظهر الجمعة الذي يصلي بنية الشك في صحة الجمعة حيث ينوي فيه الفرض، وبين صوم الشك حيث لا ينوي فيه الفرض أن نية التعيين في الصلاة لازمة لكون وقتها ظرفاً يسعها، وغيرها بخلاف الصوم فظهر الجمعة لا يصح، ولو في وقتها إلا أن نواه على التعيين بخلاف وقت الصوم فإنه معيار لا يسع غيره ره سيد عن الحموي، وهذا إنما يرد على مذهب أبي يوسف لا على المعتمد بقي أن ما ذكره المصنف من حديث من صام يوما الشك فقد عصى أبا القاسم لا أصل له كما قاله الزيلعي قوله : (الصورة النهي) أي المنهي عنه يعني صورة الواجب كصورة الفرض للقرب بينهما فلذاكره، ولو ظهرت رمضانيته في هذه الصورة أجزأه لو مقيماً، ولو مسافراً فعن الواجب عند الإمام، ولو ظهر من شعبان فعما نوى في الصحيح قوله : (كصلاته في أرض الغير فإن الكراهة هنا للعارض المجاور، وهو الشرح . ملك الغير بلا رضاه كما كره الواجب للعارض وهو تصوره بصورة المنهي عنه. قوله: (لعدم التشبه أي بأهل الكتاب في الزيادة على مقدار الصوم بقي ما لو ردد بين واجب، ونفل ومكروه تنزيهاً ولو تردد بين فرض وواجب كره فإن ظهر أنه من شعبان لم يجز عن الواجب لأن الجهة لم تثبت للتردد فيها، وأصل النية لا يكفيه، ويكون فرضاً غير مضمون بالقضاء إذا كان غير رمضان لشروعه فيه مسقطاً. قوله : (لا يكون صائماً كما أنه ليس بصائم لو نوى إنه إن لم يجد غداء فصائم، وإلا فمفطر تنوير قوله : (والمراد به التقديم الخ) فيه تأمل إذ ليس ذلك بلازم لأن العلة المعقولة توهم الزيادة، ولو من بعض الناس، وهذه تتحقق بتقديم الصوم، ولو على أنه من شعبان، ومعنى الحديث لا تصوموا قبل رمضان الخ ومما يدل على ما ذكرنا قوله : لا تقدموا الشهر أي شهر الصيام المفروض بغيره، وكذا ذكر في التحفة، ونصها الصوم قبل رمضان يومين مكروه أي صوم كان، وما ذكره المحبي أخذه في الفوائد وأفاده في العناية، ومثله في الإيضاح، ونصه لا بأس بصوم يوم، أو يومين، أو ثلاثة قبل رمضان لما روي أنه كان يصل شعبان برمضان، والمراد بقوله : لا لا تقدموا الحديث استقبال الشهر بصوم في الدراية قال الكمال وما في التحفة أوجه فالحاصل أنه إذا صام يومين، أو يوماً هل يكره منه ؟ أو ومثله من بعضهم كصاحب التحفة قال بالكراهة مطلقاً، وبعضهم وهو الأكثر قيد بما إذا نوى أن ذلك رمضان، وما عليه الأكثر هو الذي ذكره في الهداية قوله : (لأن التقديم بالشيء على الشيء أن ينوي الخ) فيه نظر ظاهر فإن تقدم الشيء على الشيء لا يلزم فيه ما ذكره، وأجيب بأن الشيء أعيد معرفة فيكون عيناً والتقديم هنا إنما هو لوصف الفرض قوله : (لا يكره صوم ما فوقهما) وقال الإمام الشافعي: إذا انتصف شعبان، فلا صيام إلا رمضان لحديث ورد فيه، وأوردن التقديم بنية صوم الفرض لا يخص اليومين بل الحكم الكراهة فيما زاد حيث نوى الفرض، وأجيب بأنهم خصوا الكراهة باليوم واليومين لدفع توهم أن القليل عفو كما عفي في كثير من الأحكام أي فيفهم حكم الكثير بالأولى، وبأنه لما كان يقع النقص في الشهور، فيتوهم متوهم وقوع النقص في رجب، وفي شعبان معاً فيصوم يومين قبل الرؤية بناء منه على هذا التوهم من غير تحقيق تأمل، وراجع الشرح قوله : أن يأمر المفتي) إنما كان الأمر المفتي لا القاضي لأنّ الصوم لا يدخل تحت القضاء إلا تبعاً أي يأمر القاضي على أنه إفتاء لا حكم قوله : (بإظهار النداء الباء فيه كالباء في كتبت بالقلم، ويظهر النداء في الأسواق والمنارات كما في الشرح.
Book of Fasting. It suffices for Ramadan that (which one fasts) with any intention, unless he is a traveler and intends another obligatory fast as previously mentioned, and if it appears from Sha'ban and he intended it as nafl, it is not guaranteed because of the inclusion of expiation in his determination in one respect, and the dislike of the obligatory due to the form of prohibition like his prayer in another's land, and it is less than the dislike of it as being from Ramadan due to lack of resemblance. As for the dislike of nafl with hesitation, it is because he intends the obligatory in one respect, and that is to say: if from Ramadan then it is for it, otherwise voluntary. (And if) a person (hesitates in it) i.e. in the day of doubt (between whether it is tomorrow). Speech then the author appeared that he from fasting the day of doubt has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim. In the commentary of al-Sayyid: From it i.e. from his saying 'except a nafl fast' which necessitates no dislike, it is known that what is derived from what he is accustomed to or not, and whether the doubt is nafl is not disliked absolutely, whether it coincides with a fast he fasts alone or not by joining another, and whether what he joined is one day or more like two days, it is sound with no objection, and does not contradict what will come of his saying 'and disliked fasting a day or two from the end of Sha'ban' because it is restricted to when the anticipation is intended to be from Ramadan. End. His saying: (unless he is a traveler) is the madhhab of the Imam as before. His saying: (because of the inclusion of expiation in his determination) i.e. in his intention of fasting in one respect, and that is if it appears that it is from Ramadan, then it suffices for him, as if he did not begin as committed but rather as expiating, so there is no makeup upon him if he invalidates it. His saying: (and the dislike of the obligatory etc.) the first is what he did in the sharh where he said: As for the dislike of his fasting as being from Ramadan, it is due to his saying 'whoever fasts the day of al-Qasim', and in it is resemblance to the People of the Book in increasing the duration of fasting. If its Ramadan-ness appears, it suffices him, and if he breaks it from Sha'ban, he does not make it up like the presumptive because he began as expiating. As for the dislike of the obligatory etc., and the difference between the noon of Friday which he prays with intention of doubt in the validity of Friday where he intends the obligatory, and between the fast of doubt where he does not intend the obligatory, is that the intention of specification in prayer is necessary because its time is a container that accommodates it and others, unlike fasting, so the noon of Friday is not valid even in its time unless he intends it specifically, unlike the time of fasting because it is a measure that does not accommodate others. (rah) al-Sayyid from al-Hamawi. This only counters the madhhab of Abu Yusuf, not the relied upon. Remain that what the author mentioned of the hadith 'whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim' has no basis as al-Zayla'i said. His saying: (the form of prohibition) i.e. the forbidden thing, meaning the form of the obligatory like the form of the obligatory for the closeness between them, so for that reason he disliked it. And if Ramadan-ness appears in this form, it suffices him if a resident, and if a traveler, then from the obligatory according to the Imam, and if it appears from Sha'ban, then from what he intended in the correct view. His saying: (like his prayer in another's land) the dislike here is for the adjacent accident, and it is the sharh. Ownership of another without his consent, just as the obligatory is disliked for the accident which is its taking the form of the forbidden. His saying: (due to lack of resemblance) i.e. to the People of the Book in increasing beyond the measure of fasting. Remain what if he hesitated between obligatory and nafl and makruh tanzihan, and if he hesitated between fard and wajib, it is disliked. Then if it appears that it is from Sha'ban, it does not suffice for the obligatory because the aspect is not established due to hesitation in it, and the basic intention is not sufficient, and it becomes a fard not guaranteed by makeup if it is other than Ramadan because he began it as expiating. His saying: (he is not fasting) just as he is not fasting if he intends 'if I find supper then I am fasting, otherwise I am breaking' (Tanwir). His saying: (and what is meant by anticipation etc.) in it is reflection since that is not necessary because the rational cause suggests increase, even from some people, and this is realized by anticipating the fast even if as from Sha'ban, and the meaning of the hadith 'do not fast before Ramadan' etc. And among what indicates what we mentioned is his saying: 'do not anticipate the month' i.e. the month of obligatory fasting by other than it, and likewise mentioned in al-Tuhfa, and its text: fasting before Ramadan by two days is disliked, whatever fast it is. And what al-Muhibbi mentioned he took from al-Fawa'id and benefited from al-Inaya, and similarly in al-Idah, and its text: there is no harm in fasting a day or two or three before Ramadan because it is narrated that he used to connect Sha'ban with Ramadan. And what is meant by his saying: 'do not anticipate' the hadith is receiving the month by fasting. In al-Diraya, al-Kamal said: and what is in al-Tuhfa is preferred. So the conclusion is that if he fasts two days or one day, is it disliked from him? And similarly some like the author of al-Tuhfa said it is disliked absolutely, and others, which is the majority, restricted it to if he intended that to be Ramadan, and what the majority is upon is what he mentioned in al-Hidaya. His saying: (because anticipation of something is that one intends etc.) in it is apparent consideration, for the precedence of something over something does not necessarily require what he mentioned, and it was answered that the thing is repeated as a definite noun so it becomes a specific entity, and anticipation here is only for the attribute of the obligatory. His saying: (there is no dislike for fasting above two days) and Imam al-Shafi'i said: when half of Sha'ban passes, there is no fasting except Ramadan due to a hadith reported. And we mentioned that anticipation with the intention of obligatory fast is not specific to two days, rather the ruling of dislike applies to more where one intends the obligatory, and it was answered that they specified the dislike to one or two days to repel the assumption that the small amount is excused as excused in many rulings, i.e. so the ruling for more is understood a fortiori. And because when deficiency occurs in the months, someone might imagine deficiency in Rajab and Sha'ban together, so he fasts two days before sighting based on this assumption without investigation. Reflect. And refer to the sharh. His saying: (that the mufti should order) the command is only for the mufti, not the qadi, because fasting is not subject to qada except indirectly, i.e. the qadi orders as ifta' not as a ruling. His saying: (with announcement) the ba' in it is like the ba' in 'I wrote with a pen', and the announcement is made in markets and minarets as in the sharh.
Source pages p. 648

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi addresses two closely related rulings concerning fasting in Sha'ban. The first ruling deals with fasting on the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk)—the 30th of Sha'ban when it is uncertain whether it is actually Ramadan. The second ruling concerns fasting during the last days of Sha'ban in anticipation of Ramadan. The commentary opens by affirming that if a person fasts on the day of doubt and it later turns out to be Ramadan, that fast suffices for Ramadan regardless of the original intention, except in the case of a traveler who intended a different obligatory fast. If the person intended a nafl (supererogatory) fast, it is not considered a guaranteed (ghayr madmun) fast because it has the quality of being a substitute (isqat) should it become Ramadan. The dislike (karaha) of fasting with an obligatory intention on the day of doubt is explained through analogy with praying in another's land without permission—the act is valid but disliked due to an external circumstance (resemblance to the People of the Book's practice of lengthening the fast). The hadith 'Whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim' is cited but noted by al-Zayla'i to have no authentic basis. The commentary then discusses the ruling if one hesitates (taraddad) between intending Ramadan and nafl—such hesitation is disliked. It also covers the scenario where one makes a conditional intention like 'if it is Ramadan then I am fasting, otherwise I am not'—in that case one is not considered fasting. The second part of the passage addresses the ruling on fasting the last days of Sha'ban. The base text states it is disliked to fast a day or two before Ramadan. The commentary clarifies that this dislike applies only if one intends the fast as part of Ramadan or in anticipation of it. If one fasts for a different reason (like making up missed fasts or regular voluntary fasting), it is not disliked. There is an intra-madhhab difference: some scholars like the author of al-Tuhfa hold absolute dislike, while the majority (and the position in al-Hidaya) restrict dislike to cases where the intention is to anticipate Ramadan. The passage also records the Shafi'i view that after mid-Sha'ban no fasting is allowed except for Ramadan. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the ruling for one or two days versus more, and explains that the hadith 'Do not anticipate the month' (لا تقدموا الشهر) is interpreted as prohibiting receiving Ramadan with fasting, not prohibiting all fasting. The commentary concludes with a procedural note: the mufti (not the qadi) should instruct the public to delay fasting until the sighting of the moon, announcing this in markets and minarets.

Key Terms
تقديم (taqdim): Anticipation; to fast the last days of Sha'ban with the intention of being ready for Ramadan or as if it is Ramadan.
كراهة تنزيهية (karaha tanzihiyya): Preventive dislike; an act that is better to avoid but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, what is the ruling if a person fasts on the 29th of Sha'ban with the intention of making up a missed fast from last Ramadan?
A) The fast is valid and not disliked.
B) The fast is invalid because it is after mid-Sha'ban.
C) The fast is valid but disliked because it is the day before Ramadan.
D) The fast is invalid because makeup fasts cannot be performed in Sha'ban.

Key Takeaway
Fasting on the last days of Sha'ban is not inherently disliked; the dislike attaches only to the intention of anticipating Ramadan. Different intentions yield different rulings.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Fasting Before Ramadan: Hanafi Ruling and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on karahah of fasting one or two days before Ramadan with proof and Shafi'i objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fasting one or two days before Ramadan, explain the proof, and compare it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Fasting before Ramadan is disliked only when intending Ramadan; the Shafi'i absolute restriction is rejected.

This lesson delves into the ruling on fasting in the last days of Sha'ban. The Hanafi school distinguishes between fasting with the intention of Ramadan, which is disliked, and voluntary fasting, which is permitted. This position is contested by Imam al-Shafi'i, who prohibits all fasting after mid-Sha'ban. We will examine the evidence and the practical consequences of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling in dispute
Determine the specific act (fasting one or two days before Ramadan) and the ruling (makruh tanzihi) according to the Hanafi school. Note that the karahah is conditional on intending it as Ramadan.
The act is not inherently prohibited; it is a precautionary measure to avoid anticipation.
2
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
State the Hanafi ruling: fasting one or two days with intention of Ramadan is makruh; without that intention it is not disliked. The proof is the hadith 'Do not anticipate the month by a day or two' and the principle that Sha'ban is time for nafl.
The prohibition in the hadith is interpreted as karahah because it is not absolute; the exception for habitual fasters shows permissibility.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that after mid-Sha'ban, no fasting is allowed except Ramadan, based on a hadith. This is an absolute prohibition of fasting after the 15th of Sha'ban.
The Shafi'i hadith is considered weaker or interpreted differently by Hanafis.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the karahah is not limited to two days; it applies whenever one intends Ramadan. The restriction to two days in the hadith is to prevent the assumption that a little is excused, implying that more is also disliked but the primary reason for karahah is the intention.
The Hanafi response addresses the Shafi'i proof by questioning its authenticity and offering a different interpretation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Shafi'is refrain from all fasting after mid-Sha'ban except for qada or nadhr; Hanafis allow voluntary fasting throughout Sha'ban and only dislike fasting with the intention of Ramadan.
This affects daily practice for observant Muslims in the second half of Sha'ban.

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiyah discusses the ruling on fasting before Ramadan. The matn states that if someone says 'If it is Ramadan, I am fasting; otherwise, I am not fasting,' they are not considered fasting because their intention is conditional. If it turns out to be Ramadan, it counts as a make-up (qada). The main topic is the karahah (dislikeness) of fasting one or two days at the end of Sha'ban with the intention of being from Ramadan. The proof is the hadith 'Do not anticipate the month by a day or two.' The commentator explains that karahah applies only when intending Ramadan; if one fasts those days as voluntary (nafl) for Sha'ban, it is not disliked. A difference of opinion is noted: some scholars (like the author of al-Tuhfah) say it is disliked absolutely, while the majority (including al-Hidayah) restrict it to intending Ramadan. The latter is the relied-upon view. Then the passage addresses Imam al-Shafi'i's position that after mid-Sha'ban, no fasting is allowed except Ramadan. The Hanafi response is that the ruling of karahah is not limited to two days; it applies to any number if intending Ramadan. However, the scholars specified one or two days to prevent the idea that a small amount is excused, implying that more is likewise disliked. The passage also briefly mentions that the mufti should order the public to wait (talammus) on the day of doubt, which is a prelude to the next section.

Key Terms
التقديم (al-taqdim): Anticipation: intending to do an act before its prescribed time.
الكرهة (al-karahah): Dislikeness (makruh): an act that is not prohibited but discouraged.
التلوم (al-talammus): Waiting: suspending the intention to fast until the status of the day becomes clear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, when is fasting one or two days before Ramadan disliked?
A) Always, regardless of intention
B) Only if the person intends it as part of Ramadan
C) Only if three or more days are fasted
D) Only for the mufti and judge

Key Takeaway
Fasting one or two days before Ramadan is disliked only when intended as Ramadan; otherwise it is permissible, and the Shafi'i absolute prohibition is not accepted in the Hanafi school.

Ruling on the Day of Doubt: The Mufti, Judge, and Elite
Ruling on what the mufti commands and how the elite fast on the day of doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fasting the day of doubt for the mufti, judge, and elite, and apply the distinction between prohibition and recommendation based on the hadith of sirar.

Core Idea
The day of doubt is prohibited for the public but recommended secretly for the mufti, judge, and elite.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk), a day when there is uncertainty whether it is Ramadan or still Sha'ban. While the general public is ordered not to fast, the mufti, judge, and those who can control their intention are encouraged to fast secretly. We will examine the evidence from the hadith of sirar and the practice of Abu Yusuf, and understand the reasoning behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Distinguish the general public, the mufti/judge, and the elite (khawass). Each has a different ruling.
2
Understand the mufti's order
The mufti commands the public to wait (talammus) and then break the fast if the moon is not sighted by forenoon. This prevents anticipation.
The judge issues the order as a fatwa, not a judicial ruling.
3
Explain the secret fast for the elite
The mufti, judge, and elite fast secretly as a voluntary act. They must not intend it as Ramadan and must be able to control their intention.
The elite fast secretly to avoid accusations of disobedience from the public.
4
Analyze the hadith of sirar
The hadith commands fasting a day in place of a missed fast. Hanafis interpret this as recommendation (nadb) because it conflicts with the prohibition of anticipating Ramadan.
The story of Abu Yusuf illustrates the practice: he publicly ordered breaking but privately fasted.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Imam Ahmad holds the hadith as evidence for obligation. Hanafis reconcile the texts and prefer recommendation.

His saying: That the mufti should order - The order is for the mufti, not the judge, because fasting does not fall under judiciary except incidentally, i.e., the judge orders it as a fatwa, not a ruling. His saying: To announce the call - the preposition is like in 'I wrote with a pen,' and the announcement is made in markets and minarets, as in the commentary. The hadith of al-sirar... the book of fasting... the secret of doubt... then he disobeyed, starting (the day of doubt) to preserve the possibility of performing the obligatory fast by initiating the intention with the appearance of the situation in its time. Then he orders the public to break the fast if the time for initiating the intention has passed, which is when the forenoon (duha) comes, and the situation is not clear, to cut off the source of belief in increase. And he (the mufti) fasts it, i.e., as a voluntary fast, and the judge - with disobedience for committing the fast based on what is narrated: 'Whoever fasts the day of Abu al-Qasim has disobeyed,' conflicting with what he was ordered to do of breaking the fast. And he also fasts it secretly, whoever is among the elite, i.e., one who can control himself from internal agitation (tardid in intention) and from noticing that he is fasting for the obligatory (if it is Ramadan) due to the hadith of al-sirar, which is his saying, peace be upon him, to a man: 'Did you fast from the sirar (last part) of Sha'ban?' He said: 'No.' He said: 'Then if you break the fast, fast a day in its place.' And 'sirar' of the month, with fath and kasr, its end, because the moon is hidden therein. Since it is in conflict with the prohibition of anticipation by fasting a day or two, the anticipation is interpreted as intending the obligatory fast, and the hadith of al-sirar indicates its recommendation as a voluntary fast, because the understood meaning is to conclude... named... h. His saying: 'By waiting' - the preposition is for modification. His saying: 'By initiating the intention' is connected to 'performance'. His saying: 'By the appearance of the situation' - the preposition means 'with', i.e., with the appearance that it is Ramadan. His saying: 'In its time' - i.e., the intention is connected to appearance. His saying: 'Then he orders the public' is in the accusative, coordinated with the first 'orders'. His saying: 'The hadith of al-sirar' will be mentioned soon. His saying: 'He is accused of disobedience' is the reason for his saying 'secretly'. He said in the commentary: For if he gives them the fatwa to break after waiting, and then they oppose him by fasting, they are accused of disobedience, holding on to what is narrated: 'Whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim,' which is famous among the common people! His saying: 'By committing' - the preposition is for causation, connected to 'disobedience', and his saying: 'with what is narrated' - the preposition means 'lam' (for), and his expression in al-Saghir and al-Kabir: 'it is narrated' and his saying in al-Kabir: 'it is famous among the common people' indicates that it has no basis, and it is so, as passed from al-Zayla'i. And the evidence that the judge fasts it is what Asad ibn 'Umar narrated: I came to the door of al-Rashid, and Abu Yusuf the judge approached, wearing a black turban, a black cloak, and black socks, riding a black horse, with nothing white about him but his white beard, and it was the day of doubt. He gave the people a fatwa to break the fast. I said to him: 'Are you breaking the fast?' He said: 'Come close to me.' So I approached, and he said in my ear: 'I am fasting.' Is the blackness the emblem of the Abbasids? His saying: 'Conflicting' is a circumstantial qualifier from the subject of the omitted infinitive which is 'committing', i.e., his committing the fast while conflicting with what he was ordered to do of breaking. And the order is in the active voice, and the object is omitted, i.e., the public. His saying: 'Whoever is' - i.e., among the elite in this context. His saying: 'And from noticing' is a coordination of the specific. His saying: 'Fast a day in its place' - the command is for recommendation. His saying: 'Sirar of the month' with fath and kasr - al-Qamus said: al-sirar (like kitab) is the last night of the month, like sirarihi and sirrihi. And he said: before that, al-sirr is the beginning of the month or its end. Imam Ahmad used this hadith as evidence for the obligation of fasting the day of doubt, as in the commentary. His saying: 'It is named by it' i.e., by al-sirar, which indicates hiddenness. His saying: 'Because when it was' - is the cause for recommending its fast for the mufti, judge, and whoever is among the elite. His saying: 'He interpreted the anticipation' - i.e., the prohibited one. His saying: 'On'.
Source pages p. 649

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiyah discusses the ruling on the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk), which is the 30th of Sha'ban when the new moon of Ramadan is not sighted. The mufti (not the judge, since fasting is not a judicial matter except incidentally) is to command the public to wait (talammus) without intending to fast. If the status does not become clear by the time of the forenoon (duha), he orders them to break the fast (i.e., not to fast that day) to prevent any assumption that the month has been extended. However, the mufti and the judge themselves are encouraged to fast secretly (as a voluntary fast) on that day, based on the hadith of 'sirar' (the last part of the month). The hadith reports that the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked a man if he had fasted from the sirar of Sha'ban, and when he said no, the Prophet told him to fast a day in its place after breaking. This indicates the recommendation of fasting the last part of Sha'ban. Since there is a conflict with the prohibition of anticipating Ramadan (by fasting a day or two with the intention of Ramadan), the anticipation is interpreted as intending the obligatory fast, so fasting on the day of doubt without that intention is not included in the prohibition. The elite (khawass) are those who can control their intention and not think they are fasting the obligatory fast if it turns out to be Ramadan. The passage also mentions that the common people might accuse those who fast on the day of doubt of disobedience, based on a famous but baseless narration: 'Whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim.' The commentator notes that this narration has no basis (la asla lahu). The story of Abu Yusuf is given as evidence that the judge fasts secretly: he gave a fatwa to the public to break, but he himself was fasting secretly, as confided to Asad ibn 'Umar.

Key Terms
يوم الشك (yawm al-shakk): The day of doubt: the 30th of Sha'ban when the new moon of Ramadan is not sighted, and it is unclear whether it is Ramadan or still Sha'ban.
التلوم (al-talammus): Waiting: the mufti commands the public to wait without intending to fast until the status becomes clear or until the time for initiating intention expires.
السرر (al-sirar / al-sarar): The last part (specifically the last night) of the lunar month, when the moon is hidden.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is encouraged to fast on the day of doubt?
A) The general public
B) Only the mufti and judge
C) The mufti, judge, and the elite (khawass)
D) No one, it is haram

Key Takeaway
The day of doubt is not a day of universal prohibition; the mufti, judge, and elite are encouraged to fast secretly, while the public must refrain.

Fasting the Day of Doubt: Rules for Public and Elite
Explains ruling on yawm al-shakk for general public, mufti, qadi, and elite

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on fasting the day of doubt for the general public (must break fast) and the elite (may fast as supererogatory), and explain the proof from the hadith of sirar.

Core Idea
The day of doubt: the public must break fast, but the elite may fast secretly as supererogatory.

Fasting on the day of doubt (the 30th of Sha'ban without sighting the crescent) is a nuanced issue in the Hanafi school. The ruling depends on the category of the person: the general public is prohibited from fasting, while the mufti, qadi, and other elite individuals may fast secretly as a supererogatory act. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the proof from the hadith of sirar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
The passage divides people into three categories: the general public, the mufti/qadi, and the elite (khawass). Note the conditions for each.
2
State the ruling for each
For the general public: break fast after mid-morning if unclear. For mufti/qadi and elite: fast secretly as supererogatory.
The mufti/qadi are included in the elite category.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of sirar: the Prophet commanded a man to fast a day in place of the sirar of Sha'ban.
The hadith text is quoted in the passage.
4
Explain the interpretation
The imperative 'صم' is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) because it conflicts with the prohibition of fasting a day or two before Ramadan. The Hanafi principle that al-amr yufidu al-wujub is overridden.
The hadith is ahad and zanni al-thubut.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
The Shafi'i school generally prohibits fasting the day of doubt for everyone, based on a different interpretation of the same evidence.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابتداء يوم الشك محافظة على إمكان أداء الفرض بإنشاء النية بظهور الحال في وقتها ثم يأمر العامة بالإفطار إذا ذهب وقت إنشاء النية وهو عند مجيء الضحوة الكبرى ولم يتبين الحال حسماً لمادة اعتقاد الزيادة ويصومه نفلاً المفتي والقاضي سراً بالعصيان بارتكاب الصوم مما يروى من صام يوم أبا القاسم مخالفاً لما أمر به من الفطر ويصومه أيضاً سراً من كان من الخواص وهو من يتمكن من ضبط نفسه عن الاضجاع وهو الترديد في النية وعن ملاحظة كونه صائماً عن الفرض إن كان من رمضان لحديث السرر، وهو قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لرجل: هل صمت من سرار شعبان؟ قال: لا، قال: فإذا أفطرت فصم يوماً مكانه. وسرار الشهر بالفتح والكسر آخره لاستتار القمر فيه لأنه لما كان معارضاً بنهي التقدم بصيام يوم أو يومين حمل التقدم على نية الفرض، وحديث السرر على استحبابه نفلاً لأن المعنى الذي يعقل فيه ختم شعبان بالعبادة كما يستحب ذلك في كل شهر.
Beginning the day of doubt, preserving the possibility of performing the obligation by initiating the intention with the appearance of the situation in its time. Then he orders the general public to break the fast when the time for initiating the intention has passed, which is at the arrival of the great forenoon, and the situation has not become clear, decisively cutting off the material of belief in increase. And the mufti and the judge fast it as a supererogatory (fast) secretly, with disobedience due to committing the fast based on what is narrated: 'Whoever fasts the day of Abu al-Qasim has disobeyed,' contradicting what he was commanded to do of breaking the fast. And also fasts it secretly whoever is among the elite, who is able to control himself from turning over, which is hesitation in the intention, and from observing that he is fasting as an obligation if it is from Ramadan, due to the hadith of sirar, which is his saying, peace be upon him, to a man: 'Did you fast from the sirar of Sha'ban?' He said: 'No.' He said: 'Then if you break the fast, fast a day in its place.' And sirar of the month, with fath and kasr of its last letter, due to the concealment of the moon in it, because when it was opposed by the prohibition of preceding by fasting a day or two days, the preceding was interpreted as intending the obligation, and the hadith of sirar as recommending it as a supererogatory, because the meaning understood by it is the conclusion of Sha'ban with worship, as that is recommended in every month.
Source pages p. 650

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk), the 30th day of Sha'ban when the crescent of Ramadan is not sighted. The ruling is that one begins the day by intending to fast with the condition that if it turns out to be Ramadan, it counts; but after the time for intention passes (mid-morning), if it remains unclear, the general public must break the fast to avoid any possibility of adding to Ramadan. The mufti and qadi, however, fast secretly as a supererogatory act (nafl), despite the fact that ordinary people who fast are considered disobedient based on the report: 'Whoever fasts the day of Abu al-Qasim has disobeyed.' The elite (khawass) also fast secretly, provided they can control themselves from hesitation in intention and from regarding their fast as obligatory. The proof is the hadith of sirar, where the Prophet commanded a man to fast a day in place of the sirar (end of month) if he breaks it; this indicates recommendation, not obligation, because the prohibition of fasting a day or two before Ramadan is interpreted as intending the obligatory fast of Ramadan. Thus, the hadith supports supererogatory fasting on the day of doubt for those who can do so properly.

Key Terms
يوم الشك (yawm al-shakk): The day of doubt, i.e., the 30th day of Sha'ban when the crescent of Ramadan is not sighted.
السرر (al-sirar): The end of the lunar month when the moon is hidden; specifically the last day of Sha'ban.
الخواص (al-khawass): The elite, those capable of controlling their intention and not confusing the fast with Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Everyone

Key Takeaway
The day of doubt is not a blanket prohibition; the Hanafi school allows elite individuals to fast it as supererogatory, based on the hadith of sirar, while the general public must break fast to avoid confusion with Ramadan.
