Forgetfulness Does Not Break the Fast
States that forgetful eating/drinking/intercourse do not invalidate the fast, with proof and refinement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the forgetful (nasi) and the mistaken (mukhti') person in fasting and state the ruling for each, citing the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness in fasting does not invalidate the fast; but being mistaken does.

When a fasting person deliberately breaks the fast, the fast is invalidated and expiation may be required. But what if he forgets he is fasting? The Hanafi school, relying on a clear hadith, rules that forgetfulness does not break the fast. However, there is a subtle distinction: the forgetful is contrasted with the mistaken (mukhti'), who remembers the fast but inadvertently causes something to enter his body. In that case, the fast is broken. This lesson will unpack that distinction and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Locate the ruling on forgetfulness
In the passage, find the explicit statement that eating, drinking, or intercourse forgetfully do not break the fast. Note the phrase 'لا يفسد' (does not break).
The ruling applies to all three acts individually or combined.
2
Define 'nasiyan' (forgetful)
The text defines forgetfulness as 'عدم استحضار الشيء عند الحاجة' – the absence of recalling the fast when needed. Understand that the person is genuinely unaware of being in a state of fasting.
This is not mere distraction; it's a complete lapse of memory.
3
Contrast with 'mukhti' (mistaken)
The passage explains that the mistaken is one who remembers the fast but does not intend to break it, yet something enters his body inadvertently (e.g., water during rinsing or food during tasting). The ruling for the mistaken: the fast is broken.
The key difference is the presence or absence of awareness at the time of action.
4
Analyze the hadith proof
The Prophet ﷺ said: 'إذا أكل الصائم ناسياً فإنما هو رزق' – 'If the fasting person eats forgetfully, it is merely provision.' This hadith is the primary evidence. The phrase 'فإنما هو رزق' indicates that the food is Allah's provision, implying no sin or invalidation.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) in transmission but is accepted as sound by the school.
5
Apply the distinction to new cases
Given a scenario (e.g., rinsing mouth and accidentally swallowing water), determine whether the person is nasi or mukhti. If he remembered the fast, he is mukhti and the fast is broken; if he forgot, it is valid.
The sleeping person is treated like the mistaken, per the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في بيان ما لا يفسد الصوم وهو أربعة وعشرون شيئاً تقريباً لا تحديداً بالمرة منها ما لو أكل) الصائم (أو شرب أو جامع) أو جمع بينهما (ناسياً) لصومه لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : إذا أكل الصائم ناسياً فإنما هو رزق . الفساد والبطلان في العبادة سيان . قوله : (بالمرة) يحتمل تعلقه بقوله : لا يفسد أي لا يفسد بفعل شيء منها ومفهومه أنه يفسد إذا اجتمعت أو بعضها وليس كذلك، ويحتمل تعلقه بقوله : لا تحديداً أي ليس هذا العدد مقطوعاً به بحيث لا يزيد والأولى حذف هذه العبارة إذ لا كبير فائدة لها على أن إدخال أل على مرة مولد قوله: (ناسياً) النسيان عدم استحضار الشيء عند الحاجة كذا في الشرح وقيد بالناسي للاحتراز عن المخطىء، وهو الذاكر للصوم غير القاصد للفطر بأن لم يقصد الأكل، ولا الشرب، بل قصد المضمضة، أو اختبار طعم المأكول فسبق شيء منه إلى جوفه، أو باشر مباشرة فاحشة فتورات حشفته، فإنه يفسد، والمكروه والنائم كالمخطىء كذا في شرح السيد. قوله: (الصومه) لا ناسياً فعله لأنه
Chapter on explaining what does not break the fast. It includes approximately twenty-four things, not definitively limited. Among them: if the fasting person eats, drinks, or has intercourse, or combines them, forgetfully due to his fast, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'If the fasting person eats forgetfully, it is merely provision.' Corruption and invalidity in worship are the same. His saying: (at all) possibly relates to his saying: does not break, i.e., it does not break by doing any one of them, and its implication is that it breaks if they are combined or some, but it is not so; and possibly relates to his saying: not definitive, i.e., this number is not absolute such that it cannot increase, and it is better to omit this expression because there is no great benefit; moreover, inserting 'al' on 'marrat' is a neologism. His saying: (forgetfully) forgetfulness is the absence of recalling something when needed, as in al-Sharh. He restricted it to the forgetful to differentiate from the mistaken, who is the one mindful of the fast but not intending to break it, such that he did not intend to eat or drink but intended rinsing or testing the taste of food, and something entered his throat, or he engaged in lewd contact resulting in exposure of his glans, then it breaks. The disapproved and the sleeping are like the mistaken, as in Sharh al-Sayyid. His saying: (his fast) not forgetfully doing it, because
Source pages p. 657

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi opens the chapter on things that do not break the fast. It is a critical refinement of the main text (Maraqi al-Falah). The ruling is clear: if a fasting person eats, drinks, or has intercourse forgetfully (i.e., unaware of the fast), the fast is not broken. The proof is the Prophet's hadith: 'If the fasting person eats forgetfully, it is merely provision provided by Allah.' The commentary clarifies two important distinctions: (1) The word 'nasiyan' is defined as the absence of recalling the fast at the time of need. (2) Nasiyan (forgetful) is contrasted with mukhti' (mistaken). The mistaken is one who remembers the fast but does not intend to break it, yet inadvertently causes something to enter his body (e.g., water during rinsing). According to the Hanafi school, the mistaken's fast is broken, whereas the forgetful's is not. The sleeping person is treated like the mistaken. The commentary also discusses the phrase 'twenty-four things approximately' indicating that the list is not exhaustive.

Key Terms
ناسياً (nasiyan): Forgetful: lacking recall of the fast at the time of action.
مخطىء (mukhti'): Mistaken: one who remembers the fast but does not intend to break it, yet something enters his body inadvertently.
تحديداً (tahdidan): Definitively limited; the list of 24 items is approximate, not exhaustive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a fasting person accidentally swallows water while rinsing his mouth, is his fast valid?
A) Yes, because it was forgetful.
B) No, because he remembered the fast but did not intend to break it, making him mukhti'.
C) Yes, because it was unintentional.
D) No, because any water entering the throat invalidates the fast.

Key Takeaway
Forgetfulness (nasi) does not break the fast; but the mistaken (mukhti') who remembers the fast does break it – a distinction rooted in hadith and refined by Hanafi scholars.
